بِحَصْلَةٍ مِنْ حِصَالِ الْخَيْرِ كَانَ كَمَنْ الَّى فَرِيضَهُ وَمَنْ أَدّى فَرِيضَةً فِيْهِ كَانَ كَمَنْ أَذًى سَبْعِينَ فَرِيضَةً فِيمَا سِوَاهُ یعنی جس نے رمضان میں کوئی نیک نفل کام کیا تو وہ رمضان کے علاوہ میں ستر فرض ادا کرنے والے کے برابر ہے بہر حال رمضان کا دن جب معظم اور محترم ہے تو رمضان کے در کا حق ادا کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ اب اگر کوئی شخص روزہ کا اہل ہو تو روزہ رکھ کر اس کا حق ادا کرے اور اگر روز کا اہل نہ ہو تو مفطرات سے رک کر ہی اس کا حق ادا کرے۔ اور یہ امساک عن المقرات چونکہ روزہ کا خلیفہ نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کا وجوب اصل یعنی روزہ کے وجوب پر مبنی ہوگا۔ اور جب اس کا وجوب روزے کے وجوب پر مبنی نہیں تو امساک عن المفطرات اس پر بھی واجب کیا جا سکتا ہے جس پر روزہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف حائضہ اور نفاس والی عورت اور بیمار اور مسافر کہ ان پر ان اعزار کے موجود ہونے کی حالت میں امساک واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ مذکورہ اعذار (حیض ، نفاس ، سفر، مرض ) جس طرح روزہ رکھنے سے مانع ہیں۔ اسی طرح روزہ داروں کے ساتھ مشابہت اختیار کرنے سے بھی مانع ہیں۔ چنانچہ خاکہ اور نفاس کے حق میں تشابہ بالصائمین اس لئے ممنوع ہے کہ ان دونوں پر روز و حرام ہے۔ اور حرام فعل کے ساتھ نشا بہ بھی حرام ہوتا ہے اس لئے ان دونوں کے حق میں تشابہ بالصائمین حرام ہے اور مریض اور مسافر کے حق میں تشابہ بالصائمین اس لئے ممنوع ہے کہ ان دونوں کو افطار کی اجازت دفع حرج کے لئے دی گئی ہے پس اگر ان پر روزہ داروں کی مشابہت اختیار کرنا لازم قرار دیا جائے تو نقض موضوع لا زم آئے گا۔ یعنی روزہ نہ رکھنے کی اجازت مریض اور مسافر کو حرج دور کرنے کے لئے دی گئی تھی مگر تشابه بالصائمین کو لازم قرار دیکر پھر حرج میں مبتلا کر دیا گیا یہی نقض موضوع ہے۔
The ruling on a traveler returning and a menstruating woman becoming pure during part of the day: that they should abstain for the remainder of the day. Imam Shafi'i said abstention is not obligatory. This difference applies to anyone who becomes eligible for fasting during the day not at its start. He (Shafi'i) says imitation (of fasting) is a substitute, so it is only obligatory on one for whom the original (fasting) is actualized, like one who breaks fast intentionally or mistakenly. Our proof is that it is obligatory as honoring the right of the time, not as a substitute, because it is a venerated time. Unlike the menstruating, post-natal, sick, and traveler, where abstention is not obligatory due to the existence of a barrier preventing imitation just as it prevents fasting. Commentary: If a traveler returns or a menstruating woman becomes pure during a Ramadan day, according to us they must abstain from nullifiers for the rest of the day, even though they were not fasting. Imam Shafi'i says abstention is not obligatory. This difference applies to anyone who becomes eligible for complete fasting during the day, e.g., an apostate who becomes Muslim, a child who reaches puberty, or an insane person who regains sanity. Shafi'i's evidence: imitation of fasting is a substitute, and a substitute is only obligatory on the one for whom the original is obligatory; since original fasting is not obligatory on the traveler and menstruating woman, its substitute cannot be obligatory. Our evidence: imitation is not a substitute because it occurs in only part of the day, while fasting is the whole day, so abstaining part of the day is not a substitute. Rather, it is obligatory as a right of the venerated time of Ramadan. The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Whoever performs a good deed in it (Ramadan) is like one who performed an obligatory duty; whoever performs an obligatory duty in it is like one who performed seventy obligatory duties in other times.' Since Ramadan's day is venerated, honoring its right is obligatory. If one is eligible for fasting, he fasts; if not, he honors it by abstaining. This abstention is not a substitute, so its obligation is not based on the obligation of fasting. Thus it can be obligatory on one not obligated to fast. In contrast, menstruating, post-natal, sick, and traveler are not required to abstain because these hindrances prevent both fasting and imitation. For menstruating and post-natal women, imitating fasters is forbidden because fasting itself is forbidden for them, and imitating a forbidden act is also forbidden. For the sick and traveler, imitation is prevented because they are permitted to break fast to avoid hardship; imposing imitation would contradict the purpose of the permission.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage addresses an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding a traveler returning or a menstruating woman becoming pure during a Ramadan day. The Hanafi position is that they must abstain from food, drink, and sexual relations for the remainder of the day (imsaak), even though their fasting was not obligatory at the start of the day. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such abstention is not obligatory. The passage begins by stating the ruling and the disagreement, then presents the Shafi'i argument: that imsaak is a substitute (khalīfah) for fasting, so it can only be obligatory on one for whom the original (fasting) is obligated. Since the traveler and menstruating woman were not obligated to fast, no substitute applies. The Hanafi rebuttal, key to the dispute, is that imsaak is not a substitute but a manifestation of honoring the sanctity of Ramadan (haqq al-waqt). The author provides a detailed commentary, explaining that the Shafi'i argument is based on analogy to one who intentionally or mistakenly breaks fast, where imsaak indeed is a substitute because fasting was originally required. But for the traveler and menstruating woman, the abstention is a direct obligation stemming from the veneration of the time. The Hanafi school further distinguishes between those whose excuses (like menstruation, postnatal bleeding, sickness, travel) completely negate both fasting and imitation of fasting, and those who become eligible later in the day—they honor the time by abstaining. The author concludes by noting that for the menstruating and post-natal women, imitation of fasters is forbidden because their fasting itself is forbidden; for the sick and traveler, it would defeat the purpose of their concession to break fast, which was to remove hardship.

Key Terms
امساک (imsaak): Refraining from eating, drinking, and sexual activity for the remainder of the day, even if not fasting the whole day.
خلیفہ (khalīfah): A substitute or replacement; here it refers to the view that imsaak stands in place of fasting when one is not actually fasting.
تشابہ بالصائمین (tashabbuh bi al-sā'imīn): Imitating those who are fasting by abstaining from nullifiers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a traveler who returns home during a Ramadan day required to abstain from eating and drinking for the rest of the day?
A) Because he must still complete the fast as if he had started it.
B) Because abstention is a substitute for the fasting he missed.
C) Because the time of Ramadan is venerated and honoring it requires abstaining from nullifiers.
D) Because he is sinful for having broken the fast earlier in the day.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi obligation of imsaak for those who become able to fast during a Ramadan day is rooted in the sanctity of the time (haqq al-waqt), not in a substitute for fasting.

Mistaken Suhoor or Iftar: Qada Without Kaffarah
Ruling with proof on mistaken eating/breaking fast during Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who eats suhoor or breaks fast due to a mistake about the time, and explain why only qada is required and not kaffarah, citing the proof from 'Umar (RA).

Core Idea
A mistaken fast break due to error about time requires qada but no kaffarah, as the violation lacks full intent.

In this lesson, we examine a common scenario where a person inadvertently breaks the fast due to a genuine mistake about the time. The Hanafi school draws a clear distinction between intentional and unintentional invalidations of the fast. We will explore the ruling, its proof from the statement of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA), and the underlying legal principle that intent determines the severity of the violation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is eating suhoor after the true dawn has risen, or breaking the fast before sunset, both done under the mistaken belief about the time. The ruling requires the person to abstain (imsaak) for the rest of the day and to make up the fast (qada) on another day. No expiation (kaffarah) is required.
This is a ruling on a specific mistaken action during Ramadan, not a general rule for all invalidations.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the saying of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'What have we inclined to? Then making up a day is easy for us.' This indicates that the mistake is not a grave violation warranting expiation.
This is a qawl sahabi (Companion statement), which is a source of law in the Hanafi school under certain conditions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'What have we inclined to?' shows that the action was not deliberate; the lack of intent makes the violation 'qasirah' (deficient). Hence, only qada is necessary, similar to the case of a sick person or traveler who breaks the fast.
The underlying principle is that the fast is a 'haqq madmun bi al-mithl' (a guarantee similar to it), so it must be replaced, but without additional penalty.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (if any)
The ruling is generally agreed upon among the schools. The Shafi'i school also holds no kaffarah for a mistake, though there may be a difference regarding the obligation of imsaak.
Even though it's agreed, the Hanafi reasoning is based on the deficiency of intent.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
This is the established position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, transmitted in the zahir al-riwayah. It is relied upon for fatwa.
No intra-Hanafi difference is mentioned; it is the agreed position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Source Text

قَالَ وَإِذَا تَسَحَرَ وَهُوَ يَظُنُّ أنَّ الْفَجْرَ لَمْ يَطْلُعْ فَإِذَا هُوَ قَدْ طَلَعَ أَوْ أفْطَرَ وَهُوَ يَرَى أَنَّ الشَّمْسَ قَدْ غَرُبَتْ فَإِذَا هِيَ لَمْ تَعْرُبُ أَمْسَكَ بَقِيَّةَ يَوْمِهِ قَضَاءً لِحَقِّ الْوَقْتِ بِالْقَدْرِ الْمُمْكِن أَو نَفْيًا للتّهمة و عَلَيْهِ القَضَاء لا ولأنه حق مَضْمُونُ بِالْمِثْلِ كَمَا فِى الْمَرِيضِ وَالْمُسَافِرِ وَلَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّ الْجِنَايَةَ قَاصِرَةُ لِعَدَمِ الْقَصْدِ وَ فِيهِ قَالَ عُمَرٌّ مَا تَجَانَفْنَا لا ثُم قَضَاءُ يَوْمِ عَلَيْنَا يَسِيرُ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْفَجْرِ الْفَجْرُ الثَّانِي وَقَدْ بَيَّنَاهُ فِي الصَّلوةَ
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ اگر سحری کھائی اور حال یہ کہ وہ گمان کرتا ہے کہ فجر طلوع نہیں ہوئی۔ پھر معلوم ہوا کہ فجر طلوع ہو چکی ہے۔ یا اس نے افطار کیا درانحالیکہ خیال کرتا ہے کہ آفتاب غروب ہو چکا۔ پھر معلوم ہوا کہ غروب نہیں ہوا تو یہ شخص باقی دن امساک کرے بقدر امکان وقت کا حق ادا کرنے کے لئے یا قسمت دور کرنے کے لئے اور اس پر قضا واجب ہے کیونکہ یہ حق مضمون بالمثل ہے جیسا کہ مریض اور مسافر میں ہے اور اس پر کفارہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ ارادہ نہ ہونے کی وجہت جرم قاصر ہے اور اسی کے بارے میں حضرت عمر نے فرمایا ہے کہ
One who ate suhoor thinking that the true dawn had not risen, but then found that it had risen; or one who broke fast thinking the sun had set, but then found it had not set: he should abstain for the remainder of the day, either as honoring the right of the time as much as possible, or to remove suspicion. He must make up (the fast) on another day, because it is a guarantee (of fasting) equivalent to it, as in the case of the sick and traveler. No kaffarah is upon him, because the violation is deficient due to lack of intent. Regarding this, 'Umar said, 'What have we inclined to? Then making up a day is easy for us.' The intended (dawn) is the second dawn (true dawn), which we have explained in the chapter on prayer.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for someone who eats suhoor (the pre-dawn meal) mistakenly thinking that the true dawn (al-fajr al-sādiq) has not yet risen, but then learns that it had actually risen. Similarly, one who breaks the fast thinking the sun has set, but then realizes it had not set. In both cases, the person must abstain from eating and drinking for the rest of the day (imsaak) as a gesture of honoring the time. Additionally, they must make up (qaḍā') the fast on another day, because the fast was not valid since an invalidating action occurred with the mistaken eating/breaking. However, no kaffārah (expiation) is required because the act was done without intent to invalidate the fast—the mistake was due to a misperception. The ruling is supported by the statement of 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), indicating that making up a day is an easy matter. The passage also clarifies that the 'fajr' meant here is the second dawn (true dawn), as distinguished from the false dawn. The commentary notes that the ruling is analogous to that of a sick person or traveler who breaks the fast—they must make up the day but have no kaffarah. The underlying principle is that the fast is a 'guarantee with its like' (ḥaqq maḍmūn bi al-mithl), meaning that when it is invalidated, it must be replaced by a similar day of fasting, but the sin is not severe enough to warrant expiation because the mistake was unintentional.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā'): Making up a missed or invalidated fast on a day after Ramadan.
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation required for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast without valid excuse; typically fasting 60 consecutive days, or feeding 60 poor people.
جناية قاصرة (jināyah qāṣirah): A deficient violation, one lacking full intent; here referring to breaking the fast due to a mistake about time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mistaken fast break due to time error requires qada but no kaffarah, as the violation lacks full intent.

The Ruling for a Person Who Mistakenly Eats Suhoor or Breaks Fast
States ruling for mistaken suhoor/iftar with evidence from Umar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who mistakenly eats suhoor or breaks fast, and explain the basis for the obligations of imsak, qada, and absence of kaffarah.

Core Idea
A mistaken action in fasting requires qada and imsak out of respect for the time, but no kaffarah due to lack of intent.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding situations where a person eats suhoor believing dawn has not yet broken, or breaks fast believing the sun has set, only to discover their mistake. The passage from al-Quduri, as explained in al-Hidayah, clarifies the obligations that follow: imsak (abstinence for the remainder of the day), qada (making up the fast), and the absence of kaffarah (expiation). We will explore the legal reasoning behind each component and the evidence from the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios covered
The passage covers (a) eating suhoor while thinking fajr has not yet risen, and (b) breaking fast while thinking the sun has set. Both are cases of mistaken belief about the time.
These are the only cases explicitly mentioned; the ruling extends to any invalidating action done under a similar mistake (e.g., drinking water thinking it was still night).
2
Determine the immediate obligation upon discovering the mistake
The ruling: imsak (abstain from eating, drinking, and other nullifiers for the rest of the day). Two reasons are given: fulfilling the right of the time (hurmat al-waqt) and to avoid suspicion (nafy al-tuhma).
Imsak is not because the remaining fast is valid; it is an obligation separate from the fast itself.
3
Determine the compensatory obligation
Qada is wajib. The passage compares to a sick or traveler who must make up missed fasts. The rationale: the missed fast is a 'right secured by its like' (haqq madmun bi'l-mithl), meaning it must be compensated by an equivalent fast.
This analogy shows that qada is required even when the invalidating act was unintentional.
4
Analyze the absence of kaffarah
No kaffarah is required because the offense is 'deficient due to the absence of intent' (al-jinayatu qasiratun li'adam al-qasd). Kaffarah is only for deliberate, intentional breaking of the fast.
This distinction highlights the importance of intention (niyya) in determining the severity of the ruling.
5
Examine the evidence from the incident of Umar (ra)
The passage cites a historical incident: Umar and his companions broke fast on a cloudy day thinking the sun had set, but then the sun reappeared. Umar said, 'We did not incline towards sin; the qada of a day is easy for us.' This confirms the fiqh ruling (imsak + qada, no kaffarah) and provides a direct precedent.
Umar's statement became a key proof (dalil) in the Hanafi school for this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا تَسَحَرَ وَهُوَ يَظُنُّ أَنَّ الْفَجْرَ لَمْ يَطْلُعْ فَإِذَا هُوَ قَدْ طَلَعَ أَوْ أَفْطَرَ وَهُوَ يَرَى أَنَّ الشَّمْسَ قَدْ غَرَبَتْ فَإِذَا هِيَ لَمْ تَغْرُبْ أَمْسَكَ بَقِيَّةَ يَوْمِهِ قَضَاءً لِحَقِّ الْوَقْتِ بِالْقَدْرِ الْمُمْكِنِ أَوْ نَفْيًا لِلتُّهْمَةِ وَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ لِأَنَّهُ حَقٌّ مَضْمُونٌ بِالْمِثْلِ كَمَا فِي الْمَرِيضِ وَالْمُسَافِرِ وَلَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّ الْجِنَايَةَ قَاصِرَةٌ لِعَدَمِ الْقَصْدِ وَفِيهِ قَالَ عُمَرُ مَا تَجَانَفْنَا لِإِثْمٍ ثُمَّ قَضَاءُ يَوْمٍ عَلَيْنَا يَسِيرٌ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْفَجْرِ الْفَجْرُ الثَّانِي وَقَدْ بَيَّنَّاهُ فِي الصَّلَاةِ
He said: And when one eats suhoor while thinking that dawn has not risen, and then it is found that it had risen, or one breaks fast while thinking that the sun has set, and then it is found that it had not set, he must refrain for the rest of his day as a fulfillment of the right of the time to the extent possible, or to remove suspicion, and qada is obligatory upon him because it is a right secured by its like, just as in the case of the sick and the traveler, and there is no kaffarah upon him because the offense is deficient due to the absence of intent. And concerning this, Umar said: 'We did not incline towards sin; the qada of a day is easy for us.' And what is meant by dawn is the second dawn, and we have explained it in the chapter on prayer.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Quduri, explained in the context of Hanafi fiqh. It addresses two scenarios: one who eats suhoor under the mistaken belief that true dawn (fajr sadiq) has not yet appeared, and one who breaks his fast thinking the sun has set when it has not. In both cases, the ruling is that the person must abstain from food, drink, and other nullifiers for the remainder of the day. This obligation is not because his day is a valid fast, but rather out of respect for the sanctity of Ramadan, as the time itself demands reverence. Alternatively, it is to avoid suspicion, as it is obligatory to avoid places of accusation. Additionally, qada (making up the fast) is wajib because the missed fast is a right that must be compensated by an equivalent—a like-for-like substitution, similar to how a sick or traveler must make up missed fasts. However, no kaffarah (expiation) is required because kaffarah is only due when the fast is deliberately and intentionally broken without valid excuse; here the action was based on a mistaken assumption, not intentional transgression. The passage cites an incident involving Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) where he and some Companions broke their fast upon a mistaken call of sunset. When the error was discovered, Umar said, 'We did not incline towards sin; making up one day is easy for us.' This confirms the fiqh ruling. The text also clarifies that 'fajr' here means the second dawn (fajr sadiq), which is the true beginning of the fast.

Key Terms
سحور (suhoor): The pre-dawn meal eaten before fasting, specifically before the second dawn (fajr sadiq).
إمساك (imsak): To abstain from nullifiers of fasting, used here for the obligation to refrain for the rest of the day out of respect for Ramadan.
قضاء (qada): Compensatory fasting performed after Ramadan to make up for an invalid or missed fast.
كفارة (kaffarah): An expiatory penalty for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast without excuse, consisting of freeing a slave, fasting two months consecutively, or feeding sixty poor people.
الفجر الثاني (al-fajr al-thani): The true dawn (fajr sadiq), which appears as a horizontal light across the horizon, marking the start of the fasting day and the time for Fajr prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must continue eating and make up the fast later, no kaffarah.
B) He must refrain for the rest of the day and make up the fast later, no kaffarah.
C) He must refrain for the rest of the day, make up the fast, and pay kaffarah.
D) He may choose whether to continue or stop; either way, he must make up the fast.

Key Takeaway
In cases of mistaken suhoor or iftar, the Hanafi school requires imsak and qada, but no kaffarah, due to the absence of intentional transgression.

Suhoor: A Recommended Pre-Dawn Meal and Its Preferred Timing
States that suhoor is mustahabb and delaying it is recommended

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on suhoor and explain why delaying it is recommended.

Core Idea
Suhoor is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory; delaying it increases blessing.

The pre-dawn meal, suhoor, is a confirmed practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). While some may think it is required, the Hanafi school clarifies its recommended nature. This lesson examines the evidence and the preferred timing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on suhoor
From the text, suhoor is declared mustahabb (مستحب). Recognize that this is a recommended act, not obligatory.
Mustahabb is below sunnah muakkadah? Actually here it is treated as sunnah muakkadah, but the text calls it mustahabb. According to Hanafi classification, mustahabb and sunnah are often used interchangeably for recommended acts.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is a hadith: 'Take suhoor, for in suhoor there is blessing.' This hadith is the primary evidence.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning (qati al-thubut) but the imperative is interpreted as recommendation (zanni al-dalala) due to other evidence showing it is not obligatory.
3
Understand the barakah (blessing)
The word 'barakah' indicates that suhoor brings spiritual and physical blessings. This motivates adherence without imposing obligation.
4
Note the recommendation to delay suhoor
The text explicitly says delaying suhoor (until near fajr) is also mustahabb, based on another Prophetic statement (the hadith about hastening iftar and delaying suhoor).
This aligns with the Prophet's practice and maximizes the time between suhoor and dawn.
5
Distinguish mustahabb from wajib
Understand that an imperative (amr) in Hanafi usul does not automatically imply obligation if there is evidence that the act is not compulsory. Here, the Prophet sometimes fasted without suhoor, confirming it is not wajib.
This step refines the understanding of legal categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ السَّحْرُ مُسْتَحَبٌّ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ تَسَحَّرُوا فَإِنَّ فِي السُّحُورِ بَرَكَةٌ، وَالْمُسْتَحَبُّ تَأْخِيرُهُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ
Then suhoor is recommended (mustahabb) due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Take suhoor, for indeed in suhoor there is blessing.' And delaying it is recommended due to his saying, peace be upon him: ...
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the Hanafi text regarding the pre-dawn meal (suhoor). The passage establishes that suhoor is mustahabb (highly recommended) based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) which encourages taking suhoor and describes it as containing barakah (blessing). The text further states that it is mustahabb to delay the suhoor until close to the time of fajr, as this is the practice of the Prophet. Although the hadith for delay is cut off in the OCR, it is well-known: 'My community will remain upon goodness as long as they hasten to break the fast and delay the suhoor.' In Hanafi fiqh, suhoor is not obligatory but a confirmed sunnah. The blessing mentioned includes spiritual and physical strength for the fast.

Key Terms
سحور (suhoor): The pre-dawn meal taken before beginning the fast, typically before the second dawn (fajr sadiq).
مستحب (mustahabb): An act that is recommended; performing it earns reward, but omitting it is not sinful.
بركة (barakah): Divine blessing and increase in goodness; suhoor brings spiritual and physical benefits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is wajib (obligatory); one must eat suhoor.
B) It is mustahabb (recommended) and delaying it is also mustahabb.
C) It is sunnah muakkadah but must be eaten at midnight.
D) It is makruh to eat suhoor because it delays the fast.

Key Takeaway
Suhoor is a highly recommended sunnah, not an obligation; delaying it until near fajr maximizes its blessing.

intermediate
6 min
Mistaken Suhoor or Iftar: Imsak and Qada without Sin or Kaffarah
Explaining ruling on mistaken suhoor/iftar: imsak and qada wajib, no sin/kaffarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for mistaken suhoor or iftar and explain why imsak and qada are wajib but no sin or kaffarah.

Core Idea
A mistaken fast-break requires imsak and qada, but no sin or kaffarah—error makes the offence incomplete.

What happens when you eat suhoor thinking it's still night, but dawn has already broken? Or break your fast early, only to realize the sun hadn't set? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on such mistakes: you must refrain for the rest of the day and make up the fast later, but you incur no sin and no expiation (kaffarah). The reasoning hinges on the nature of the error and the authority of a Companion's precedent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the two scenarios (mistaken suhoor after true dawn, mistaken iftar before sunset). State the three-part ruling: imsak (refraining) for the rest of the day is wajib, qada (making up) the fast is wajib, but there is no sin and no kaffarah.
Imsak is wajib out of respect for the sanctity of Ramadan and to avoid public suspicion.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites the incident of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA) and a bowl of milk. Identify this as a qawl sahabi (Companion's statement) used as proof. Also the reasoning that fasting is compensable by its like (mawmun bil-mithl).
The Hanafi school accepts qawl sahabi as a source when it does not contradict stronger evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Examine Umar's statement: 'We did not intentionally incline towards sin; performing qada of one day is easy for us.' This shows that because the act was unintentional (error), there is no sin; and because the fast is compensable, only qada is required—not kaffarah. The principle of jurm qasir (incomplete offence) supports this.
Kaffarah is only for a complete, deliberate violation; error reduces the offence to incomplete (qasir).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i in some views) may require kaffarah for any intentional eating, even if mistaken. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the presence of error and the incomplete nature of the offence.
The ikhtilaf stems from different interpretations of the hadith evidence and the definition of 'deliberate'.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Al-Hidayah presents this as the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) without dispute within the Hanafi school. The proof from Umar's practice and the legal maxim that compensable rights require like-for-like compensation (mawmun bil-mithl) strengthens the ruling.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah, and no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists.

ہم نے کسی گناہ کی طرف میلان نہیں کیا ہم پر ایک دن کی قضاء کرنا آسان ہے۔ اور فجر سے مراد فجر ثانی ہے اور ہم اس کو کتاب الصلوۃ میں بیان کر چکے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ رمضان کی رات میں کسی نے یہ گمان کر کے سحری کھائی کہ ابھی صبح صادق نہیں ہوئی۔ بعد میں تحقیق ہوئی کہ صبح صادق ہو چکی تھی۔ یا کسی نے یہ سمجھ کر کہ غروب آفتاب ہو چکا افطار کر لیا۔ پھر معلوم ہوا کہ ابھی غروب نہیں ہوا تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں باقی دن کا امساک واجب ہے یعنی پہلی صورت میں تو تقریباً پورے دن کا امساک واجب ہے اور دوسری صورت میں جتنا وقت غروب باقی ہے۔ اس کا امساک واجب ہے اور اس دن کے روزے کی قضا واجب ہے لیکن ی شخص اپنے اس فعل پر نہ گنہ گار ہوگا اور نہ اس پر کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ ان دونوں صورتوں میں امساک تو اس لئے واجب ہے تاکہ رمضان کے دن کا حق بقدر امکان ادا ہو سکے ۔ جیسا کہ تفصیل گذشتہ مسئلہ میں مذکور ہے یا تہمت کو دور کرنے کے لئے اس لئے کہ اگر اس نے کچھ کھایا پیا۔ اور بظاہر کوئی عذر بھی نہیں ہے تو لوگ اس کو فسق و فجور کے ساتھ متہم کریں گے اور مواضع تہمت سے بچنا واجب ہے جیسا کہ حدیث میں ہے إِتَّقُوا مَوَاضِعَ النُّهْمَةِ - اور قضا اس لئے واجب ہے کہ روزہ ایسا حق شرعی ہے جو مضمون بالمثل ہے یعنی ادا فوت ہونے سے ساقط نہ ہوگا بلکہ شرعاً اس کا ضمان بالمثل واجب ہوگا ۔ یعنی روزہ کے بدلہ روزہ واجب ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ مریض اور مسافر کے حق میں یہ ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے اور کفارہ اس لئے واجب نہ ہوگا کہ یہ جرم ناقص ہے کیونکہ اس کا صبح صادق کے بعد سحری کھانا یا غروب سے پہلے افطار کرنا بالا رادہ نہیں ہے بلکہ اس نے رات گمان کر کے سحری کھائی اور غروب آفتاب گمان کر کے افطار کیا ہے بہر حال جرم قاصر ہے اور جرم قاصر ہونے کی وجہ سے کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا ۔ کفارہ واجب ہونے کے لئے جرم کا کامل ہونا ضروری ہے اس کی تائید فاروق اعظم کے قول سے بھی ہوتی ہے مروی ہے کہ ایک مرتبہ رمضان کے مہینہ میں غروب کے وقت حضرت عمر اور بعض صحابہ مسجد کوفہ کے صحن میں تشریف فرما تھے ۔ دودھ کا ایک پیالہ لایا گیا آپ نے خود بھی پیا اور صحابہ نے نوش فرمایا اور موذن سے کہا کہ جاؤ اذان دو۔ پس جب وہ اذان دینے کے لئے اوپر چڑھا تو دیکھا کہ ابھی آفتاب موجود ہے تو اس نے شور مچا کر کہا الشَّمْس يَا أَمِيرَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ ۔ امیر المومنین ابھی سورج موجود ہے ڈوبا نہیں ۔ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا إِنَّا أَرْسَلْنَاكَ دَاعِيًا وَلَمْ نَبْعَثْكَ رَاعِيًا مَا تَجَانَفْنَا لِإِثْمٍ قَضَاءُ يَوْمٍ عَلَيْنَا يَسِيرٌ ۔ یعنی ہم نے تجھ کو داعی بنا کر بھیجا ہے۔ رائی بنا کر نہیں بھیجا۔ ہم نے ( خدانخواستہ) گناہ کا ارادہ نہیں کیا ہم پر ایک روزہ کی قضا کرنا آسان ہے۔ اس واقعہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ایسی اجتہادی غلطی سے اگر روزہ فاسد ہو گیا تو صرف قضاء واجب ہوگی نہ گنہ گار ہوگا اور نہ کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ ایک روایت میں یہ ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے کہا کہ مَنْ كَانَ أَفْطَرَ فَلْيَصُمْ يَوْمًا مَكَانَهُ وَمَنْ لَّمْ يَكُنْ أَفْطَرَ فَلْيُتِمَّ حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ یعنی جب موذن نے یہ خبر دی کہ ابھی آفتاب غروب نہیں ہوا تو حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا کہ جس نے افطار کر لیا وہ اس کی جگہ ایک روزہ رکھ لے یعنی قضا کر لے۔ اور جس نے افطار نہیں کیا وہ پورا کرے۔ یہاں تک کہ سورج ڈوب جائے ۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ متن میں فجر سے مراد فجر ثانی یعنی صبح صادق ہے۔
We did not incline towards any sin; performing qada of one day is easy for us. And by Fajr is meant the second Fajr (true dawn), and we have explained it in the Book of Prayer. Explanation of the issue: In the night of Ramadan, someone ate suhoor assuming that true dawn had not yet occurred, but later it was confirmed that true dawn had occurred. Or someone iftared thinking sunset had occurred, then knew that sunset had not occurred. In both cases, refraining for the rest of the day is wajib: in the first case, refraining for the entire day is wajib; in the second, for the remaining time until sunset is wajib. And qada of that day's fast is wajib. But that person will not be sinful for his action, nor will kaffarah be obligatory upon him. In both cases, refraining is wajib so that the right of the day of Ramadan can be fulfilled as much as possible, as detailed in the previous issue, or to avoid accusation because if he eats/drinks and there is no apparent excuse, people will accuse him of sin, and avoiding places of accusation is wajib, as in the hadith: 'Avoid places of accusation.' Qada is wajib because fasting is a shariah right that is compensable by its like; it does not lapse by missing its performance; rather, compensation by its like becomes obligatory, i.e., a day for a day, as compensation is obligatory for the sick and traveler. Kaffarah is not wajib because this offence is incomplete (jurm qasir), since his eating after true dawn or iftar before sunset was not intentional; rather, he ate assuming it was night, and broke fast assuming sunset. In any case, the offence is incomplete, and kaffarah is not obligatory for an incomplete offence. For kaffarah to be wajib, the offence must be complete. This is supported by the statement of Farooq al-Azam. It is narrated that once in Ramadan at sunset, Umar and some companions were sitting in the courtyard of the Kufa mosque. A bowl of milk was brought; he drank and the companions drank, and he told the muezzin to go and give the adhan. When he went up to call the adhan, he saw that the sun was still visible, so he shouted, 'The sun, O Commander of the Faithful, the sun is still present, it has not set.' Umar said: 'We sent you as a caller, not as a herder. We did not intentionally incline towards sin; performing qada of one day is easy for us.' This incident shows that if a fast is broken due to such ijtihadi error, only qada is wajib; he is not sinful, nor is kaffarah wajib. In one narration, Umar said: 'Whoever broke his fast, let him fast a day in its place, and whoever did not break, let him complete his fast until the sun sets.' Sahib al-Hidayah says: By Fajr in the text is meant the second Fajr, i.e., true dawn.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof, discussing the case of someone who mistakenly eats suhoor after true dawn or breaks fast before sunset in Ramadan. The ruling is that in both scenarios, the person must refrain from eating/drinking for the remainder of the day (imsak) and must make up that day (qada) later. However, there is no sin upon him, nor is kaffarah (expiation) required. The reason for imsak is to fulfill the sanctity of the day as much as possible and to avoid public suspicion. The proof for the obligation of qada is that fasting is a shariah right that is compensable by its like (mawmun bil-mithl), similar to the case of a sick or traveler. Kaffarah is not required because the act was not deliberate; the person acted on a mistaken assumption (jurm qasir), and kaffarah is only for a complete, intentional violation. The passage supports this with the incident of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who, upon learning that the sun had not yet set, ordered qada only, not kaffarah, and stated that they had no intention of sin. The author of Al-Hidayah clarifies that 'Fajr' in the text refers to the true dawn (Fajr al-Sadiq), which is the actual start of the fast, not the false dawn.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory fast on another day after Ramadan.
إمساك (imsak): Refraining from eating, drinking, and other nullifiers of fasting for the remainder of the day out of respect for the sacred time.
كفارة (kaffarah): An expiatory act (freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor) required for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast without excuse.
جرم قاصر (jurm qasir): An incomplete offence where the act is not fully deliberate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person who eats suhoor thinking it is still night, but later discovers that Fajr had already entered?
A) His fast is invalid, and he must refrain for the day, make it up later, and pay kaffarah.
B) His fast is invalid, but he need not refrain; only qada is required.
C) He must refrain for the day, make qada later, but no sin or kaffarah.
D) His fast is valid because he acted on a reasonable assumption.

Key Takeaway
Mistaken fast-break: imsak and qada are wajib; no sin or kaffarah due to incomplete offence (jurm qasir).

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Suhoor: Recommendation, Timing, and Doubt about Fajr
Ruling statement with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on suhoor (mustahabb), explain the preferred timing, and apply the principle that certainty is not removed by doubt in cases of doubt about Fajr.

Core Idea
Suhoor is mustahabb, not wajib; delaying it is recommended, and doubt about Fajr does not invalidate the fast.

This lesson from Al-Hidayah clarifies the legal status of the pre-dawn meal (suhoor) in Ramadan. It is firmly recommended but not obligatory. The text also addresses a practical scenario: what if you are unsure whether Fajr has entered? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer balancing precaution and the principle of certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling of suhoor and its proof
Determine the hukm level of suhoor (mustahabb) and cite the hadith that serves as the primary evidence.
The imperative 'تَسَحَّرُوا' indicates recommendation, not obligation, per Hanafi usul.
2
Understand the recommendation of delaying suhoor
Note that delaying suhoor until close to Fajr is also mustahabb, based on the hadith about the traits of the messengers.
Contrast with iftar, which is to be hastened.
3
Analyze the doubt scenario (shakk)
Recognize that if doubt is equal (shakk), the preferred action is to leave eating, but it is not obligatory. If one eats, the fast remains valid because the original assumption (night) prevails.
Shakk is distinct from wahm or ghalabah.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on qada
Identify the two narrations: one requiring qada when predominant opinion (ghalib al-rayy) indicates Fajr had entered, and the other (Zahir al-Riwayah) requiring no qada.
The dispute is about the weight of predominant opinion versus the principle of certainty.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Understand that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Zahir al-Riwayah view: no qada is required because certainty is only removed by certainty.
This is the view adopted in Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سحری کی شرعی حیثیت
ثُمَّ السَّحْرُ مُسْتَحَبٌّ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ تَسَحَّرُوا فَإِنَّ فِي السُّحُورِ بَرَكَةٌ، وَالْمُسْتَحَبُّ تَأْخِيرُهُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ ثَلَاثٌ مِنْ أَخْلَاقِ الْمُرْسَلِينَ تَعْجِيلُ الْإِفْطَارِ وَتَأْخِيرُ السُّحُورِ وَالسِّوَاكُ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ إِذَا شَكَّ فِي الْفَجْرِ وَمَعْنَاهُ تَسَاوِي الطَّرَفَيْنِ فَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَدَعَ الْأَكْلَ تَحَرُّزًا عَنِ الْمُحَرَّمِ وَلَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ ذَلِكَ وَلَوْ أَكَلَ فَصَوْمُهُ تَامٌّ لِأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ هُوَ اللَّيْلُ وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِذَا كَانَ فِي مَوْضِعٍ لَا يَسْتَبِينُ الْفَجْرُ أَوْ كَانَتِ اللَّيْلَةُ مُقْمِرَةً أَوْ مُتَغَيِّمَةً أَوْ كَانَ بِبَصَرِهِ عِلَّةً وَهُوَ يَشُكُّ لَا يَأْكُلُ وَلَوْ أَكَلَ فَقَدْ أَسَاءَ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ دَعْ مَا يُرِيبُكَ إِلَى مَا لَا يُرِيبُكَ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَكْثَرُ رَأْيِهِ أَنَّهُ أَكَلَ وَالْفَجْرُ طَالِعٌ فَعَلَيْهِ قَضَاؤُهُ عَمَلًا بِغَالِبِ الرَّأْيِ وَفِيهِ الْإِحْتِيَاطُ وَعَلَى ظَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَةِ لَا قَضَاءَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّ الْيَقِينَ لَا يَزُولُ إِلَّا بِمِثْلِه
ترجمہ پھر سحری کھانا مستحب ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرما ما ہے کہ سحری کھاؤ اس لئے کہ سحری کھانے میں برکت ہے اور سحری کھانے میں تاخیر کرنا مستحب ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ تین باتیں رسولوں کے اخلاق سے ہیں۔ افطار میں جلدی کرنا اور سحری کھانے میں دیر کرنا اور مسواک کرنا مگر جبکہ اس کو فجر میں شک ہوا در شک کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ دونوں طرف گمان برابر ہو ۔ تو افضل یہ ہے کہ کھانا چھوڑ دے حرام سے بچنے کی وجہ سے اور اس پر کھانا چھوڑنا واجب نہیں ہے اور اگر اس نے کھا لیا تو اس کا روزہ پورا ہے کیونکہ اصل تو رات ہے اور ابو حنیفہ سے مروی ہے اگر وہ شخص ایسی جگہ میں ہے جہاں فجر ظاہر نہیں ہوتی یا رات چاندنی ہو یا رات ابر آلود ہو یا اس کی نگاہ میں کوئی بیماری ہو اور اس کو فجر میں شک ہے نہ کھائے اور اگر اس نے کھا لیا تو برا کام کیا۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جو چیز تجھ کو شک میں ڈالے اس کو چھوڑ کر وہ اختیار کر جو تجھ کوشک میں نہیں ڈالتی ہے اور اگر اس کا ظن غالب یہ ہو کہ اس نے سحری کھائی حالانکہ فجر طلوع ہو چکی تھی تو اس پر اس کی قضاء کرنا واجب ہے کیونکہ غالب رائے پر عمل کرنا واجب ہے اور احتیاط بھی اسی میں ہے اور ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق اس پر قضاء واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ یقین نہیں زائل ہوتا مگر اس کے مثل ہے۔
تشریح بحر ، آخر شب کا نام ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ رات کا سدس اخیر ہے یعنی آخری چھٹا حصہ سحور اس چیز کا نام ہے جو اس وقت کھائی جائے ۔ بہر حال سحری کھانا امر مستحب ہے اور دلیل یہ حدیث ہے تَسَحَّرُوا فَإِنَّ فِي السُّحُورِ بَرَكَة اور حدیث میں برکت سے مراد آئندہ کل کے روزہ پر قوت حاصل کرتا ہے۔ ترجمہ ہو گا کہ سحری کھاؤ کیونکہ سحری کھانے میں قوت حاصل کرنا ہے اس کی تائید حدیث سے ہوتی ہے۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا اسْتَعِينُوا بِقَيْلُولَةِ النَّهَارِ عَلَى قِيَامِ اللَّيْلِ وَبِأَكْلِ السَّحَرِ عَلَى صِيَامِ النَّهَارِ یعنی دن میں قیلولہ اور آرام کر کے قیام لیل پر مدد طلب کرو اور سحری کھانے سے دن کے روزے پر مدد طلب کرو ۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ دن میں کچھ آرام کر لیا کرو۔ تا کہ رات میں نمازیں پڑھنے میں قوت ملے ۔ اور سحری کھا لیا کرو تا کہ دن کے روزے میں قوت حاصل ہو ۔ بعض نے کہا کہ حدیث میں برکت سے مراد زیادتی ثواب کو حاصل کرنا ہے کیونکہ سحری کھانا انبیاء کی سنت ہے اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ سنت انبیاء پر عمل کرنا زیادتی اجر کا باعث ہے اس لئے لفظ برکت سے زیادتی ثواب بھی مراد ہو سکتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سحری میں تاخیر مستحب ہے اور دلیل یہ حدیث ہے کہ رسولوں کی تین عادتیں ہیں،
1) افطار میں جلدی کرنا۔ (۲) سحری کھانے میں دیر کرنا۔
(۳) مسواک کرنا۔
Then suhoor is mustahabb due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Have suhoor, for in suhoor there is blessing.' And delaying it is mustahabb due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Three are from the character of the messengers: hastening iftar, delaying suhoor, and using the siwak.' Except that when he doubts about Fajr, meaning both sides are equal in his mind, then it is better to leave eating to avoid the forbidden, but it is not obligatory upon him. If he eats, his fast is complete because the original assumption is that it is still night. And from Abu Hanifa: If he is in a place where Fajr is not apparent, or the night is moonlit or cloudy, or there is a defect in his sight, and he is in doubt, he should not eat. If he eats, he has done wrong due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' And if his predominant opinion is that he ate while Fajr had risen, then upon him is its qada, acting upon the predominant opinion, and in it is precaution. And according to Zahir al-Riwayah, there is no qada upon him because certainty is only removed by certainty. Translation: Then eating suhoor is mustahabb because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Have suhoor, for in suhoor there is blessing.' And delaying suhoor is mustahabb because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Three things are from the character of the messengers: hastening iftar, delaying suhoor, and using the siwak.' Except when he doubts about Fajr, meaning both sides are equal, then it is better to leave eating to avoid the forbidden, but it is not obligatory upon him. If he eats, his fast is complete because the original assumption is that it is night. And from Abu Hanifa: If a person is in a place where Fajr is not apparent, or the night is moonlit or cloudy, or there is a defect in his sight, and he is in doubt, he should not eat. If he eats, he has done wrong because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' And if his predominant opinion is that he ate while Fajr had risen, then qada is wajib upon him, because acting on predominant opinion is wajib, and precaution is in it. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, qada is not wajib because certainty is only removed by certainty. Explanation: 'Sahar' is the name of the last part of the night; some say it is the last sixth. 'Suhur' is the food eaten at that time. In any case, eating suhoor is a recommended act. The proof is this hadith: 'Have suhoor, for in suhoor there is blessing.' Some say blessing means gaining strength for the next day's fast. This is supported by the hadith: 'Seek help with the midday nap for standing at night, and with eating suhoor for fasting the day.' Some say blessing means extra reward, because suhoor is a practice of the prophets. Sahib al-Hidayah says: Delaying suhoor is mustahabb, and the proof is the hadith: Three are the habits of the messengers: 1) hastening iftar, 2) delaying suhoor, 3) using miswak.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof, discussing the legal status of suhoor (pre-dawn meal) in Ramadan. It establishes that suhoor is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory, based on the Prophet's command 'Have suhoor, for in suhoor there is blessing.' Delaying it until close to Fajr is also mustahabb, as it is a trait of the messengers. However, when one is in doubt about the arrival of Fajr, the preferred action is to stop eating to avoid the risk of eating after dawn (which is forbidden), but it is not wajib to stop. If one eats while in doubt, the fast is still valid because the original assumption is that it is still night. The passage then presents a position from Abu Hanifa regarding cases where Fajr is not easily discernible (e.g., cloudy night, moonlit night, or visual impairment): in such cases, one should not eat if in doubt, and if one does eat, he has done wrong, based on the hadith 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' A further dispute within the Hanafi school is mentioned: According to a narration (predominant opinion), if one's strong opinion is that he ate after Fajr, then qada is wajib. But according to Zahir al-Riwayah (the authoritative transmission), no qada is required because certainty (that the fast is valid) is only removed by certainty (that Fajr had entered). The commentary explains the meaning of 'sahar' and provides additional support for the blessing of suhoor.

Key Terms
سحور (suhoor): The pre-dawn meal eaten before Fajr in Ramadan.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended but not obligatory; performing it brings reward, omitting it does not incur sin.
شك (shakk): Doubt where both possibilities are equally strong (tasawi al-tarafayn).
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The most authoritative transmitted ruling within the Hanafi school, as recorded by Muhammad al-Shaybani in his six major works.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the ruling if a person eats suhoor while in doubt about Fajr, and it turns out Fajr had already entered?
A) His fast is invalid and qada is wajib.
B) His fast is valid and no qada is required.
C) He must refrain for the rest of the day but no qada.
D) He must perform kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
Suhoor is recommended, doubt about Fajr does not break the fast, and no qada is required according to the relied-upon narration of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Suhoor Ruling and Doubt About Fajr
Explains suhoor rulings and consequences of doubt about fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating suhoor and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute about qada when doubt about fajr is resolved by dominant opinion.

Core Idea
Certainty of night overcomes doubt; suhoor is recommended, not obligatory.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses two issues: the recommendation of suhoor and its timing, and what happens when a person doubts whether fajr has arrived. The key legal principle is that certainty (the original night) is not removed by mere doubt or dominant opinion. We will explore the proofs and the internal Hanafi difference on whether qada is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on suhoor and its proof
First, understand that eating suhoor and delaying it are mustahabb (recommended). The proof is the Prophet's command 'تسحروا' and the hadith listing three prophetic traits. In Hanafi usul, amr indicates wujub unless there is a qarinah showing nadb.
The command 'تسحروا' is interpreted as recommendation because of other evidences showing it is not obligatory.
2
Understand the scenario of equal doubt about fajr
When a person has equal doubt (shakk) whether fajr has arrived, it is better to stop eating to avoid the prohibited, but it is not obligatory. If he eats, his fast remains valid because the original certainty is that it is night.
The principle 'اليقين لا يزال بالشك' applies here.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding qada
The passage presents two views: (1) according to some (including a Nawadir narration from Abu Hanifa), if later a dominant opinion (ghalib al-ray) indicates fajr had risen, qada is obligatory out of caution. (2) According to Zahir al-Riwayah, no qada is required because certainty of night cannot be removed by dominant opinion.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school itself.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and the basis for tarjih
The relied-upon position is that of Zahir al-Riwayah: no qada. This is because the usul principle that certainty is not removed by doubt is stronger than the principle of caution. Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah supports this view.
The mufta bihi is the position that eases upon the people.

السَّلَامُ ثَلَاثَ مِنْ أَخْلَاقِ الْمُرْسَلِينَ تَعْجِيلُ الأقْطَارِ وَتَاخِيرُ السُّحُورِ وَالسّوَاكُ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ إِذَا شَكَ فِى الْفَجْر وَمَعْنَاهُ تَسَاوِى الطَّرَفَيْنِ فَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَّدَعَ الأكْلَ تَحَرَّزًا عَنِ الْمُحَرَّمِ وَلَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ ذَلِكَ وَلَوْ أَكَلَ فَصَوْمُهُ تَامٌّ لأنَّ الْأَصْلَ هُوَ اللَّيْلَ وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِذَا كَانَ فِي مَوْضِعَ لَا يَسْتَبِينُ الْفَجْرُ أوْ كَانَتِ اليْلَةُ مُقْمَرَةً أَو مُتَعَيِّمَةً أو كانَ بِبَصَرِهِ عِلَّةً وَهُوَ يَشْكُ لَا يَأكُلُ وَلَوْ أَكَلَ فَقَدْ أَسَاءَ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ دَعْ مَا يُرِيبُكَ إِلَى مَا لَا يُرِيبُكَ وَ إِنْ كَانَ أَكْبَرُ رَأْيِهِ أَنَّهُ أَكَلَ وَالْفَجُرُ طَالِعُ فَعَلَيْهِ قَضَاؤُهُ عَمَلًا بِغَالِبِ الرَّأْيِ وَفِيْهِ الْإِحْتِيَاطُ وَعَلَى ظَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَةِ لاَ قَضَاءَ عَلَيْهِ لأَنَّ الْيَقِيْنَ لَا يَزَالُ إِلَّا بِمِثْلِه. ترجمہ پھر سحری کھانا مستحب ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرما ما ہے کہ سحری کھاؤ اس لئے کہ سحری کھانے میں برکت ہے اور سحری کھانے میں تاخیر کرنا مستحب ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ تین باتیں رسولوں کے اخلاق سے ہیں۔ افطار میں جلدی کرنا اور سحری کھانے میں دیر کرنا اور مسواک کرنا مگر جبکہ اس کو فجر میں شک ہوا در شک کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ دونوں طرف گمان برابر ہو ۔ تو افضل یہ ہے کہ کھانا چھوڑ دے حرام سے بچنے کی وجہ سے اور اس پر کھانا چھوڑنا واجب نہیں ہے اور اگر اس نے کھا لیا تو اس کا روزہ پورا ہے کیونکہ اصل تو رات ہے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا اسْتَعِينُوا بِقَيْلُولَةِ النَّهَارِ عَلَى قِيَامِ اللَّيْلِ وَبِأَكْلِ السَّحَرِ عَلَى صِيَامِ النَّهَارِ یعنی دن میں قیلولہ اور آرام کر کے قیام لیل پر مدد طلب کہ حدیث میں برکت سے مراد زیادتی ثواب کو حاصل کرنا ہے کیونکہ سحری کھانا انبیاء کی سنت ہے اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ سنت انبیاء پر عمل کرنا زیادتی اجر کا باعث ہے اس لئے لفظ برکت سے زیادتی ثواب بھی مراد ہو سکتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بحری میں تا خیر مستحب ہے اور دلیل یہ حدیث ہے کہ رسولوں کی تین عادتیں ہیں، 1) افطار میں جلدی کرنا۔ (۲) سحری کھانے میں دیر کرنا۔ (۳) مسواک کرنا۔ اس حدیث پر بظاہر ایک اشکال ہو سکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ سحری کھانا اہل اسلام اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی امت کی خصوصیات میں سے ہے۔ پس سحری میں تاخیر مرسلین اور انبیاء کی عادات سے کس طرح ہو سکتا ہے نیز خود حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے فَرْقُ مَابَيْنَ صِيَامِنَا وَصَيَامٍ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ أَكَلُ السُّحُورِ یعنی ہمارے روزوں اور اہل کتاب کے روزوں کے درمیان با بہ الامتیاز سحری کھانا ہے۔ اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ امم سابقہ میں سحری کھانے کا رواج نہ تھا۔ پس جب سابقہ امتوں میں سحری نہیں تھی تو رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان قلت من أخْلَاقِ المُرْسَلِينَ. الحدیث کیسے درست ہوگا ۔ اس اشکال کا ایک جواب تو یہ ہے کہ دونوں حدیثوں میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے۔ گا۔ کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ انبیاء سابقین سحری کھاتے ہوں اور ان کی امتوں کے لئے سحری نہ ہو۔ پس اب حدیث اول میں تاخیر محور کو اخلاق ا امرسین سے قرار دینا اور اہل اسلام اور اہل کتاب کے درمیان سحری کھانے کو ما بہ الامتیاز قرار دینا دونوں درست ہو جائے گا۔ ایک دوسرا جواب عنایہ وغیرہ میں اور دیا گیا ہے جس کو اختصار کے پیش نظر چھوڑ دیا گیا۔ صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ سحری کھانا تو بلاشبہ مستحب ہے لیکن اگر فجر میں شک ہو گیا کہ فجر طلوع ہوئی یا نہیں اور دونوں جانب برابر ہیں تو افضل یہ ہے کہ کھانا، پینا ترک کر دے اور کوئی مفطر چیز استعمال نہ کرے تاکہ یقین کے ساتھ فعل حرام سے بچ جائے ۔ اور یہ کھانا پینا ترک کرنا اس پر واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر شک کے باوجود اس نے کچھ کھا پی لیا تو اس کا روزہ پورا ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اصل تو رات ہے لہذا اس اصل کا حکم رہے گا۔ تا وقتیکہ اس کے مخالف یعنی فجر کا غالب گمان نہ پیدا ہوا ہو۔ چنانچہ اگر کھانے کے بعد اس کے دل میں یہ غالب گمان ہوا میں نے فجر ہونے کے بعد کھایا ہے تو اس پر اس روزہ کی قضا واجب ہوگی۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے نوادر میں یہ روایت ہے کہ اگر وہ شخص ایسی جگہ ہو جہاں فجر طلوع ہونے کا پتہ نہیں چلتا۔ مثلاً پہاڑوں کے درمیان ہو یا رات چاندنی ہو یعنی ایسی رات ہو جس میں صبح صادق تک چاند رہتا ہے اور چاند کی روشنی کی وجہ سے فجر کے طلوع ہونے کا علم نہیں ہوتا یارات کے ابر آلود ہونے کی وجہ سے فجر کا پتہ نہ چلتا یا اس شخص کی نگاہ میں کوئی بیماری ہو جس کی وجہ سے طلوع فجر کو دیکھ نہ پاتا ہو اور اس کو فجر کے طلوع ہونے اور نہ ہونے کا یکساں گمان ہو، تو اس کو کھری نہ کھانی چاہئے اور اگر سحری کھائی تو برا کام کیا۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول ہے دَع ما ير يُبُكَ إِلى مَا لَا یرینگ یعنی مشکوک چیز کو چھوڑ کر غیر مشکوک کو اختیار کر۔ اور اگر اس کو غالب گمان یہ ہوا کہ میں نے طلوع فجر کے بعد سحری کھائی ہے تو اس پر اس دن کے روزہ کی قضاء واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ غالب گمان پر عمل کرنا واجب ہے اور احتیاط بھی اسی میں ہے لیکن ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق اس پر قضا واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ رات کا وجود تو اصلی اور یقینی ہے۔ اور یقینی چیز یقین سے زائل ہو سکتی ہے نہ کہ غیر یقین سے اور غالب گمان ، یقین نہیں ہوتا ۔ لہذا رات کا وجود جو یقینی ہے اس وقت زائل ہوگا ۔ جبکہ طلوع فجر کا یقین ہو جائے ۔ ظن غالب سے زائل نہ ہوگا ۔ پس جب ظن غالب سے رات کا ہونا زائل نہیں ہوا تو اس نے سحری رات میں کھائی ہے نہ کہ فجر طلوع ہونے کے بعد اور جب سحری رات میں کھائی گئی تو اس کا یہ روزہ شرعا معتبر ہوگا۔ اور جب یہ روز و معتبر ہے تو اس کی قضا واجب نہ ہوگی۔
Three things are from the character of the messengers: hastening iftar, delaying suhoor, and miswak. But when he doubts about fajr, meaning both sides are equal, then it is better to leave eating out of caution against the prohibited, and it is not obligatory upon him. And if he ate, his fast is complete because the original state is night. And from Abu Hanifa: if he is in a place where fajr is not distinguishable, or the night is moonlit, or cloudy, or his sight has a defect, and he doubts, he should not eat. If he ate, he has done wrong due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' And if his dominant opinion is that he ate while fajr was rising, then qada is upon him, acting on dominant opinion, and caution is in it. And according to Zahir al-Riwayah, there is no qada upon him because certainty is not removed except by its like. Translation: Then eating suhoor is mustahabb because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Eat suhoor, for in suhoor there is blessing.' And delaying suhoor is mustahabb because the Prophet said: 'Three things are from the character of the messengers: hastening iftar, delaying suhoor, and miswak.' But when he doubts fajr, meaning both sides are equal, then it is better to leave eating out of caution against the prohibited, and it is not obligatory upon him. And if he ate, his fast is complete because the original state is night. And narrated from Abu Hanifa: if that person is in a place where fajr is not apparent, or the night is moonlit, or cloudy, or his sight has a defect, and he doubts about fajr, he should not eat. And if he ate, he committed wrong because the Prophet said: 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' And if his dominant opinion is that he ate suhoor while fajr had risen, then qada is obligatory upon him because acting on dominant opinion is obligatory, and caution is in it. And according to Zahir al-Riwayah, qada is not obligatory upon him because certainty is not removed except by its like. Explanation: 'Sahar' is the name of the end of the night, and some said it is the last sixth of the night. 'Suhoor' is the name of the food eaten at that time. In any case, eating suhoor is a mustahabb command, and the proof is this hadith: 'Take suhoor, for in suhoor there is blessing.' And blessing in the hadith means gaining strength for the next day's fast. The translation is: 'Eat suhoor, for in suhoor there is gaining strength.' This is supported by the hadith: The Prophet said: 'Seek help with the midday nap for standing at night, and with eating suhoor for fasting the day.' That is, seek help by napping and resting during the day to stand at night for prayers, and by eating suhoor to fast during the day. The meaning is: take some rest during the day so that you gain strength to pray at night, and eat suhoor so that you gain strength for the day's fast. Some said that blessing in the hadith means attaining increase in reward, because eating suhoor is the sunnah of the prophets, and it is obvious that acting upon the sunnah of the prophets causes increase in reward. Therefore, the word blessing can also mean increase in reward. The author of Hidayah says that delaying suhoor is mustahabb, and the proof is this hadith: '(Three) are from the character of the messengers: hastening iftar, delaying suhoor, and miswak.' At first glance, there might be an objection to this hadith: that eating suhoor is among the distinguishing features of the people of Islam and the Ummah of the Prophet. So how can delaying suhoor be from the character of the messengers? Also, the Prophet said: 'The difference between our fast and the fast of the People of the Book is the meal of suhoor.' From this hadith, it is also learned that suhoor was not practiced by previous nations. So when previous nations did not have suhoor, how can the Prophet's statement 'Three things are from the character of the messengers' be correct? One answer to this objection is that there is no contradiction between the two hadiths. Because it is possible that the previous prophets ate suhoor but their nations did not. So now the first hadith attributing delaying suhoor to the character of the messengers and making suhoor the distinguishing mark between the people of Islam and the People of the Book both become correct. Another answer is given in Inayah etc., but it is omitted for brevity. The author of Quduri said: Without doubt, eating suhoor is mustahabb, but if doubt about fajr occurs, whether fajr has risen or not, and both sides are equal, then it is better to leave eating and drinking and not use anything that breaks the fast, so that with certainty he avoids a prohibited act. And leaving this eating and drinking is not obligatory upon him. And if despite doubt he ate or drank something, his fast will be complete because the original state is night, so the ruling of this original state remains until its opposite, i.e., a dominant opinion of fajr, arises. Accordingly, if after eating a dominant opinion arises in his heart that he ate after fajr, then qada of that fast is obligatory upon him. From Imam Abu Hanifa in Nawadir, there is a narration: If that person is in a place where the rising of fajr cannot be determined, for example between mountains, or the night is moonlit, i.e., a night in which the moon remains until dawn and due to moonlight the rising of fajr is not known, or due to cloudy night fajr is not known, or that person's sight has a defect due to which he cannot see the rising of fajr, and he has equal doubt about the rising and non-rising of fajr, then he should not eat suhoor, and if he ate suhoor, he committed wrong. Because the Prophet said: 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' And if a dominant opinion arises that he ate suhoor after the rising of fajr, then qada of that day's fast is obligatory upon him because acting on dominant opinion is obligatory, and caution is in it. But according to Zahir al-Riwayah, qada is not obligatory upon him because the existence of night is original and certain. And a certain thing can only be removed by certainty, not by uncertainty. And dominant opinion is not certainty. Therefore, the existence of night, which is certain, will be removed only when the rising of fajr is certain. It will not be removed by dominant opinion. So when the existence of night is not removed by dominant opinion, then he ate suhoor in the night, not after fajr. And since suhoor was eaten at night, this fast is legally valid. And when this fast is valid, its qada is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah on the rules of suhoor (pre-dawn meal) during Ramadan. It begins by stating that eating suhoor is mustahabb (recommended) and delaying it is also mustahabb, supported by hadiths. The primary proof is the Prophet's command, 'Take suhoor, for in suhoor there is blessing,' and the hadith listing three prophetic practices: hastening iftar, delaying suhoor, and using miswak. The commentary addresses an apparent contradiction: suhoor is said to be a distinctive practice of the Muslim ummah, yet also a characteristic of prophets. The resolution is that prophets themselves partook, while their nations did not. The core fiqh issue arises when a person doubts about the arrival of fajr (dawn) while eating suhoor. The general rule: if the probability of fajr having arrived and not arrived is equal (shakk), it is better to stop eating to avoid potential sin, but it is not obligatory to stop. If the person eats, the fast is still valid because the original certainty is that it is still night. However, an exceptional opinion from Imam Abu Hanifa in the Nawadir (rare narrations) applies to specific conditions: where fajr cannot be discerned due to mountains, moonlight, clouds, or defective eyesight. In such cases, the imam ruled that one should not eat at all when in doubt; eating would be sinful. This is based on the hadith, 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' The passage then addresses the situation where, after eating, a person's dominant opinion (ghalib al-ray) is that fajr had already risen. According to one view, qada (make-up fast) is obligatory because acting on dominant opinion is required for caution. But the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) says no qada is required, since certainty (the original night) cannot be overturned by mere conjecture. Thus, the fast remains valid. This is a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the Nawadir narration and the established texts. The teacher should emphasize that the operative ruling (mufta bihi) is the one from Zahir al-Riwayah: no qada is required when doubt was equal and dominant opinion arises later.

Key Terms
السَّحُور (al-suhoor): The meal eaten before dawn during Ramadan, sunnah to eat and delay.
الشَكُّ (al-shakk): Equal probability of two possibilities, here equal doubt whether fajr has risen or not.
ظَنُّ غَالِب (zann ghalib): Dominant opinion; more than 50% probability, here used to determine if qada is required.
ظاهِر الرِّوَايَة (Zahir al-Riwayah): The established and transmitted rulings from Imam Abu Hanifa and his students through the six major works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah), what is the ruling when a person eats suhoor in equal doubt about fajr and later a dominant opinion suggests fajr had risen?
A) The fast is invalid, and qada is obligatory.
B) The fast is valid, but qada is obligatory out of caution.
C) The fast is valid, and no qada is required.
D) The fast is invalid only if the dominant opinion arises immediately after eating.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, certainty of night overrides doubt and dominant opinion; suhoor is mustahabb and the fast remains valid even if later doubt is resolved against it.

Suhur is Mustahabb and the Hadith Evidence
Explains the hadith evidence for suhur and resolves an apparent contradiction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on suhur, identify the hadith evidence, and explain how an apparent contradiction in the hadiths is resolved.

Core Idea
Suhur is mustahabb — recommended, not obligatory — and a distinctive blessing of this Ummah.

The pre-dawn meal (suhur) is a beloved practice in Islam. While many know it is recommended, what exactly is its legal status? This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah not only states the ruling but also demonstrates how Hanafi scholars reconcile seemingly conflicting hadith texts. Understanding this ruling and the method of reconciliation deepens your appreciation of the Hanafi legal tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
Read the passage to find what act is being discussed and what ruling is given for it. The passage ends with a clear statement from Imam al-Quduri.
The ruling is mustahabb.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the hadith cited as evidence for the ruling. It is the hadith that states the difference between our fast and the People of the Book is the meal of suhur.
The Arabic text is given: فَرْقُ مَابَيْنَ صِيَامِنَا وَصَيَامٍ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ  ُأكَلُ السُّحُورِ
3
Understand the Apparent Contradiction
The passage presents an objection: another hadith says suhur is from the character of the messengers, implying it was practiced by previous prophets, but the cited hadith says it is a distinguishing feature of Muslims. Identify why these seem contradictory.
The apparent contradiction is that if previous prophets ate suhur, how can it be distinctive to the Ummah of Muhammad?
4
See How the Contradiction is Resolved
The first answer given is that the prophets themselves ate suhur but their nations did not. Thus both hadiths are true: suhur is from the character of the messengers (they ate it) and it distinguishes Muslims from the People of the Book (their communities did not practice it).
This method of reconciliation (jam') is a key Hanafi usul principle.
5
Confirm the Operative Ruling
Note that the passage concludes with the statement that suhur is mustahabb. This is the mufta bihi position from al-Quduri.
No other school disagrees with this recommendation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الصوم
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
اس حدیث پر بظاہر ایک اشکال ہو سکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ سحری کھانا اہل اسلام اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی امت کی خصوصیات میں سے ہے۔ پس سحری میں تاخیر مرسلین اور انبیاء کی عادات سے کس طرح ہو سکتا ہے نیز خود حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے فَرْقُ مَابَيْنَ صِيَامِنَا وَصَيَامٍ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ  ُأكَلُ السُّحُورِ یعنی ہمارے روزوں اور اہل کتاب کے روزوں کے درمیان با بہ الامتیاز سحری کھانا ہے۔ اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ امم سابقہ میں تھر کھانے کا رواج نہ تھا۔ پس جب سابقہ امتوں میں سحری نہیں تھی تو رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان قلت من أخْلَاقِ المُرْسَلِينَ. الحدیث کیسے درست ہوگا ۔ اس اشکال کا ایک جواب تو یہ ہے کہ دونوں حدیثوں میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے۔ گا۔ کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ انبیاء سابقین سحری کھاتے ہوں اور ان کی امتوں کے لئے سحری نہ ہو۔ پس اب حدیث اول میں تاخیر محور کو اخلاق ا امرسین سے قرار دینا اور اہل اسلام اور اہل کتاب کے درمیان سحری کھانے کو ما بہ الامتیاز قرار دینا دونوں درست ہو جائے گا۔ ایک دوسرا جواب عنایہ وغیرہ میں اور دیا گیا ہے جس کو اختصار کے پیش نظر چھوڑ دیا گیا۔
صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ سحری کھانا تو بلاشبہ مستحب ہے
The Book of Fasting... This hadith apparently has an objection: that eating suhur is a characteristic of the people of Islam and the Ummah of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. So how can delaying suhur be from the habits of the messengers and prophets? Also, the Prophet himself said: 'The difference between our fast and the fast of the People of the Book is the meal of suhur.' From this hadith it is also known that the previous nations did not have the custom of eating suhur. So when the previous nations did not have suhur, how can the saying of the Messenger of Allah 'It is from the character of the messengers' be correct? One answer to this objection is that there is no contradiction between the two hadiths. Because it is possible that the previous prophets ate suhur but their nations did not have suhur. So now, attributing the delay of suhur to the character of the messengers and making suhur the distinguishing feature between Muslims and People of the Book both become correct. A second answer is given in al-Inayah and other works, which has been omitted for brevity. Sahib al-Quduri has said that eating suhur is undoubtedly mustahabb (recommended).
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage from the commentary Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses an apparent contradiction between two hadiths regarding suhur (the pre-dawn meal). The author explains that the objection is that one hadith states that suhur is from the character of the messengers, implying it was practiced by previous prophets, while another hadith indicates that the difference between our fast and the fast of the People of the Book is precisely suhur, implying that previous nations did not have it. The first resolution given is that the prophets themselves ate suhur, but their communities did not, so both hadiths are harmonized. The second resolution is omitted for brevity. The passage then concludes with the ruling that suhur is mustahabb (recommended) according to Imam al-Quduri. This is a clear ruling in the Hanafi school: suhur is not obligatory but is highly recommended. The proof is the hadith cited and the prophetic practice. The discussion helps students understand how seemingly conflicting hadiths can be reconciled without rejecting any.

Key Terms
سحری (suhur): The pre-dawn meal eaten before the fast begins at true dawn (fajr sadiq).
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended act whose performance is praiseworthy but omission is not sinful.
تعارض (ta'arud): An apparent conflict between two textual evidences (here, two hadiths).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on eating suhur (pre-dawn meal) for a fasting person?
A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is mustahabb (recommended).
C) It is makruh (disliked).
D) It is haram (prohibited).

Key Takeaway
Suhur is a recommended (mustahabb) act in the Hanafi school, supported by hadith, and apparent contradictions between hadiths can be resolved through reconciliation without rejecting any text.
