Doubt About Fajr During Suhur: Fast Validity and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the Hanafi rulings when a fasting person doubts whether fajr has begun, including the intra-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of suhur when there is doubt about fajr and distinguish between the Nawadir and Zahir al-Riwayah positions, applying the principle that certainty is not overridden by doubt.

Core Idea
Certainty (night) is not overridden by doubt: suhur consumed in doubt of fajr does not invalidate the fast in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a common concern during Ramadan: what if you are unsure whether fajr has begun while eating suhur? The text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between the well-known transmitted positions (Zahir al-Riwayah) and a rarer narration (Nawadir) from Imam Abu Hanifa. Understanding the ruling helps you avoid unnecessary qada and reinforces a key usul principle: certainty is not lifted by doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and the Default Ruling
First, note the scenario: a person has equal doubt (shakk) about whether fajr has entered while eating suhur. The default ruling from Sahib al-Quduri is that it is better to stop eating, but it is not obligatory, and if he eats, his fast is valid.
The default is based on istishab – the original state of night.
2
Recognize the Condition that Raises a Dispute
The passage then introduces a nuance: if after eating, a person develops a predominant belief (ghalabah al-zann) that he ate after fajr, a narration from Abu Hanifa in the Nawadir requires qada. This creates an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
This shows that not all Hanafi narrations agree on the effect of predominant belief.
3
Analyze the Zahir al-Riwayah Position
The text explicitly states that according to Zahir al-Riwayah, no qada is required. The reasoning: the existence of night is certain (yaqin), and certainty can only be removed by certainty, not by predominant belief. Therefore, the fast remains valid.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position of the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the Nawadir Position and its Basis
The Nawadir narration from Abu Hanifa holds that if a person has predominant belief of eating after fajr, qada is wajib. This is based on acting on predominant belief (al-ghalabah al-zann) as a form of caution, supported by the hadith 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.'
This view is weaker in the school and not the basis for fatwa.
5
Apply the Principle to a Special Case
The passage also discusses a person who cannot ascertain fajr due to mountains, moonlight, clouds, or eye disease. In such cases, both narrations advise caution (avoid eating), but the mufta bihi remains that if he eats, his fast is valid and no qada is needed.
The special case reinforces that the default ruling applies unless there is certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ سحری کھانا تو بلاشبہ مستحب ہے لیکن اگر فجر میں شک ہو گیا کہ فجر طلوع ہوئی یا نہیں اور دونوں جانب برابر ہیں تو افضل یہ ہے کہ کھانا، پینا ترک کر دے اور کوئی مفطر چیز استعمال نہ کرے تاکہ یقین کے ساتھ فعل حرام سے بچ جائے ۔ اور یہ کھانا پینا ترک کرنا اس پر واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر شک کے باوجود اس نے کچھ کھا پی لیا تو اس کا روزہ پورا ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اصل تو رات ہے لہذا اس اصل کا حکم رہے گا۔ تا وقتیکہ اس کے مخالف یعنی فجر کا غالب گمان نہ پیدا ہوا ہو۔ چنانچہ اگر کھانے کے بعد اس کے دل میں یہ غالب گمان ہوا میں نے فجر ہونے کے بعد کھایا ہے تو اس پر اس روزہ کی قضا واجب ہوگی۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے نوادر میں یہ روایت ہے کہ اگر وہ شخص ایسی جگہ ہو جہاں فجر طلوع ہونے کا پتہ نہیں چلتا۔ مثلاً پہاڑوں کے درمیان ہو یا رات چاندنی ہو یعنی ایسی رات ہو جس میں صبح صادق تک چاند رہتا ہے اور چاند کی روشنی کی وجہ سے فجر کے طلوع ہونے کا علم نہیں ہوتا یارات کے ابر آلود ہونے کی وجہ سے فجر کا پتہ نہ چلتا یا اس شخص کی نگاہ میں کوئی بیماری ہو جس کی وجہ سے طلوع فجر کو دیکھ نہ پاتا ہو اور اس کو فجر کے طلوع ہونے اور نہ ہونے کا یکساں گمان ہو، تو اس کو کھری نہ کھانی چاہئے اور اگر سحری کھائی تو برا کام کیا۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول ہے دَع ما ير يُبُكَ إِلى مَا لَا یرینگ یعنی مشکوک چیز کو چھوڑ کر غیر مشکوک کو اختیار کر۔ اور اگر اس کو غالب گمان یہ ہوا کہ میں نے طلوع فجر کے بعد سحری کھائی ہے تو اس پر اس دن کے روزہ کی قضاء واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ غالب گمان پر عمل کرنا واجب ہے اور احتیاط بھی اسی میں ہے لیکن ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق اس پر قضا واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ رات کا وجود تو اصلی اور یقینی ہے۔ اور یقینی چیز یقین سے زائل ہو سکتی ہے نہ کہ غیر یقین سے اور غالب گمان ، یقین نہیں ہوتا ۔ لہذا رات کا وجود جو یقینی ہے اس وقت زائل ہوگا ۔ جبکہ طلوع فجر کا یقین ہو جائے ۔ ظن غالب سے زائل نہ ہوگا ۔ پس جب ظن غالب سے رات کا ہونا زائل نہیں ہوا تو اس نے سحری رات میں کھائی ہے نہ کہ فجر طلوع ہونے کے بعد اور جب سحری رات میں کھائی گئی تو اس کا یہ روزہ شرعا معتبر ہوگا۔ اور جب یہ روز و معتبر ہے تو اس کی قضا واجب نہ ہوگی۔
Sahib al-Quduri said that eating suhur is undoubtedly mustahabb, but if there is doubt about fajr—whether dawn has appeared or not, and both sides are equal—then it is better that he abstain from eating and drinking and not consume any invalidating substance, so that he may definitely avoid a forbidden act. And abstaining from eating and drinking is not obligatory upon him. And if despite the doubt he eats or drinks something, his fast will be complete. Because the original state is night, so the ruling of that original state remains, unless the opposite, i.e., a predominant belief of fajr arises. So, if after eating he has a predominant belief in his heart that he ate after fajr, then qada of that fast is wajib upon him. There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa in the Nawadir that if a person is in a place where the arrival of fajr cannot be known—e.g., among mountains, or on a moonlit night where the moon remains until true dawn and the moonlight prevents knowledge of fajr, or due to cloudiness, or a disease in his eyes, and he has equal doubt about whether fajr has risen—then he should not eat suhur, and if he does eat, he has done a bad deed. Because the Messenger of Allah said: 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' And if he has predominant belief that he ate suhur after dawn, then qada of that day's fast is wajib upon him. Because acting on predominant belief is wajib, and caution is in that. However, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, qada is not wajib upon him because the existence of night is certain. A certain thing can only be removed by certainty, not by uncertainty. Predominant belief is not certainty. Therefore, the existence of night, which is certain, will only be removed when there is certainty of fajr. It will not be removed by predominant belief. Since the night is not removed by predominant belief, he has eaten suhur during the night, not after dawn. And when he ate suhur during the night, his fast is valid. And when the fast is valid, qada is not wajib.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi rulings on suhur when there is doubt about whether the true dawn (fajr sadiq) has appeared. Imam al-Quduri first states the general ruling: if a person is uncertain whether fajr has occurred, it is better to stop eating but not obligatory. If he does eat, his fast remains valid because the original ruling is night (i.e., the day is presumed not to have started). However, the text then introduces an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: if after eating, he develops a predominant belief (ghalabah al-zann) that he ate after fajr, one narration from Imam Abu Hanifa (in the Nawadir) says qada is wajib, while the Zahir al-Riwayah says qada is not wajib. The latter position is based on the principle that certainty (al-yaqin) cannot be overridden by doubt or even predominant belief. The fast is valid because at the time of eating, the original state of night was certain. The Nawadir narration emphasizes acting on predominant belief as a precaution. The passage also discusses the case of a person who cannot ascertain fajr due to external factors like mountains, moonlight, clouds, or eye disease. In that situation, the text advises caution: it is better not to eat, and if he eats, it is considered a bad deed. However, the operative ruling according to Zahir al-Riwayah is that the fast is valid and no qada is required. The mufta bihi (relied upon) position in the Hanafi school is the Zahir al-Riwayah view: no qada is required when there is doubt about fajr, whether there is predominant belief or not, because certainty is not overridden by mere conjecture. The proof is the general principle that the original state (night) remains until proven with certainty.

Key Terms
شک (shakk): Doubt or uncertainty where both possibilities are equal in strength.
غالب گمان (ghalabah al-zann): Predominant belief; a strong probability that outweighs the opposite possibility but falls short of certainty.
اصل (asl): The original state or presumptive ruling (istishab al-hal). Here, the original state is night until fajr is certain.
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmitted positions in the Hanafi school, found in the six works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare or less authenticated narrations from the founding imams, not part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi Zahir al-Riwayah, if a person doubts whether fajr has arrived and eats suhur, what is the ruling on his fast?
A) His fast is invalid and he must make qada.
B) His fast is valid and no qada is required.
C) His fast is valid but he must pay kaffara.
D) His fast is makruh but valid, and qada is recommended.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, certainty is not overridden by doubt or predominant belief: suhur consumed while uncertain about fajr does not invalidate the fast, and no qada is required, based on the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Kaffara Not Required for Unknowing Suhur After Fajr
States that kaffara is not required when suhur is eaten after fajr unknowingly.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when someone eats suhur after fajr unknowingly, and explain why kaffara is not required based on the condition of intentionality (amdan).

Core Idea
Kaffara requires intentional breaking; acting on the original state negates intentionality.

Many people worry that if they accidentally eat after dawn, they must pay expiation. The Hanafi school, however, distinguishes between deliberate and unintentional acts. This passage clarifies that only qada (make-up) is required when a person acts on the presumption that night still remains, because the severe penalty of kaffara is reserved for willful violation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Read the scenario: a person eats suhur, then later learns that dawn had already risen. Determine that the fast was broken, so qada is wajib. But the key question is whether kaffara is also required.
2
Understand the condition for kaffara
Recall that kaffara in Hanafi fiqh is only obligatory for intentional breaking (amdan) of a Ramadhan fast without excuse. Intentionality (علم وعمد) is a strict requirement.
Hanafi position: kaffara is for deliberate violations only.
3
Apply the principle of building on the original state
The person ate thinking it was still night. They relied on the original state (istishab al-hal) that darkness remained. Because of this reliance, their action was not a willful transgression. Therefore, the condition for kaffara (amdan) is not met.
The text says: 'he based his action on the original state, so intentional breaking is not realized.'
4
Distinguish qada from kaffara
Qada is required because the fast was factually broken (eating after dawn). Kaffara is not required because the breaking was not intentional. Conclude: qada wajib, kaffara not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سحری کھانے کے بعد معلوم ہو کہ کھانے سے پہلے صبح صادق طلوع ہو چکی تھی ، کفارہ لازم نہیں وَ لَوْ ظَهَرَ انَّ الْفَجْرَ طَالِعُ لَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ بَنَى الْأمْرَ عَلَى الْأَصْلِ فَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ العَمَدِيَّةُ ترجمہ اور اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ فجر طلوع ہو چکی تھی اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس نے اپنے کام کو اصل پر بنی کیا ہے۔ تو عمد افطار کرنا متحقق نہ ہوا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حرفی کھانے کے بعد ظاہر ہوا کہ سحری کھانے سے پہلے فجر طلوع ہو چکی تھی تو اس پر قضا ، واجب ہوگی ۔ لیکن کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس نے یہ سمجھ کر سحری کھائی ہے کہ ابھی رات باقی ہے۔ پس جب یہ سمجھ کر حری کھائی تو عدا افار کرنا تحقیق نہ ہوا۔ اور جب عمداً افطار کرنا نہیں پایا گیا تو کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کفار وعمد افطار کرنے سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔
If after eating suhur it becomes known that dawn had already risen before eating, then kaffara is not obligatory. Text: 'And if it becomes apparent that dawn had risen, there is no kaffara upon him because he based his action on the original state, so intentional breaking is not realized.' Translation: And if it appeared that dawn had risen, kaffara is not wajib upon him because he based his action on the original state, so intentional breaking did not occur. Explanation: The issue is that if after eating suhur it appears that before eating suhur fajr had risen, then qada is wajib upon him, but kaffara is not wajib because he ate suhur thinking that the night was still remaining. Since he ate with this understanding, intentional breaking was not realized. And when intentional breaking is not found, kaffara is not wajib, because kaffara becomes wajib due to intentional breaking of the fast.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage clarifies a specific scenario: a person eats suhur under the impression that it is still night, but later discovers that the true dawn had already risen before he ate. In this case, the ruling is that he must make up that fast (qada) because he actually ate after dawn, which invalidates the fast. However, he does not have to pay kaffara (expiation). The reason given is that kaffara is only obligatory when there is intentional (amdan) breaking of the fast without any excuse. Since he acted based on the original ruling (that night was still present), his action was not willful violation. The Hanafi school strictly requires 'amdan (intentionality) for kaffara. This aligns with the general principle that kaffara is a severe penalty reserved for deliberate, knowing violation of the fast.

Key Terms
عمد (amdan): Intentionally; deliberate action with knowledge of the ruling.
کفارہ (kaffara): Expiation; a specific penalty for deliberately invalidating a fast without excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Only kaffara is required, no qada.

Key Takeaway

Rulings on Doubting Sunset
Ruling on doubt in sunset for fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on breaking the fast when in doubt about sunset and explain the consequences of qada and kaffara.

Core Idea
Certainty is not overridden by doubt; daytime is the original state, so breaking fast in doubt is impermissible.

When a fasting person is unsure whether the sun has set, the default assumption is that the day continues. This lesson examines the ruling on breaking the fast in such a state of doubt and the obligations of qada and kaffara that may follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is breaking the fast when in doubt about sunset. The ruling is that it is not permissible (haram) because the original state is daytime.
The term 'asl' refers to the original state of certainty.
2
Apply the principle of certainty
Certainty (yaqin) is not removed by doubt (shakk). Since daytime was certain, it remains so until certainty of sunset.
This is a core Hanafi principle: al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk.
3
Determine the consequence of breaking
If one eats in a state of doubt, qada (make-up fast) is obligatory to uphold the original state.
Qada is required regardless of later discovery.
4
Consider predominant belief (zann ghalib)
Even with predominant belief that sunset occurred, qada is still wajib according to one narration (riwayat wahidah), because the original state remains.
Predominant belief does not equal certainty.
5
Evaluate the case of later evidence
If evidence later proves the sun had not set, then kaffara (expiation) is also wajib because the breaking becomes effectively intentional.
The text uses 'yambaghi' (it is fitting) suggesting a reasoned opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غروب آفتاب میں شک ہو تو افطار حلال نہیں
وَ لَوْ شَكَ فِي غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ لَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ الْفِطْرُ لِأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ هُوَ النَّهَارُ وَ لَوْ أَكَلَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ عَمَلًا بِالْأَصْلَ وَ إنْ كَانَ أَكْبَرُ رَ أَبِه أَنَّهُ أَكَلَ قَبْلَ الْغُرُوبِ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاء رِوَايَةَ وَاحِدَةً لأنَّ النَّهَارَ هُوَ الْأَصْلُ وَلَوْ كَانَ شَاكَا فِيهِ وَ تَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهَا لَمْ تَغْرُبُ يَنْبَغِى أَنْ تَجِبَ الْكَفَّارَةَ نَظَرًا إِلَى مَا هُوَ الْأَصْلُ وَهُوَ النَّهَارُ
ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے غروب آفتاب میں شک کیا تو اس کے لئے افطار حلال نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اصل تو دن ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے کھایا تو اصل پر عمل کرتے ہوئے اس پر قضاء واجب ہے۔ اور اگر اس کو غالب گمان یہ ہو کہ اس نے غروب سے پہلے کھا لیا ہے تو اس پر روایت واحدہ قضاء واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ دن ہی اصل ہے۔ اور اگر وہ اس میں شک کرنے والا ہے اور ظاہر ہوا کہ ابھی غروب نہیں ہوا تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ اصل یعنی دن کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے کفارہ واجب ہو۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر روزہ دار کو غروب آفتاب میں شک ہوا یعنی غروب ہونے اور نہ ہونے کی دونوں جانب یکساں ہیں تو اس کو روزہ افطار کرنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اصل تو دن ہی ہے اس لئے کہ دن پہلے سے چلا آرہا ہے ۔ پس دن کا ہونا یقینی ہوا۔ اور یقین ، یقین ہی سے زائل ہو سکتا ہے شک سے زائل نہیں ہوتا۔ پس چونکہ دن کا وجود یقینی ہے اس لئے افطار کرنا بھی حلال نہ ہوگا ۔ اور اس کے باوجود کہ افطار کرنا حلال نہ تھا اگر اس نے کچھ کھا لیا تو اس پر قضاء واجب ہوگی تاکہ اصل پر عمل ہو کیونکہ اصل تو یہی ہے کہ دن موجود ہو ۔ اور اگر اس کو ظن غالب یہ تھا کہ اس نے غروب سے پہلے کھایا ہے تو اس پر باتفاق روایات قضاء واجب ہے کیونکہ دن کا ہونا تو اصل ہے لیکن اس کے ساتھ غالب گمان بھی مل گیا تو یقیناً قضاء واجب ہوگی۔ اور اگر اس کو آفتاب کے غروب ہونے میں شک تھا اور افطار کر لیا اور پھر دلیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ آفتاب غروب نہیں ہوا تھا تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس پر قضاء کے ساتھ کفارہ بھی واجب ہو ۔ کیونکہ اصل بھی یہ ہے کہ دن موجود ہو اور دلیل سے بھی دن کا ہونا یعنی غروب نہ ہونا ثابت ہو گیا گویا اس نے عمد اون میں افطار کیا ہے اور دن میں افطار کرنا قضاء اور کفارہ دونوں کو واجب کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے قضاء کے ساتھ کفارہ بھی واجب کرنا مناسب ہے۔
If there is doubt about the setting of the sun, breaking the fast is not permissible for him because the original state is daytime. If he eats, then qada is upon him, acting on the original state. And if his predominant belief is that he ate before sunset, then qada is upon him according to one narration (riwayat wahidah), because the original state is daytime. And if he is in doubt about it and it becomes clear that the sun had not set, then it is fitting that kaffara becomes wajib, considering the original state, which is daytime. Explanation: The issue is that if a fasting person has doubt about sunset—i.e., both possibilities of setting and not setting are equal—then it is not permissible for him to break his fast because the original state is daytime, since the day has been ongoing. So the existence of daytime is certain. And certainty can only be removed by certainty, not by doubt. Since the existence of daytime is certain, breaking the fast is not permissible. Despite that breaking was not permissible, if he ate something, then qada is wajib upon him to act on the original state, because the original is that daytime exists. And if he had predominant belief that he ate before sunset, then according to all narrations, qada is wajib because daytime is the original, and now predominant belief also aligns, so certainly qada is wajib. And if he was in doubt about the setting of the sun and he broke his fast, and then by evidence it became known that the sun had not set, then it is fitting that along with qada, kaffara also becomes wajib. Because the original is that daytime exists, and by evidence the existence of daytime (i.e., non-setting) is also proven, so it is as if he intentionally broke the fast during the day, and breaking fast during the day makes qada and kaffara both wajib. Therefore, it is appropriate to make kaffara wajib along with qada.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage addresses the rulings when a fasting person is uncertain about whether the sun has set. The principle applied is similar to the dawn case but reversed: the original state is daytime (nahar), which is certain. Therefore, it is not permissible to break the fast based on doubt. If one does break the fast in such a state of doubt, qada is obligatory. The text further discusses scenarios: if the person has predominant belief (ghalabah al-zann) that the sun had set, but later it appears otherwise, then according to one narration (riwayat wahidah), qada is still required. The strongest case is when doubt exists and then evidence shows the sun had not set; then both qada and kaffara are appropriate because the person acted without certainty and evidence confirms he broke the fast during the day intentionally. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that kaffara is required when a fast is deliberately broken during Ramadan without valid excuse. The text uses the term 'yambaghi' (it is fitting) suggesting a reasoned opinion rather than a definitive fatwa. However, the reliance is on the original state principle: daytime certainty is not removed by doubt.

Key Terms
غروب (ghurub): The setting of the sun, which marks the time to break the fast.
روایت واحدہ (riwayat wahidah): A single narration; a transmission that may not be as strong as multiple narrations.
ظن غالب (zann ghalib): Predominant belief; a high probability but not certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is permissible only if one has been fasting for the whole day.
D) It is obligatory to break to avoid harm.

Key Takeaway
The fast may only be broken with certainty of sunset; doubt does not permit breaking, and if broken, qada is obligatory.

Ruling on Eating After Dawn by Mistake (Qada, Not Kaffara)
States ruling that qada is required but not kaffara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for unintentionally eating after dawn and explain why kaffara is not required.

Core Idea
Eating after dawn by mistake requires qada but not kaffara because intentionality is absent.

This passage addresses a common situation in Ramadan: a person eats suhur believing it is still night, but later discovers dawn had already broken. The text clarifies the legal consequences, distinguishing between qada (make-up) and kaffara (expiation) based on the critical factor of intentionality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and potential obligations
Determine what the person did (ate after dawn) and what obligations could arise: qada (make-up) and kaffara (expiation).
2
Understand the key factor: intentionality
Recognize that kaffara requires 'amdiyyah (intentionality). The person ate thinking it was still night, so intentional breaking is not established.
The text uses 'amadiyya to mean deliberate violation with knowledge and memory.
3
Apply the presumption (asl) of night
The person acted on the original state (asl) that night continued until proven otherwise. Since his action was based on this presumption, it is not considered intentional.
This is a foundational usul principle: the original state remains until certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سحری کھانے کے بعد معلوم ہو کہ کھانے سے پہلے صبح صادق طلوع ہو چکی تھی ، کفارہ لازم نہیں وَ لَوْ ظَهَرَ انَّ الْفَجْرَ طَالِعُ لَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ بَنَى الْأمْرَ عَلَى الْأَصْلِ فَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ العَمَدِيَّةُ ترجمہ اور اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ فجر طلوع ہو چکی تھی اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس نے اپنے کام کو اصل پر بنی کیا ہے۔ تو عمد افطار کرنا متحقق نہ ہوا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حرفی کھانے کے بعد ظاہر ہوا کہ سحری کھانے سے پہلے فجر طلوع ہو چکی تھی تو اس پر قضا ، واجب ہوگی ۔ لیکن کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس نے یہ سمجھ کر سحری کھائی ہے کہ ابھی رات باقی ہے۔ پس جب یہ سمجھ کر حری کھائی تو عدا افار کرنا تحقیق نہ ہوا۔ اور جب عمداً افطار کرنا نہیں پایا گیا تو کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کفار وعمد افطار کرنے سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔
After eating suhur, if it becomes known that true dawn had risen before eating, kaffara is not incumbent. And if it becomes apparent that dawn had risen, there is no kaffara upon him because he based his action on the original state, so intentionality is not established. Explanation: The issue is that if after eating it becomes clear that dawn had risen before suhur, qada is wajib upon him. But kaffara will not be wajib because he ate suhur thinking that night still remained. So when he ate with this thought, intentional breaking of the fast is not established. And when intentional breaking is not found, kaffara will not be wajib because kaffara is wajib only upon intentional breaking.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the consequence of unintentionally eating after dawn. The principle is that one who eats under the mistaken belief that it is still night has not intentionally broken the fast. Since kaffara (expiation) is only required for deliberate, intentional nullification of the fast (with the conditions of being aware of the prohibition and remembering the fast), this person is excused from kaffara. However, the fast is invalid because dawn had actually broken, so qada (make-up) is required. The reasoning relies on the legal maxim that certainty (the day) is not removed by doubt; here the person acted on the original assumption (asl) that it was still night, so his action is not 'amd (intentional).

Key Terms
قَضَاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory act later; here, fasting another day as compensation.
كَفَّارَة (kaffara): An expiatory penalty for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast, consisting of freeing a slave, or fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor persons.
عَمَدِيَّة (amdiyyah): Intentionality; the quality of an act done deliberately with knowledge and will.
أَصْل (asl): The original legal state; here, the continuation of night until certainty of dawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person eats suhur thinking it is still night but later learns that dawn had already broken, what is the ruling?
A) No qada and no kaffara
B) Qada required, no kaffara
C) Both qada and kaffara required
D) Only kaffara required

Key Takeaway
Intentionality is key: qada compensates the invalidated fast, but kaffara attaches only to deliberate, voluntary nullification.

beginner
6 min
Ruling on Breaking Fast When Sunset is Uncertain
Explains consequences of breaking fast while uncertain about sunset

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on breaking the fast when sunset is uncertain and apply the principle of istishab to determine the necessity of qada and kaffara.

Core Idea
Uncertainty does not remove certainty; the original state of daytime persists until sunset is confirmed.

In this passage, the author explains the consequences of breaking the fast when one is in doubt or has a dominant opinion that sunset may have occurred. The key legal principle is that the original state (asl) — that it is still daytime — remains binding until proven otherwise. Therefore, any act of breaking the fast under uncertainty triggers at least qada, and if it later becomes certain that the sun had not set, kaffara also becomes wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the passage deals with breaking the fast when sunset is uncertain, not when it is known.
The uncertainty can be equal doubt (shakk) or dominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann).
2
Understand the proof
The proof is the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity): the original state of daytime persists until its opposite is certain. This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).
The maxim 'al-asl baqa' ma kana' (the original state persists) applies.
3
Apply the principle to three scenarios
Work through each scenario in the passage: (1) shakk (equal doubt) — qada, and if later proven sun had not set, kaffara; (2) ghalabat al-zann (dominant opinion) — qada only; (3) confirmed error (sun not set) — qada and kaffara.
For ghalabat al-zann, the text says 'riwayah wahidah' (one narration) qada, implying no kaffara.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غروب آفتاب میں شک ہو تو افطار حلال نہیں وَ لَوْ شَكَ فِي غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ لَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ الْفِطْرُ لِأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ هُوَ النَّهَارُ وَ لَوْ أَكَلَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ عَمَلًا بِالْأَصْلَ وَ إنْ كَانَ أَكْبَرُ رَ أَبِه أَنَّهُ أَكَلَ قَبْلَ الْغُرُوبِ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاء رِوَايَةَ وَاحِدَةً لأنَّ النَّهَارَ هُوَ الْأَصْلُ وَلَوْ كَانَ شَاكَا فِيهِ وَ تَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهَا لَمْ تَغْرُبُ يَنْبَغِى أَنْ تَجِبَ الْكَفَّارَةَ نَظَرًا إِلَى مَا هُوَ الْأَصْلُ وَهُوَ النَّهَارُ ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے غروب آفتاب میں شک کیا تو اس کے لئے افطار حلال نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اصل تو دن ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے کھایا تو اصل پر عمل کرتے ہوئے اس پر قضاء واجب ہے۔ اور اگر اس کو غالب گمان یہ ہو کہ اس نے غروب سے پہلے کھا لیا ہے تو اس پر روایت واحدہ قضاء واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ دن ہی اصل ہے۔ اور اگر وہ اس میں شک کرنے والا ہے اور ظاہر ہوا کہ ابھی غروب نہیں ہوا تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ اصل یعنی دن کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے کفارہ واجب ہو۔
And if he doubts about the setting of the sun, breaking the fast is not permissible for him because the original state is the day. And if he eats, qada is upon him according to the original state. And if he had a dominant opinion that he ate before sunset, qada is upon him according to one narration, because the day is the original state. And if he is in doubt about it and it becomes evident that the sun had not set, it is fitting that kaffara becomes wajib, considering that the original state is the day.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof based on the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity). The original state (asl) is that the day continues until sunset is certain. Therefore, one who breaks the fast while in doubt has violated a certain obligation; qada is required. If later it is proven that the sun had actually not set, then the breaking was intentional (since there was no legitimate excuse), so kaffara is also wajib. The proof is rational: the day's existence is certain; uncertainty does not remove that certainty. The 'dominant opinion' (ghalabat al-zann) scenario also requires qada, emphasizing that even a strong guess does not override the original state.

Key Terms
شَكّ (shakk): Doubt where both possibilities are equally strong regarding whether sunset occurred.
غُلْبَةُ الظَّنّ (ghalabat al-zann): Dominant opinion; a strong probability that something is true but not certain.
أَصْل (asl): The original legal status; here, the continuation of daytime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a fasting person breaks his fast while in doubt about sunset, and later it is proven that the sun had not set, what is the ruling?
A) No penalty because he was uncertain
B) Only qada is required
C) Both qada and kaffara are required
D) Only kaffara is required

Key Takeaway
Breaking the fast while uncertain about sunset always requires qada; if it is later confirmed that the sun had not set, kaffara is also wajib due to the principle that the original state of daytime continues until certainty of sunset.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Kaffara after Forgetful Eating
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kaffara obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on whether kaffara is wajib after forgetful eating followed by intentional eating, and identify the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
A legal shubha from qiyas can prevent kaffara even if the specific hadith is known.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute. A person forgetfully eats during Ramadan, then mistakenly believes this broke the fast, and then intentionally eats. The majority view (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that only qada is required, while a narration from Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn requires kaffara. Understanding the role of shubha and qiyas is key to distinguishing the two positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes a person who first eats forgetfully, then mistakenly believes that act broke the fast, and then intentionally eats. Determine the legal issue: is kaffara obligatory?
2
State the two positions
Zahir al-Riwayah says no kaffara (only qada). A narration from Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn says kaffara is wajib.
The Sahibayn are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Analyze the proof for each position
The first view relies on shubha derived from qiyas (the general principle that violating a rukn invalidates the act). The second view argues that once the person knows the hadith, there is no shubha.
The qiyas is khafi (subtle analogy).
4
Compare with the father-slave girl analogy
The passage analogizes to a father who has intercourse with his son's slave girl. Despite knowing the general prohibition, a shubha in ownership prevents the hadd. Similarly, the shubha from qiyas prevents kaffara.
This illustrates the concept of hukmi shubha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس نے بھول کر کھایا پھر گمان کیا کہ روزہ ٹوٹ چکا پھر جان بوجھ کر کھایا اسپر قضاء ہے کفارہ نہیں وَمَنْ أَكَلَ فِي رَمَضَانَ نَاسِيًّا وَظَنْ أَنَّ ذَلِكَ يُفْطِرُهُ فَأَكَلَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ مُتَعَمِّدًا عَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ دُونَ الْكَفَّارَة لِأَنَّ الإشتباة أستيد إلى الْقِيَاسِ فَتَحَقَّقَ الشَّبْهَةُ وَإِنْ بَلَغَهُ الْحَدِيثُ وَعَلَّمَهُ فَكَذَلِكَ فِي ظَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَةِ وَ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ أَنَّهَا تَجِبُ وَكَذَا عَنْهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ لَا اشْتِبَاهَ فَلَا شُبهة وجهُ الْأَوَّلِ قِيَامُ الشُّبْهَةِ الْحُكميَّةِ بِالنَّظر إِلَى الْقِيَاسِ فَلَا يَنتَفِى بِالْعِلْمِ كَوَطى الْآبِ جَارِيَةَ ابْنِهِ
And one who ate in Ramadan forgetfully and thought that this breaks his fast, then after that he ate intentionally: upon him is qada without kaffara, because the confusion is based on qiyas, so shubha is established. And even if the hadith reached him and he knew it, likewise in Zahir al-Riwayah. And from Abu Hanifah that it (kaffara) is wajib, and likewise from them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because there is no confusion, so no shubha. The first face (reason) is the existence of legal shubha by looking at qiyas, so it is not removed by knowledge, like the father's intercourse with his son's slave girl.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the case of a person who forgetfully eats during Ramadan, then mistakenly believes that forgetful eating invalidates the fast, and then intentionally eats. The primary ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah is that only qada is required, not kaffara. The reasoning is that the mistaken belief (shubha) arises from qiyas (analogical reasoning) because generally missing a rukn invalidates an act. This shubha is a legal excuse that prevents the obligation of kaffara, even if the person knows the prophetic hadith that forgetful eating does not break the fast. A narration from Abu Hanifah and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) holds that kaffara is wajib because once the person knows the hadith, there is no real shubha. However, the dominant position (Zahir al-Riwayah) argues that the shubha is 'hukmiyya' (legal) based on qiyas, and knowledge of the specific hadith does not remove that general analogical doubt. An analogy is drawn: a father who has intercourse with his son's slave girl is not subject to the hadd penalty for zina even if he knows the prohibition, because of a shubha in ownership.

Key Terms
شُبْهَة (shubha): A legal doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of a penalty (hadd or kaffara).
قِيَاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here, the analogy that missing a rukn (like eating) invalidates the act.
ظَاهِرُ الرِّوَايَة (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from Imam Abu Hanifah through his students, especially Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered authoritative in the school.
شُبْهَة حُكميَّة (shubha hukmiyya): A legal doubt arising from a valid source of law (like qiyas) rather than from ignorance of facts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the ruling for a person who forgetfully eats, then intentionally eats thinking the fast is broken, even if he knows the hadith about forgetful eating?
A) Both qada and kaffara
B) Only kaffara
C) Only qada, no kaffara
D) No penalty at all

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that a person who forgetfully eats and then intentionally eats under the shubha that the fast is broken owes only qada, not kaffara, due to the persistence of legal doubt.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Kaffarah After Forgetful Eating with Mistaken Belief
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on kaffarah when a fasting person mistakenly believes forgetful eating invalidates the fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on kaffarah when a fasting person eats forgetfully and then intentionally due to mistaken belief, and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute between Zahir al-Riwayah and Abu Hanifa/Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Legal doubt (shubhah) from qiyas can persist even with knowledge of a contrary hadith, thereby dropping the kaffarah.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hanafi fasting jurisprudence: a person forgetfully eats in Ramadan and mistakenly believes this breaks the fast. He then intentionally eats, assuming his fast is already invalid. The central question is whether he must only make up that day (qada) or also pay expiation (kaffarah). The answer involves a delicate intra-Hanafi dispute between the authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah texts and a narration from the founding imams. Understanding how legal doubt (shubhah) from analogical reasoning (qiyas) interacts with explicit hadith is key to grasping the preferred position.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the default ruling
Identify the exact situation: a fasting person eats forgetfully, then mistakenly believes that breaks the fast, and then intentionally eats. The relied-upon ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah is that only qada is required, not kaffarah.
The key operative principle is that the intentional eating did not occur during a valid fast because the person believed it was already broken.
2
Identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view
Recognize that a narration from Abu Hanifa and the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ: they hold that kaffarah is obligatory if the person knows the hadith that forgetful eating does not break the fast.
This disagreement hinges on whether knowledge of the hadith removes the legal doubt (shubhah).
3
Analyze the proof for the Zahir al-Riwayah position
Understand the reasoning: the forgetful eating creates a confusion (ishtibah) that is attributed to qiyas, because analogically, any eating (even forgetful) seems to break the fast since the essential element (imsak) is lost. This generates a legal doubt (shubhah hukmiyyah) that persists even if the person knows the specific hadith.
The doubt is not factual but legal, rooted in a valid proof.
4
Examine the rebuttal and the analogy with the father and his son's slave-girl
The opposing view argues that once the hadith is known, qiyas is abandoned, so no doubt remains. The Hanafi response uses an analogy: a father who has intercourse with his son's slave-girl does not receive the hadd penalty even if he knows the prohibition, because the doubt of ownership remains. Similarly, the doubt from qiyas is not removed by mere knowledge.
This analogy illustrates that a legal doubt can survive knowledge of a specific ruling.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) and the mufta bihi
If kaffarah is required, the person must fast 60 consecutive days or feed 60 poor people or free a slave. If not, only one day of qada is needed. The Zahir al-Riwayah position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in the Hanafi school.
This has significant practical implications for the fasting person's obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم ۲۶۲
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
جس نے بھول کر کھایا پھر گمان کیا کہ روزہ ٹوٹ چکا پھر جان بوجھ کر کھایا اسپر قضاء ہے کفارہ نہیں
وَمَنْ أَكَلَ فِي رَمَضَانَ نَاسِيًّا وَظَنْ أَنَّ ذَلِكَ يُفْطِرُهُ فَأَكَلَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ مُتَعَمِّدًا عَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ دُونَ الْكَفَّارَة لِأَنَّ الإشتباة أستيد إلى الْقِيَاسِ فَتَحَقَّقَ الشَّبْهَةُ وَإِنْ بَلَغَهُ الْحَدِيثُ وَعَلَّمَهُ فَكَذَلِكَ فِي ظَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَةِ وَ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ أَنَّهَا تَجِبُ وَكَذَا عَنْهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ لَا اشْتِبَاهَ فَلَا شُبهة وجهُ الْأَوَّلِ قِيَامُ الشُّبْهَةِ الْحُكميَّةِ بِالنَّظر إِلَى الْقِيَاسِ فَلَا يَنتَفِى بِالْعِلْمِ كَوَطى الْآبِ جَارِيَةَ ابْنِهِ
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے رمضان میں بھول کر کھایا اور گمان یہ کیا کہ بھول کر کھانا روزہ کو افطار کر دیتا ہے پھر اس کے بعد عمداً کھایا تو اس پر قضاء واجب ہے نہ کہ کفارہ کیونکہ اشتباہ قیاس کی طرف منسوب ہوا ہے اس لئے شبہ متحقق ہو گیا اور اگر اس کو حدیث پہنچی اور اس نے اس کو جان بھی لیا تو ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق یہی حکم ہے۔ اور ابو حنیفہ سے مروی ہے کہ کفارہ واجب ہے اور یہی صاحبین سے مروی ہے کیونکہ کوئی اشتباہ نہیں ہے تو شبہ نہ ہوا۔ اور اول کی وجہ قیاس کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے حکمی شبہ کا وجود ہے لہذا وہ علم سے دور نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے باپ کا اپنے بیٹے کی باندی سے وطی کرنا ۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے رمضان کے دن میں بھول کر کچھ کھا لیا پھر خیال ہوا کہ بھول کر کھانے سے روزہ ٹوٹ جاتا ہے۔ پس یہ سمجھ کر کہ روزہ تو ٹوٹ ہی گیا اس نے عمداً بھی کھا پی لیا تو اس پر فقط قضاء واجب ہے کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ بھول کر کھانے پینے سے روزہ باقی نہ رہنے کا اشتباہ قیاس سے پیدا ہوا ہے کیونکہ قیاس کا مقتضی یہ ہے کہ بھول کر کھانے پینے سے روزہ باقی نہ رہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی روزہ کا رکن یعنی امساک مشکی ہو گیا ہے پس جب یہ اشتباہ قیاس صحیح کی طرف منسوب ہے تو بھول کر کھانے سے روزہ باقی نہ رہنے کا شبہ پیدا ہو گیا۔ اس کے بعد جب اس نے عمداً کھایا تو یہ کھانا گویا روزہ کی حالت میں نہ ہوا۔ اور جب عمداً کھانا روزے کی حالت میں نہ ہوا تو اس پر کفارہ بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کفارہ تو اس وقت واجب ہوتا ہے جبکہ روزے کی حالت میں عمد کھانا پینا یا جماع کرنا پایا جائے۔ اور اگر اس شخص کو حدیث مَنْ نَسِيَ وَهُوَ صَائِمٌ فَأَكَلَ أَوْ شَرِبَ فَلَيْتِمَّ صَوْمَهُ فَإِنَّمَا أَطْعَمَهُ اللهُ وَ سَفَاهُ پہنچ گئی اور اس نے اس حدیث کے مفہوم کوسمجھ بھی لیا کہ نسیانا کھانے پینے سے روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوتا مگر اس کے باوجود نسیا نا کھانے پینے کے بعد اس نے عمداً کھایا پیا تو ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق اس پر بھی کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے البتہ نو اور میں امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ اس صورت میں کفارہ واجب ہوگا اور یہی حکم صاحبین سے مروی ہے امام صاحب کی اس روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب اس کو حدیث معلوم ہے کہ نسیان کی صورت میں روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوتا۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہے کہ حدیث کے مقابلہ میں قیاس متروک ہوتا ہے۔ اور متروک کسی قسم کا شبہ پیدا نہیں کرتا تو اس صورت میں بھی عدم صوم کا شبہ تحقیق نہ ہوگا ۔ اور جب شبہ نہیں پایا گیا تو کفارہ بھی ساقط نہ ہوگا ۔ اور ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق عدم وجوب کفارہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قیاس کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے حکماً شبہ موجود ہے بایں طور کہ چین اپنے رکن کے فوت ہونے سے باقی نہیں رہتی پس اس میں عالم اور جاہل دونوں برابر ہیں ۔ یعنی اس بات کو عالم بھی جانتا ہے کہ شئی رکن فوت ہونے سے باقی نہیں رہتی اور جاہل بھی جانتا ہے اس لئے حدیث من نسى الخ کے جانے سے قیاس متقی نہیں ہوگا۔ جیسے باپ اگر اپنے بیٹے کی باندی کے ساتھ دلی کرے تو باپ پر حد واجب نہ ہوگی خواہ باپ اس کی حرمت سے واقف ہو یا واقف نہ ہو کیونکہ حدیث انسنت و
Book of Fasting. Whoever eats in Ramadan forgetfully and thinks that breaks the fast, then eats intentionally afterwards: upon him is qada without kaffarah, because the confusion is attributed to qiyas, so shubhah is established. And if the hadith reaches him and he knows it, it is the same in Zahir al-Riwayah. And from Abu Hanifa that it (kaffarah) is obligatory, and likewise from them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because there is no confusion, so no shubhah. The basis of the first is the existence of legal shubhah by considering qiyas, so it is not removed by knowledge, like the father's intercourse with his son's slave-girl. Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a fasting person who forgetfully eats, then mistakenly believes his fast is broken, and then intentionally eats. The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that only qada is required, not kaffarah, because the forgetful eating creates a legal doubt (shubhah) based on qiyas: since the rukn of the fast (imsak) is lost, the fast appears invalid. This shubhah persists even if the person knows the hadith that forgetful eating does not break the fast, because the doubt is rooted in a valid legal proof (qiyas). The opposing view, attributed to Abu Hanifa (in a narration) and the Sahibayn, holds that knowledge of the hadith removes the shubhah, so kaffarah is obligatory. The text draws an analogy to a father having intercourse with his son's slave-girl: even if the father knows the prohibition, the shubhah of ownership prevents the hadd penalty. Similarly, here the shubhah from qiyas prevents kaffarah.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): Legal doubt that prevents the application of a fixed penalty (kaffarah). It arises from qiyas in this context.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning. Here, qiyas is used to argue that forgetful eating breaks the fast because the rukn (imsak) is lost.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six core books. In this text, it refers to the position that kaffarah is not required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A fasting person forgetfully eats, then remembers the hadith that forgetful eating does not break the fast, but then intentionally eats. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the ruling?
A) Qada only
B) Kaffarah only
C) Both qada and kaffarah
D) Neither qada nor kaffarah

Key Takeaway
The presence of legal doubt (shubhah) from a valid proof like qiyas can prevent kaffarah even if a contrary hadith is known, because the doubt is not merely personal but juristic.

Kaffarah After Cupping: The Hadith Exception Dispute
Explaining the ruling on kaffarah for intentional eating after cupping with mistaken belief, and the dispute between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding kaffarah after cupping with mistaken belief and identify the conditions under which shubhah drops kaffarah.

Core Idea
Trusting a hadith creates shubhah, dropping kaffarah — but Abu Yusuf requires following the fuqaha.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute about when kaffarah is required after intentional eating during Ramadan following cupping. The key question: does trusting a hadith that cupping breaks the fast create a legal doubt (shubhah) that removes the obligation of kaffarah? Imam Muhammad says yes; Abu Yusuf says no. Understanding this dispute clarifies the role of shubhah and the authority of hadith for laypersons.

Guided Path
1
State the basic scenario and general ruling
Identify the situation: a fasting person gets cupped, mistakenly believes cupping breaks the fast, and then intentionally eats. The general ruling is that both qada and kaffarah are required because his belief lacks a legal proof.
2
Identify the exception based on a fatwa
If a reliable mufti gave a fatwa that cupping invalidates the fast, then only qada is required because the fatwa is a legal proof for that person, creating shubhah.
3
Examine the hadith exception according to Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad extends the same exemption to a person who knows and trusts the hadith 'afṭara al-ḥājimu wal-maḥjūm'. The Prophet's word is no less than a mufti's, so shubhah exists and kaffarah drops.
Muhammad's view becomes the mufta bihi.
4
Understand Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf argues that a layperson cannot independently rely on a hadith; he must follow the fuqaha. If he knows the interpretation (e.g., that the hadith is abrogated), no shubhah exists and kaffarah is due.
Abu Yusuf's position does not create shubhah from the hadith alone.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Imam Muhammad's view: trusting the hadith creates shubhah, so only qada is required. The commentator favors this view.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

And if he gets cupped and thinks that that breaks his fast, then intentionally eats: upon him is qada and kaffarah, because his thought is not attributed to a legal proof unless a mufti gave him a fatwa of invalidation, for the fatwa is a legal proof in his right. And if the hadith reaches him and he relies on it, it is likewise according to Muhammad, because the saying of the Messenger (peace be upon him) is not lower than the saying of a mufti. And from Abu Yusuf is contrary to that, because the layperson must follow the jurists due to the lack of guidance in his right to knowledge of ahādīth, and if he knows its interpretation, kaffarah is obligatory due to the absence of shubhah. And the saying of al-Awza'i does not create shubhah because it contradicts qiyas. (Urdu translation and commentary follow, explaining the ruling and the dispute.)
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage discusses a fasting person who undergoes cupping (hijama) and then mistakenly believes his fast is broken, so he eats intentionally. The general ruling is that both qada and kaffarah are obligatory because his mistaken belief is not based on any legal proof; cupping does not break the fast (it is like phlebotomy, which is not a nullifier). However, if a reliable mufti gave him a fatwa that cupping breaks the fast, or if he knows and trusts the hadith 'afṭara al-ḥājimu wal-maḥjūm' (the cupper and the cupped have broken their fast), then according to Imam Muhammad, kaffarah is not required, because the fatwa or the hadith creates a legal doubt (shubhah). Abu Yusuf disagrees regarding the hadith: he argues that a layperson cannot independently rely on a hadith without the guidance of jurists, and if he knows its interpretation, no shubhah exists. The commentary favors Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
حجامة (hijama): Cupping, a medical procedure of drawing blood from the skin. It does not break the fast in Hanafi fiqh.
فتوى (fatwa): A legal opinion from a qualified mufti. In this context, a fatwa can be a valid legal proof for a layperson.
شبهة (shubhah): Legal doubt; here, it arises from trusting a fatwa or a hadith, and it prevents the obligation of kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A fasting person gets cupped, and then relies on the hadith 'afṭara al-ḥājimu wal-maḥjūm' to think his fast is broken. He then eats intentionally. According to Imam Muhammad, what is the ruling?
A) Qada only
B) Kaffarah only
C) Both qada and kaffarah
D) No penalty

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, shubhah from a legitimate legal source (fatwa or prophetic hadith) can remove the obligation of kaffarah, even if the act does not actually invalidate the fast.

Cupping, Mistaken Belief, and Kaffarah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Shubha
Intra-Hanafi dispute on shubha and kaffarah after cupping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid shubha in the context of kaffarah, and state the positions of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf on whether a common person can rely on a hadith to create shubha.

Core Idea
Kaffarah is dropped only by a doubt rooted in shar'i evidence, not by mere assumption.

In the Hanafi school, the obligation of kaffarah for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast is a severe penalty, but it is waived when there is a valid legal doubt (shubha). This lesson examines a specific scenario: a fasting person undergoes cupping (hijama), then mistakenly believes that this invalidates his fast, and based on that belief, he intentionally eats. Does he owe kaffarah? The answer hinges on whether his false belief was grounded in any shar'i evidence. The passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents this case and an internal Hanafi disagreement between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the probative value of a hadith for a layperson.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act in question is cupping (hijama) while fasting. According to the Hanafi school, cupping does not break the fast (it is analogous to venesection, fasd). The default ruling is that the fast remains valid.
Note that other schools differ (Hanbalis hold cupping breaks the fast).
2
State the problem of mistaken belief
After cupping, the person subjectively thinks his fast is broken (zann without evidence). He then intentionally eats. The question is whether this sequence triggers kaffarah.
Kaffarah is generally required for intentional eating/drinking without excuse.
3
Apply the rule of kaffarah and shubha
Hanafi fiqh: kaffarah is dropped if there is a valid shubha (doubt based on shar'i evidence). Mere subjective assumption (zann) not traceable to a shar'i source does not count.
Thus, if the person's belief had no basis, both qada and kaffarah are obligatory.
4
Examine the two sources of valid shubha
Two scenarios create valid shubha: (a) a reliable faqih gives a fatwa that cupping breaks the fast; (b) the person hears the hadith 'Afṭara al-ḥājimu wa al-mahjūm' and relies on it. In scenario (a), shubha is created and kaffarah is waived (only qada). In scenario (b), there is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
The fatwa itself becomes a shar'i evidence for the layperson.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad holds that the hadith, like a fatwa, creates shubha for the layperson because the Prophet's words are not less authoritative than a mufti's. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that a common person cannot independently interpret hadith; he must follow the fuqaha. Therefore, unless he also knows the correct ta'wil (interpretation), the hadith does not create shubha, and kaffarah is not dropped.
The practical difference: according to Abu Yusuf, kaffarah remains wajib; according to Muhammad, it is dropped.

Source Text

ترجمہ اوراگر پچھنے لگائے اور یہ گمان کیا کہ یہ روزہ کو توڑ دیتا ہے پھر عمداً کھایا تو اس پر قضاء اور کفارہ دونوں واجب ہیں کیونکہ اس کا یہ گمان کسی دلیل شرعی کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہوا مگر جبکہ اس کو کسی فقیہ نے روزہ فاسد ہونے کا فتویٰ دیدیا ہو۔ کیونکہ اس کے حق میں فتویٰ دلیل شرعی ہے اور اگر اس کو حدیث پہنچی پھر اس پر اعتماد کیا تو امام محمد کے نزدیک ایسا ہی ہے اس لئے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول مفتی کے قول سے کمتر نہیں ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف سے اس کے خلاف مروی ہے کیونکہ عوام پر فقہاء کی پیروی واجب ہے اس لئے کہ اس کے حق میں معرفت احادیث کی راہ معدوم ہے اور اگر حدیث کی تاویل کو جان لیا تو کفارہ واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ شبہ منتفی ہے اور اوزاعی کا قول شبہ پیدا نہیں کرتا۔ کیونکہ وہ قیاس کے مخالف ہے۔

ایسی صورت میں اس پر قضاء اور کفارہ دونوں واجب ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ اس کا یہ ظن کہ پچھنا لگوانا مفسد صوم ہے کسی دلیل شرعی کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہے، بلکہ دلیل شرعی تو عدم فساد پر ہے اس لئے کہ حجامت (پچھنا لگوانا) رگوں سے خون نکلنے میں فصد کے مانند ہے اور فصد مفسد صوم نہیں ہے لہذا احجامت بھی مفسد صوم نہ ہوگا۔ بہر حال جب اس کے اس گمان پر کوئی دلیل شرعی موجود نہیں تو فساد صوم کا شبہ بھی پیدا نہ ہوا اور جب شبہ نہیں پیدا ہوا تو کفارہ ساقط نہ ہوگا کیونکہ کفارہ شبہات ہی کے بعد ساقط ہوتا ہے ہاں اگر اس پچھنا لگوانے والے کو روزہ فاسد ہونے کا فتوی کسی ایسے فقیہ نے دیدیا ہو جس کے فتاوی پر لوگ اعتماد کرتے ہیں پھر اس نے عمدا کھا پی لیا تو اس پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ فتوی اس کے حق میں دلیل شرعی ہے لہذا اس فتوی کی وجہ سے پچھنا لگوانے سے اس کا روزہ فاسد ہو گیا۔ اس کے بعد اس نے جب عمدا کھایا پیا تو یہ روزے دار نہ تھا بلکہ بے روزے تھا اور روزہ نہ ہونے کی حالت میں رمضان میں عمدا کھانے پینے سے کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا بلکہ فقط قضا واجب ہوتی ہے اور اگر پچھنا لگوانے والے روزہ دار کو یہ حدیث پہنچی کہ أَفْطَرَ الْحَاجِمُ وَالْمَحْجُوم یعنی پچھنا لگانے والے اور پچھنا لینے والے دونوں کا روزہ افطار ہو گیا اور پھر اس حدیث پر اعتماد بھی کیا تو امام محمد کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی یہی حکم ہے کہ اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان مفتی کے قول سے کم درجہ نہیں ہے حالانکہ مفتی کے قول پر اعتماد کرنے سے کفارہ نہ تھا تو حدیث شریف پر اعتماد سے بدرجہ اولیٰ کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور حضرت امام ابو یوسف ؒ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس صورت میں کفارہ ساقط نہ ہوگا کیونکہ عوام الناس پر فقط فقہاء کی پیروی کرنا واجب ہے اس لئے کہ ان کو احادیث کی معرفت کا حاصل ہونا ناممکن ہے بایں طور کہ کوئی حدیث اپنے ظاہر پر نہ ہو یا منسوخ ہو چکی ہو تو ان باتوں کو ایک عام آدمی کیا سمجھ سکتا ہے۔ پس عام آدمی کے حق میں ایک مفتی کا فتوی دینا تو حجت شرعی ہوگا مگر حدیث اس کے حق میں حجت شرعی نہ ہوگی۔ پس جب عام آدمی کے حق میں حدیث دلیل شرعی نہیں ہے تو پچھنا لگوانا فساد صوم کا بھی شبہ پیدا نہ کرے گا۔ اور جب فساد صوم کا شبہ نہیں رہا تو کفارہ ساقط نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر پچھنا لگوانے والے کو یہ حدیث پہنچی اور اس کو اس حدیث کی تاویل بھی معلوم ہوگئی اور تاویل یہ ہے کہ پچھنا لگوانے والا اور لگانے والے دونوں دوسروں کی غیبت کیا کرتے تھے ایک مرتبہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا گذران دونوں کے پاس سے ہوا تو آپ نے فرمایا أَفْطَرَ الْحَاجِمُ وَالْمَحْجُومُ یعنی غیبت کرنے کی وجہ سے ان دونوں کے روزے کا ثواب ختم ہو گیا۔ راوی یہ سمجھا کہ آپ نے پچھنا لگوانے کی وجہ سے فرمایا ہے پس اس نے اپنی سمجھ کے موافق روایت کر دی اور کہہ دیا کہ پچھنا لگوانے سے روزہ فاسد ہو جاتا ہے دوسری تاویل یہ ہے کہ ایک بار پچھنا لگوانے والا بے ہوش ہو گیا تو پچھنا لگانے والے نے اس کے حلق میں پانی ڈال دیا حالانکہ وہ روزہ سے تھا تو آپ نے فرمایا أَفْطَرَ الْحَاجِمُ الْمَحْجُومَ یعنی پچھنا لگانے والے نے پچھنا لگوانے والے کے حلق میں پانی ڈال کر اس کا روزہ فاسد کر دیا۔ راوی نے سمجھا کہ آپ نے أَفْطَرَ الْحَاجِمُ وَالْمَحْجُومُ فرمایا ہے۔ یعنی حدیث میں اَلْحَاجِمُ فاعل اور الْمَحْجُومُ مفعول ہے۔ راوی نے سمجھا کہ دونوں بطریق عطف فاعل ہیں۔ تیسری تاویل یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث منسوخ ہے۔ بہر حال پچھنا لگوانے والے کو اگر اس حدیث کی تاویل معلوم ہو تو پچھنا لگوانے کے بعد عمداً کھانے سے یقینا کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ حدیث کی تاویل معلوم ہونے کے بعد اس حدیث سے روزہ فاسد ہونے کا شبہ نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب پچھنا لگوانے سے روزہ فاسد ہونے کا شبہ نہ ہوا تو کفارہ بھی ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر کوئی یہ اعتراض کرے کہ علماء کا اختلاف کبھی شبہ پیدا کرتا ہے اور امام اوزاعی کا قول یہی ہے کہ پچھنا لگوانے سے روزہ فاسد ہو جاتا ہے پس اس شبہ کی وجہ سے کفارہ ساقط ہو جانا چاہئے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ امام اوزاعی کا قول شبہ پیدا نہیں کرے گا کیونکہ امام اوزاعی کا قول قیاس کے مخالف ہے اس لئے کہ قیاس تو یہ ہے إِنَّ الْفِطَرَ مِمَّا يَدْخُلُ لَا مِمَّا يَخْرُجُ یعنی جو چیز پیٹ میں اندر داخل ہوتی ہے اس سے افطار ہوتا ہے اور جو چیز باہر نکلتی ہے اس سے روزہ افطار نہیں ہوتا۔ اور پچھنا لگوانے سے خون رگوں سے باہر نکل کر آتا ہے اندر کوئی چیز داخل نہیں ہوتی پس قیاس بھی یہ ہوا کہ حجامت سے روزہ فاسد نہ ہو۔ اور امام اوزاعی فاسد ہونے کے قائل ہیں تو ان کا قول قیاس کے مخالف ہوا۔ اور شبہ جب ہوتا جبکہ ان کا قول قیاس کے موافق ہوتا۔ پس جب امام اوزاعی کے قول سے فساد صوم کا کوئی شبہ پیدا نہیں ہوا تو کفارہ بھی ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ (عنایہ) اس جگہ صاحب ہدایہ کی عبارت میں تناقض معلوم ہوتا ہے اس طور پر کہ پہلے کہا کہ اگر کسی فقیہ نے پچھنا لگوانے سے روزہ فاسد ہونے کا فتویٰ دیدیا اور پھر اس نے عمداً کچھ کھا لیا تو کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ فتوی کی وجہ سے فساد کا شبہ ہو گیا اور پھر کہا کہ امام اوزاعی کا قول شبہ پیدا نہیں کرتا حالانکہ امام اوزاعی خود بہت بڑے فقیہ ہیں۔ جواب فقیہ کے فتوی دینے سے فساد صوم کا شبہ اوزاعی عام آدمی کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے فرمایا گیا اور امام اوزاعی کے قول سے شبہ پیدا نہ ہونا اس آدمی کے لئے ہے جو حدیث أَفْطَرَ الْحَاجِمُ إلخ کی تاویل اور صحیح مراد سے واقف ہے۔
فوائد ہمارے نزدیک پچھنا لگوانا مفسد صوم نہیں ہے اور حنابلہ کے نزدیک مفسد ہے حنابلہ کی دلیل تو یہی حدیث أَفْطَرَ الْحَاجِمُ وَالْمَحْجُومُ ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے أَنَّهُ احْتَجَمَ وَهُوَ صَائِمٌ ۔ دوسری روایت أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ احْتَجَمَ
Because of ownership and ownership's doubt is established, similarly due to forgetful eating, the doubt of breaking the fast exists considering analogy. So when doubt exists, kaffarah will not be obligatory because kaffarah is dropped by doubt. And if one cupped and thought that it breaks his fast, then intentionally ate, both qada and kaffarah are obligatory. Because his mere assumption was not attributable to a shar'i evidence unless a faqih gave him a fatwa that it breaks the fast, because the fatwa is a shar'i evidence in his regard. And if a hadith reached him and he relied on it, then it is the same according to Muhammad because the saying of the Messenger (peace be upon him) is not lower than the saying of a mufti. And from Abu Yusuf, the contrary is narrated because the common person must follow the fuqaha due to inability to know the hadiths in his regard, and if he knows its interpretation, kaffarah becomes obligatory due to absence of doubt. And the saying of al-Awza'i does not create doubt because it opposes analogy. ... [Translation continues for the entire passage]
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses a specific scenario in the Book of Fasting: a person performs cupping (hijama) while fasting, then mistakenly believes that this has invalidated the fast. Based on this erroneous belief, he then intentionally eats or drinks. The question is whether kaffarah (expiation) is obligatory on him. The author begins by stating the general principle: kaffarah is waived when there is a valid legal doubt (shubha). However, the mere subjective assumption (zann) of the person, without any support from a shar'i evidence (dalil shar'i), does not create such a doubt. Therefore, if the person merely assumed cupping breaks the fast based on his own opinion, then after intentionally eating, he must perform both qada (make-up) and kaffarah. The exception is if a reliable faqih gave him a fatwa that cupping breaks the fast. In that case, the fatwa itself becomes a shar'i evidence for him, creating a legitimate doubt (shubha). Because he relied on a fatwa, his subsequent intentional eating was not during a valid fast (since he believed his fast was already broken), so only qada is required, not kaffarah. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the scenario where the person relies on the hadith "Afṭara al-ḥājimu wa al-mahjūm" (The cupper and the one cupped both break their fast). According to Imam Muhammad, the hadith holds the same authority as a fatwa, so relying on it also creates shubha, and kaffarah is waived. According to Abu Yusuf, a common person cannot independently interpret hadith; he must follow the fuqaha. Therefore, the hadith does not create shubha for him unless he also knows its correct interpretation (ta'wil). If he knows the interpretation, then shubha is removed and kaffarah becomes obligatory. The passage also addresses the opinion of Imam al-Awza'i, who held that cupping breaks the fast. The author argues that al-Awza'i's view does not create shubha because it opposes clear qiyas (analogy): the fast is broken by what enters the body, not what exits. Since cupping involves blood exiting, it does not break the fast by qiyas. An objection is raised: the difference of scholars itself creates doubt. The response is that al-Awza'i's opinion, being contrary to qiyas, does not generate a valid shubha. The passage concludes with a note from the commentator resolving an apparent contradiction in the Hidayah text. Finally, a brief comparison with the Hanbali school is given: Hanafis hold cupping does not break the fast, citing the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who cupped while fasting; Hanbalis hold it breaks the fast based on the hadith. This passage demonstrates the nuanced Hanafi methodology of weighing shubha, qiyas, and the authority of fatwa versus hadith for the common person.

Key Terms
حجامة (hijama): Cupping: a traditional practice of drawing blood by applying cups to the skin. In fasting context, it is debated whether it breaks the fast.
شبهة (shubha): Legal doubt that impacts rulings. Here, a valid shubha can drop the obligation of kaffarah.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast without excuse; typically fasting 60 consecutive days.
ظن (zann): Assumption or conjecture that falls short of certainty. In this context, zann without evidence does not create shubha.
فتوى (fatwa): A legal opinion issued by a qualified jurist. In this passage, a fatwa can serve as a shar'i evidence for a common person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a fasting person cups and then relies on the hadith 'Afṭara al-ḥājimu wa al-mahjūm' to believe his fast is broken, and then intentionally eats, what is the ruling on kaffarah?
A) Kaffarah is obligatory according to both Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf.
B) Kaffarah is not obligatory according to both imams.
C) Kaffarah is not obligatory according to Imam Muhammad, but is obligatory according to Imam Abu Yusuf unless he knows the ta'wil.
D) Kaffarah is always obligatory because the hadith is considered abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah is waived only when the mistaken belief is rooted in a shar'i evidence such as a fatwa or a hadith (according to Imam Muhammad); a mere subjective assumption does not suffice.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
6 min
Backbiting and Its Effect on Fasting
Clarifying that backbiting does not break the fast but nullifies its reward

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on backbiting while fasting and apply the distinction between nullifying the fast and nullifying its reward.

Core Idea
Backbiting does not break the fast but wipes out its reward.

A common misconception is that backbiting breaks the fast like eating or drinking. The Hanafi school clarifies that backbiting is a major sin but does not invalidate the physical fast. However, if someone backbites and then intentionally eats, thinking the fast is already broken, they incur both qada and kaffarah. This lesson unpacks the proof and the key concept of ta'wil (interpretation) of the relevant hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is backbiting (ghiba) while fasting. The ruling is that it does not break the fast. The fast remains valid but its reward is lost.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'Three things break the fast...' is cited. The word 'yuftirna' (break) is the key evidence for those who claim backbiting breaks the fast.
3
Understand the ta'wil (interpretation)
The Hanafis interpret 'yuftirna' figuratively to mean 'nullify reward' because physical intake is required for actual invalidity. This interpretation is supported by ijma' (consensus).
4
Apply to a compound scenario
If someone backbites and then intentionally eats (thinking the fast is already broken), both qada and kaffarah are obligatory. The backbiting itself does not break the fast, so the eating is intentional breaking.
5
Note the practical consequence
The hadith does not create a shubha (doubt) that would waive kaffarah. Therefore, the full penalty applies. This reinforces the importance of understanding the figurative interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غیبت کرنے کے بعد عمداً کھایا تو قضا اور کفارہ دونوں لازم ہیں ۔ وَلَوْ أَكَلَ بَعْدَ مَا اعْتَابَ مُتَعَمِّدًا فَعَلَيْهِ القَضَاءً والكفَّارَةُ كيف ما كان لأنَّ الْفَطْرَ يُخَالِفُ القِيَاسَ وَالْحَدِيثُ ماول بالاجماع ترجمہ اور اگر غیبت کرنے کے بعد عمداً اس نے کچھ کھا لیا تو اس پر قضاء اور کفارہ واجب ہیں جس طرح بھی ہو۔ کیونکہ غیبت سے افطار ہونا مخالف قیاس ہے اور حدیث بالا جماع ماول ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے روزہ کی حالت میں غیبت کی اور یہ سمجھ کر کہ غیبت سے روزہ فاسد ہو جاتا ہے عمداً کھا پی لیا تو اس پر قضاء بھی واجب ہے اور کفارہ بھی واجب ہے خواہ اس کو وہ حدیث پہنچی ہو جس میں غیبت کو مفطر کہا گیا ہے خواہ یہ حدیث نہ پہنچی ہو۔ اس حدیث کی تاویل سے واقف ہو یا واقف نہ ہو کسی مفتی نے فساد کا فتوی دیا ہو یا فتویٰ نہ دیا ہو۔ کیونکہ غیبت کی وجہ سے افطار قیاس کے مخالف ہے۔ اور حدیث الْغَيْبَةُ تُفَطِرُ الصَّائِمَ بِالاْجْمَاعِ مؤول ہے یعنی حدیث کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ غیبت کرنے کی وجہ سے روزہ دار کا اجر و ثواب جاتا رہتا ہے پس جب بالاتفاق یہ حدیث مؤول ہے تو اس حدیث کی وجہ سے فساد صوم کا شبہ نہ ہوگا اور جب شبہ نہ ہوا تو کفارہ بھی ساقط نہ ہو گا۔ صاحب کفایہ نے اس حدیث کو ان الفاظ کے ساتھ ذکر کیا ہے ثَلَاثُ يُفَطِرْنَ الصَّيَامَ وَيَنقُضُنَ الوُضُوءَ وَيَهدُّ مِنَ العقل الْغَيْبَةُ وَالنَّمِيمَةَ وَالنَّظُرُ إِلى مَحَاسِن المَرْأَةِ - تین چیزیں روزہ فاسد کر دیتی ہیں اور وضو توڑ دیتی ہیں اور عقل کو تباہ دیتی ہیں۔ (1) غیبت (2) چغل خوری (3) عورت کے محاسن کو دیکھنا مراد یہ ہے کہ ان چیزوں سے روزہ اور وضو کا ثواب زائل ہو جاتا ہے اور عقل کی خوبی جاتی رہتی ہے۔
If he backbites and then intentionally eats, then qada and kaffarah are both obligatory. The Arabic text: 'And if he eats intentionally after backbiting, then upon him is qada and kaffarah, however it may be, because breaking the fast (by backbiting) is contrary to qiyas, and the hadith is interpreted (mu'awwal) by consensus.' Translation: And if after backbiting he intentionally ate something, then qada and kaffarah are obligatory in all cases. Because breaking the fast by backbiting is contrary to analogical reasoning, and the hadith is interpreted by consensus. The explanation of the issue is that if someone backbites while fasting and then, thinking that backbiting breaks the fast, intentionally eats or drinks, then upon him are both qada and kaffarah, whether he received the hadith that mentions backbiting as a mufattir or not, whether he knows the interpretation of that hadith or not, and whether a mufti gave a fatwa of invalidity or not. Because breaking the fast by backbiting is contrary to qiyas, and the hadith 'al-ghibatu tufattiru al-sa'ima' is interpreted by consensus, meaning the hadith means that due to backbiting, the reward and merit of the fasting person are lost. So when this hadith is unanimously interpreted, then no doubt about the invalidity of the fast arises from this hadith, and when there is no doubt, kaffarah is not waived. The author of al-Kifayah mentioned this hadith with these words: 'Three things break the fast, nullify the wudu, and destroy the intellect: backbiting, slander, and looking at the charms of a woman.' These three things break the fast and nullify wudu and destroy the intellect. Meaning: The reward of fasting and wudu is lost, and the excellence of intellect goes away.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding backbiting (ghiba) while fasting. The author begins by stating the ruling: if a person backbites and then intentionally eats, both qada (making up the fast) and kaffarah (expiation) are obligatory. This ruling applies regardless of whether the person knows the hadith about backbiting breaking the fast, or its interpretation, or received a fatwa. The reason given is that breaking the fast by backbiting is contrary to qiyas (analogical reasoning), because qiyas dictates that only physical ingestion breaks the fast. The hadith 'al-ghibatu tufattiru al-sa'ima' (backbiting breaks the fast of the fasting person) is understood by consensus (ijma') as interpreted (mu'awwal), meaning it refers to the loss of reward, not the invalidity of the fast itself. Therefore, this hadith does not create a doubt (shubha) that would waive kaffarah. The author then quotes from Sahib al-Kifayah a version of the hadith listing three things that 'break' the fast, nullify wudu, and destroy the intellect, clarifying that this is figurative for the loss of reward. The commentary follows the order of the text, explaining each element and emphasizing that backbiting is a sin but does not invalidate the fast; however, if one backbites and then intentionally eats, the kaffarah remains obligatory because the fast is already broken by the eating, not the backbiting.

Key Terms
غیبت (ghibah): Backbiting: speaking ill of someone behind their back.
مؤول (mu'awwal): Interpreted; a text whose apparent meaning has been set aside for a non-apparent meaning due to evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a fasting person backbites and then intentionally eats, what is required?
A) Only qada (make-up fast) is required.
B) Only kaffarah (expiation) is required.
C) Both qada and kaffarah are required.
D) Neither qada nor kaffarah because backbiting already broke the fast.

Key Takeaway
Backbiting does not break the fast but nullifies its reward; if one backbites and then intentionally eats, both qada and kaffarah are obligatory.

Ruling on a Sleeping or Insane Woman Subject to Intercourse While Fasting
Intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on qada/kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a sleeping/insane woman who is the object of intercourse while fasting, explain the reasoning distinguishing forgetfulness from sleep/insanity, and compare with the opposing view (Zufar/Shafi'i).

Core Idea
Sleep/insanity is rare, so qada is due; forgetfulness is common, so no qada.

In this passage, the author presents the Hanafi position on a delicate scenario: a woman who is sleeping or insane and intercourse occurs while she is fasting. The ruling requires her to make up the fast (qada) but not to pay expiation (kaffarah). The passage then engages with a dissenting view from Imam Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i, who argue by analogy to a forgetful person. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping Hanafi principles on the intersection of legal responsibility (taklif) and the invalidation of acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: qada is required, kaffarah is not, for the sleeping or insane woman who is the subject of intercourse while fasting.
The act invalidates the fast, but lack of intent waives kaffarah.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold that no qada or kaffarah is required, by analogy (qiyas) to a forgetful person (nasi) who eats or drinks unintentionally.
They argue that the excuse is even stronger due to complete absence of intent.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis distinguish based on frequency: forgetfulness is common ('ghalaba wujud'), so the ruling is lenient; sleep/insanity is rare ('nadir'), so a stricter ruling applies.
The fast is invalidated by the act itself, but kaffarah requires intentional violation (jinaya), which is absent.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi view, the woman must fast one day to make up (qada). Under the opposing view, no make-up is required.
This difference affects the woman's religious obligation.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position (qada required, no kaffarah) is the relied-upon view, following the majority of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
Imam Zufar's opinion is considered weak (marjuh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نائمه، مجنونہ سے جماع کیا حالانکہ وہ روزہ دار تھی اس پر قضا ہے کفارہ نہیں ... استدال فقہاء وإذا جُوَمِعَتِ النَّائِمَةُ وَ المَجْنُونَةُ وَهِيَ صَائِمَةٌ عَلَيْهَا الْقَضَاءُ دُونَ الْكَفَّارَةِ وَقَالَ زُفَرُ وَالشَّافِعِي لَا قَضَاءَ عَلَيْهَا اعْتِبَارًا بِالنَّاسِي وَالْعُذْرُ أَبْلَغُ لِعَدَمِ الْقَصْدِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ النِّسْيَانَ يَغْلِبُ وُجُودُهُ وَهَذَا نَادِرٌ وَلَا تَجِبُ الْكَفَّارَةُ لِانْعِدَامِ الْجِنَايَةِ
If intercourse is had with a sleeping or insane woman while she is fasting, upon her is qada (making up the fast) and not kaffarah. The jurists derive evidence: 'And when a sleeping woman or an insane woman is engaged in intercourse while she is fasting, upon her is qada without kaffarah.' And Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: There is no qada upon her, by analogy with a forgetful person, and the excuse is stronger due to the absence of intent. Our evidence is that forgetfulness is common in occurrence, while this (sleep/insanity) is rare, and kaffarah is not obligatory because the violation (jinaya) is absent.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute regarding a sleeping or insane woman who is the subject of intercourse while she is fasting. The Hanafi position states that such a woman must make up the fast (qada) but does not have to pay expiation (kaffarah). The dissenting opinion, held by Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) and Imam al-Shafi'i, is that she owes neither qada nor kaffarah, drawing an analogy to a forgetful person (nasi) who unintentionally eats or drinks – the forgetful person's fast is not invalidated, and here the excuse of sleep or insanity is even stronger since there is no volition at all. The Hanafi response distinguishes between forgetfulness (which is common) and sleep/insanity (which are rare). The fast is still considered broken because the act occurs, but since the woman had no intention, kaffarah (which requires intent) is waived. However, qada is required because the fast was not validly maintained. The passage ends by stating that kaffarah is not obligatory because the 'jinaya' (violation) is absent, meaning the woman is not culpable for the act. The commentary follows the author's order, first stating the ruling, then the opposing view, then the Hanafi evidence.

Key Terms
نائمه (na'ima): A sleeping woman.
مجنونه (majnuna): An insane woman, who lacks legal responsibility.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or invalidated fast on a later day.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation, a penalty for deliberately invalidating a fast, usually freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people.
جناية (jinaya): A violation or offense, here meaning intentional transgression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a sleeping woman who is the subject of intercourse while she is fasting?
A) She must perform both qada and kaffarah.
B) She must perform qada but not kaffarah.
C) She must perform kaffarah but not qada.
D) She need not perform qada or kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires qada (make-up fast) for a sleeping/insane woman subjected to intercourse, but waives kaffarah due to absence of intent, distinguishing this rare case from common forgetfulness.
