Backbiting Does Not Break the Fast; Ruling on Eating After Backbiting
Ruling with proof on backbiting and eating after it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on backbiting during fasting and apply the principle of ta'wil to resolve apparent conflict between hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Backbiting destroys reward, not the fast; intentional eating after requires both qada and kaffarah.

This passage clarifies a common confusion about backbiting and fasting. It establishes that backbiting does not legally break the fast, but eating afterward due to a mistaken belief that the fast was already broken still obligates makeup and expiation. The author uses usul principles—ta'wil and ijma'—to reconcile the apparent contrary hadith with qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The core ruling: backbiting does not nullify the fast. However, if a fasting person backbites and then intentionally eats, both qada (make-up) and kaffarah (expiation) are wajib.
This applies regardless of whether the person knew the ta'wil of the hadith.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'al-ghibatu tufattiru al-sa'ima' (backbiting breaks the fast) and the general qiyas of fasting nullification. The hadith is ahad and zanni in both transmission and meaning.
The hadith is not directly quoted in the passage but is referenced.
3
Analyze the ta'wil
The Hanafis interpret the hadith metaphorically: 'tufattiru' means 'destroys reward', not 'legally nullifies'. This ta'wil is supported by ijma' (consensus) and because the literal reading contradicts qiyas (since fasting is nullified by entry, not exit).
Ta'wil resolves the apparent conflict, so no shubha (doubt) remains.
4
Apply the ruling to the scenario
Since the ta'wil removes any doubt that backbiting breaks the fast, the person's eating was intentional nullification of a valid fast, thus both qada and kaffarah are obligatory.
Kaffarah is not dropped because there is no valid shubha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ أَكَلَ بَعْدَ مَا اعْتَابَ مُتَعَمِّدًا فَعَلَيْهِ القَضَاءً والكفَّارَةُ كيف ما كان لأنَّ الْفَطْرَ يُخَالِفُ القِيَاسَ وَالْحَدِيثُ ماول بالاجماع ترجمہ اور اگر غیبت کرنے کے بعد عد ا اس نے کچھ ھا لیا تو اس پر قضاء اور کفارہ واجب ہیں جس طرح بھی ہو۔ کیونکہ غیبت سے افطار ہونا مخالف قیاس ہے اور حدیث بالا جماع ماول ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے روزہ کی حالت میں غیبت کی اور یہ سمجھ کر کہ غیبت سے روزہ فاسد ہو جاتا ہے عدا کھا پی لیا تو اس پر قضاء بھی واجب ہے اور کفارہ بھی واجب ہے خواہ اس کو وہ حدیث پہنچی ہو جس میں نیبت کو منطر کہا گیا ہے خواہ یہ حدیث نہ پہنچی ہو۔ اس حدیث کی تاویل سے واقف ہو یا واقف نہ ہو کسی مفتی نے فساد کا فتوی دیا ہو یا فتویٰ نہ دیا ہو۔ کیونکہ غیبت کی وجہ سے افطار قیاس کے مخالف ہے۔ اور حدیث الْغَيْبَةُ تُفَطِرُ الصَّائِمَ بِالا جُمَاعِ مول ہے یعنی حدیث کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ غیبت کرنے کی وجہ سے روزہ دار کا اجر و ثواب جاتا رہتا ہے پس جب بالا تفاق یہ حدیث مؤول ہے تو اس حدیث کی وجہ سے فساد صوم کا شبہ نہ ہوگا اور جب شبہ نہ ہوا تو کفارہ بھی ساقط نہ ہو گا۔
And if he ate after backbiting intentionally, then upon him are both qada and kaffarah, however it may be, because breaking the fast (by backbiting) is contrary to qiyas, and the hadith is interpreted (mu'awwal) by consensus. Translation: And if after backbiting he intentionally ate something, then upon him are qada and kaffarah, in whatever manner. Because breaking the fast due to backbiting is contrary to qiyas, and the above hadith is interpreted by consensus. Explanation: The issue is that if someone backbites while fasting, and thinking that backbiting breaks the fast he intentionally eats or drinks, then upon him are both qada and kaffarah, whether he has heard the hadith that says backbiting breaks the fast or not, whether he knows the interpretation of the hadith or not, whether a mufti gave a fatwa of nullification or not. Because breaking the fast due to backbiting is contrary to qiyas. And the hadith 'al-ghibatu tufattiru al-sa'ima' is interpreted (mu'awwal) by consensus, meaning the hadith intends that the reward of the fasting person is lost due to backbiting. So when by consensus this hadith is interpreted, no doubt about nullification of the fast arises from this hadith, and when there is no doubt, kaffarah is not dropped.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof addressing the effect of backbiting (ghibah) on fasting and the consequence of eating after backbiting. The Hanafi position is clear: backbiting does not invalidate the fast itself, but it destroys the reward. If a fasting person backbites and then intentionally eats, mistakenly believing that backbiting had already broken his fast, he must perform both qada (make up the fast) and kaffarah (expiation). This ruling applies regardless of whether he has heard the hadith that seems to indicate that backbiting breaks the fast, or whether he knows its interpretation. The reason is that the hadith 'al-ghibatu tufattiru al-sa'ima' (backbiting breaks the fast) is interpreted by scholarly consensus (ijma') to mean that it destroys the spiritual reward of the fast, not that it nullifies the fast in a legal sense. Since nullification via backbiting is contrary to qiyas (analogical reasoning) — because fasting is nullified by something entering the body, not exiting — and the hadith is interpreted, no doubt (shubha) arises to drop the kaffarah. Hence both qada and kaffarah are obligatory.

Key Terms
الغیبة (al-ghibah): Speaking about an absent person in a way they would dislike
مؤول (mu'awwal): Interpreted away from its literal meaning due to evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only kaffarah
C) Both qada and kaffarah
D) Nothing, because backbiting had already broken the fast

Key Takeaway
Backbiting does not break the fast legally; but eating afterward intentionally obligates both makeup (qada) and expiation (kaffarah).

Cohabitation with a Sleeping or Insane Fasting Woman: Qada but No Kaffarah
Ruling on cohabitation with sleeping/insane fasting woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cohabitation with a sleeping/insane fasting woman, explain the qiyas argument of Zufar and Shafi'i, and articulate the Hanafi response distinguishing common vs. rare cases.

Core Idea
Sleeping or insane woman cohabited with must make up the fast, but no expiation; rare cases are not exempt from qada.

This passage presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a fasting woman who is cohabited with while asleep or insane. The majority Hanafi position requires her to perform qada (make-up fast) but no kaffarah (expiation). Imam Zufar, along with Imam al-Shafi'i, argues that even qada is not obligatory, drawing an analogy to a person who forgetfully eats while fasting. The Hanafi response hinges on a key distinction: forgetfulness is common, thus qada is waived to avoid hardship; cohabitation in such states is rare, so qada remains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and positions
Determine who holds each view. The majority Hanafi: qada wajib, no kaffarah. Zufar and Shafi'i: no qada.
2
Understand the opponent's qiyas
Analyze the analogical argument: the sleeping/insane woman is compared to a forgetful faster because both lack intention and have an excuse. The ruling for forgetful is no qada, so by qiyas, no qada here.
The opponent argues the excuse is even stronger due to absence of consciousness.
3
Analyze the Hanafi counter-argument
The Hanafi majority distinguishes based on frequency: forgetfulness is common (ghalib al-wujud), so waiving qada avoids hardship; cohabitation in these states is rare (nadir), so no hardship in requiring qada.
The distinction is based on the principle of raf' al-haraj (removal of hardship).
4
Determine the ruling for kaffarah
Kaffarah is not required because there is no transgression (jinayah) from the woman's side; she had no intention to break the fast.
The sin lies on the cohabiting man, not the woman.
5
Address the textual difficulty
Explain how an insane woman can be fasting: either the text originally said 'majburah' (coerced) and was miswritten, or she became insane after starting the fast.
This resolves the apparent contradiction that an insane person is not obligated to fast.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استدال فقہاء وإذا جُوَمِعَتِ الثَّائِمَةُ وَ المَجْنُونَةُ وَهِيَ صَائِمَةٌ عَلَيْهَا الْقَضاءُ دُونَ الْكَفَّارَةَ وَقَالَ زُفْرُ وَالشَّافِعِي لَا فَضَاءَ عَلَيْهَا إعْتِبَارًا بالنَّاسِي وَالْعَذَرُ أبْلَغُ لعدم القصْدِ وَ لَنَا أنَّ النِّسَانَ يَغْلِبُ وُجُودُهُ وَهَذَا نَادِرُ وَلا تَجِبُ الْكَفَّارَةُ لانعدام الجناية
Proof of the jurists: And if a sleeping woman or an insane woman is cohabited with while she is fasting, upon her is qada without kaffarah. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: No qada upon her, by analogy to the one who forgets, and the excuse is stronger due to absence of intention. And our proof: That forgetfulness is frequent in occurrence, and this is rare. And kaffarah is not obligatory due to the absence of transgression.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (with Imam Zufar) and also a cross-madhhab dispute (with al-Shafi'i). The issue: if a woman who is fasting is cohabited with while she is sleeping or insane. According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and the majority), she must perform qada (make up the fast) but no kaffarah (expiation). Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that even qada is not obligatory, analogizing her to a person who forgets and eats or drinks; they argue that her excuse (sleep or insanity) is even more compelling because there is no intention at all. The Hanafi response: Forgetfulness is common, and imposing qada in that case would lead to hardship, so qada is waived. But cohabitation with a sleeping or insane woman is rare, so requiring qada does not create hardship. Kaffarah is not required because there is no transgression (jinayah) from her side—she had no intention. The text also addresses an apparent problem: an insane woman cannot be fasting. Two solutions are offered: (1) the original word might be 'majburah' (coerced woman), and scribes later wrote 'majnunah'; (2) she could have been sane at the beginning of the day, made intention, then became insane, and later regained sanity, validating the fast.

Key Terms
الثائمة (al-na'imah): Sleeping woman
المجنونة (al-majnunah): Insane woman (possibly scribal error for coerced woman)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only kaffarah
B) Only qada
C) Both qada and kaffarah
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
A sleeping or insane fasting woman cohabited with must make up the fast (qada) but owes no expiation (kaffarah).

Validity of a Vow to Fast on Eid al-Adha
Ruling on vowing to fast on the day of Eid al-Adha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on a vow to fast on a prohibited day and distinguish it from the Shafi'i/Zufar position.

Core Idea
A vow to fast on Eid al-Adha is valid in Hanafi fiqh; the prohibition is on the day, not the act.

This passage presents a key dispute over vowing to fast on a day when fasting is prohibited. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the intrinsic permissibility of the act of fasting and the prohibition attached to a specific time. Understanding this distinction is essential for applying the rules of vows correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the opposing positions
Locate the exact act—vowing to fast on the day of Nahr (Eid al-Adha). Note that Abu Hanifa declares the vow valid, while Zufar and al-Shafi'i declare it invalid.
The dispute hinges on whether the prohibition makes the act itself sinful.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
The text states the Hanafi proof: the fast itself is an act of worship (mashru'), so the vow is valid. The prohibition is due to the day, not the act itself.
The key term is 'mashru'—the act has intrinsic legitimacy.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
The opposing school argues that because fasting on Eid is prohibited, the vow is a vow to sin, hence invalid.
This position conflates the prohibition of time with the act itself.
4
Derive the practical ruling (thamarah)
According to Hanafi, the vow is valid, so the person must not fast on Eid (to avoid sin) but must make up the fast later. If he does fast on Eid, the obligation is fulfilled.
The practical difference: Hanafi requires qada; Shafi'i requires nothing.
5
Reflect on the broader implication
This case shows the Hanafi principle of distinguishing between the act (fi'l) and the condition (hāl) when applying prohibitions.
This principle appears in other chapters, e.g., vows to perform acts that are only prohibited due to time or place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصَلَّ فِيْمَا يُوجِبُهُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ وَإِذَا قَالَ لِلَّهِ عَلَى صَوْمُ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ أَفْطَرَ وَقَضَى فَهَذَا النَّذَرُ صَحِيحُ عِنْدَنَا خِلَاقًا . لزُفَرَوَ الشَّافِعِي هُمَا يَقُوْلَانِ إِنَّهُ نَذَرُ بِمَا هُوَ مَعْصِيَّةُ لِوُرُودِ النَّهْي عَنْ صَوْمِ هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ. وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ نَذَرُ بِصَوْمٍ مَشْرُوع وَاللَّهُ لِغَيْرِهِ وَهُوَ تَرَكَ إِجَابَةِ دَعْوَةِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فَيَصِحْ نَذَرُهُ لَكِنَّهُ يُفْطِرُ إحْتَرَازًا عَنِ الْمَعْصِيةِ المُجَاوَرَةِ ثُمَّ يَقْضِى إسْقَاطًا لِلْوَاجِبِ وَإِنْ صَامَ فِيْهِ يَخْرُجُ عَنِ الْعَهْدَةِ لِأَنَّهُ أَدَّاهُ كَمَا الْتَزَمَهُ
Chapter on what he makes obligatory upon himself. And if he said: 'For Allah upon me is fasting on the day of Nahr,' he should break the fast and make it up. This vow is valid according to us, contrary to Zufar and al-Shafi'i. They both say that it is a vow to do an act of disobedience because of the prohibition against fasting on these days. And our proof: It is a vow to fast an act of worship for the sake of something else, and he has left responding to the invitation of Allah Most High, so his vow is valid. But he breaks the fast to avoid the sin of the adjacent (forbidden day), then makes it up to fulfill the obligation. And if he fasts on it, he fulfills his obligation because he performed it as he undertook it.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school (here represented by Abu Hanifa) and Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of a vow (nadhr) to fast on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah, the day of Eid al-Adha). The Hanafi position: The vow is valid. If someone says, 'I vow to fast on the day of Nahr,' he should not fast on that day (because it is prohibited) but instead make up the fast later (qada). However, if he does fast on that day, his fast is valid and fulfills the vow. The opposing view (Zufar/Shafi'i): The vow is invalid because it is a vow to do a prohibited act (since fasting on Eid is forbidden). The Hanafi reasoning: The act of fasting itself is a form of worship (mashru'), but the day is prohibited for fasting due to a command from Allah to celebrate. The prohibition is not inherent in the act but due to the occasion. So the vow is valid because the intended act (fasting) is permissible in other contexts. However, to avoid the sin of fasting on the prohibited day, he must break the fast and make it up later. If he fasts, he still fulfills his vow because he did what he pledged, and the prohibition does not invalidate the act itself for the purpose of fulfilling the nadhr.

Key Terms
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship for Allah
عيد النحر ('Id al-Nahr): The day of Eid al-Adha (10th Dhul Hijjah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, if someone vows to fast on the day of Eid al-Adha, what should he do?
A) Fast on that day and it fulfills the vow
B) Not fast on that day but make it up later
C) The vow is invalid and nothing is required
D) Fast on that day and also make it up later

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a vow to fast on a prohibited day is valid, but the day must be avoided and the vow fulfilled later.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Fasting Woman Asleep or Insane Subjected to Intercourse
Dispute over qada and kaffarah for a sleeping/insane fasting woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a sleeping or insane fasting woman subjected to intercourse, distinguish the basis for qada vs. kaffarah, and evaluate the opposing argument from analogy to forgetfulness.

Core Idea
A fasting woman who is asleep or insane must make up the fast after intercourse, but no expiation is required because intent is absent.

The fast is a sacred act that can be invalidated even without intention. This lesson examines a nuanced case: a woman who is asleep or insane and subjected to intercourse. The Hanafi school distinguishes between qada (restitution) and kaffarah (expiation) based on the presence of intent and the frequency of the occurrence, leading to a disagreement with Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i. By working through this dispute, you will understand how Hanafi jurists apply principles of hardship (haraj) and deliberate offense (jinaya) to derive rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly state what the Hanafi school says about qada and kaffarah for the sleeping or insane woman who is subjected to intercourse.
2
Identify the opposing position and its proof
Identify the ruling of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i, and extract their argument based on qiyas (analogy) to forgetful eating.
The opposing analogy: just as forgetful eating does not break the fast, sleep/insanity - being even greater excuses - should also preserve the fast.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response and its basis
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: they distinguish forgetfulness (frequent) from sleep/insanity intercourse (rare), so the ruling of no qada for forgetfulness is based on avoiding hardship, which does not apply here.
The key distinction is the frequency of occurrence ('umum al-bala' vs. nadir).
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Explain the practical difference: according to Hanafi, the woman must make up the fast; according to the opposing view, no makeup is required.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
State that the Hanafi position (qada wajib, no kaffarah) is the relied-upon view, and note the textual clarification about 'majnunah' meaning 'coerced' or referring to a woman who became insane after intending the fast.

Source Text

کتاب الصوم
۲۶۶
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی روزہ دار سوئی ہوئی عورت یا مجنونہ عورت سے جماع کیا گیا تو ان دونوں عورتوں پر قضا تو واجب ہو گی لیکن کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ اور امام زفر اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ ان پر قضاء بھی واجب نہیں ہے۔ یہاں عبارت میں ذرا سا اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ مجنونہ عورت روزہ دار کس طرح ہو سکتی ہے کیونکہ جنون اور روزہ دونوں جمع نہیں ہو سکتے ۔ اس کے دو جواب ہیں اول تو یہ کہ اصل میں یہ لفظ مجبورۃ تھا اور مجبورة بمعنی مکر بتہ یعنی وہ عورت جس سے بالجبر جماع کیا گیا ہے۔ کاتب نے غلطی سے مجنونہ لکھد یا اور پھر کتاب کے نسخے اطراف عالم میں پھیل گئے تو اس کو کاٹ کر مجبورۃ لکھنا مناسب نہ سمجھا جبکہ اس کی توجیہ بھی ممکن ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ مجنونہ سے وہ عورت مراد ہے جو دن کے اول حصہ میں عاقلہ تھی اس نے روزہ کی نیت کر کے روزہ رکھ لیا پھر وہ مجنونہ ہوگئی اسی اثنا میں اس کے شوہر نے اس سے جماع کر لیا پھر اسی دن میں افاقہ ہو گیا اور اس کو اپنے شوہر کی حرکت بھی معلوم ہوگئی ان جوابات کے بعد اشکال کی کوئی گنجائش نہیں رہے گی۔ بہر حال اصل مسئلہ میں امام زفر اور امام شافعی کی دلیل روزے کی حالت میں بھول کر کھانے والے پر قیاس ہے یعنی جس طرح نسیانا منافی صوم پائے جانے کی وجہ سے روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوتا اسی طرح نوم اور جنون کی حالت میں جماع کرنے سے روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ نوم اور جنون کا عذر نسیان سے بڑھا ہوا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ بھول کر کھانے والا کم از کم کھانے کا ارادہ ت کرتا ہے اور قوم اور جنون کی صورت میں ان کی طرف سے ارادہ بھی نہیں پایا گیا۔ پس جب بھول کر کھانیوالے پر قضاء واجب نہیں ہے تو سوئی ہوئی عورت اور مجنونہ عورت کے ساتھ جماع کرنے سے ان دونوں عورتوں پر بدرجہ اولی قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نائمہ اور مجنونہ کو ناس کے ساتھ لاحق کرنا اس وقت درست ہوتا جبکہ نائمہ اور مجنونہ من کل وجہ ناسی کے معنی میں ہوتیں ۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے کیونکہ نسیان کا وجود غالب ہے یعنی لوگوں کو بکثرت نسیان پیش آتا ہے اور نائمہ اور مجنونہ کے ساتھ جماع کرنا نادر ہے۔ پس چونکہ نسیان کے بکثرت پیش آنے کی وجہ سے قضاء کا حکم مفضی الی الحرج ہو گا اس لئے حرج دور کرنے کے واسطے نسیان کی صورت میں قضاء واجب نہیں کی گئی ہے اور نائمہ اور مجنونہ کے ساتھ چونکہ جماع کرنے کی صورت میں قضا ، واجب کرنے سے حرج واقع نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس صورت میں قضاء واجب کر دی گئی ۔ ہاں البتہ نائمہ اور مجنونہ پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ ان کی طرف سے ارادہ نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے جنایت نہیں پائی گئی اور کفارہ بغیر جنایت کے واجب نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اسن پر کفارہ واجب نہیں کیا گیا۔ واللہ اعلم کی وجہ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Explanation of the ruling: If a fasting man has intercourse with a sleeping woman or an insane woman, then upon both women qada is obligatory but kaffarah is not obligatory. And Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i have said that upon them even qada is not obligatory. Here there is a slight issue in the text: how can an insane woman be fasting because insanity and fasting cannot be combined? Two answers: first, originally the word was 'majbura' meaning coerced woman, i.e., the woman with whom intercourse was done by force; the scribe mistakenly wrote 'majnuna' and then the copies spread so it wasn't corrected. Second answer: 'majnuna' refers to a woman who was sane in the first part of the day and intended the fast, then became insane, during which her husband had intercourse, then she regained consciousness and knew what happened. After these answers, no issue remains. Anyway, in the original issue, the proof of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i is analogy (qiyas) to the one who eats forgetfully while fasting: just as fasting is not invalidated due to forgetfulness being inconsistent with the fast, similarly intercourse in sleep or insanity does not invalidate the fast because sleep and insanity are greater excuses than forgetfulness — the forgetful person at least intends to eat, while in sleep and insanity there is no intention. So when qada is not obligatory on the forgetful eater, it is even less obligatory on the sleeping and insane women. Our proof: comparing the sleeping and insane woman to the forgetful person would be correct if they were in every respect like the forgetful person, but this is not so because forgetfulness occurs frequently while intercourse with a sleeping or insane woman is rare. Since commanding qada in the case of frequent forgetfulness would lead to hardship, qada is not obligated for forgetfulness; but for sleeping/insane women, since obligating qada does not cause hardship, qada is obligated. However, kaffarah is not obligatory on them because there is no offense (jinaya) as there is no intention, and kaffarah is not obligatory without an offense. And Allah knows best. By Jamil Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning a sleeping or insane woman who is fasting and with whom intercourse occurs. The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) is that such a woman must make up that day (qada) but does not owe expiation (kaffarah). Imam Zufar (Hanafi) and Imam Shafi'i hold that even qada is not obligatory. The text first clarifies a textual difficulty: the word 'majnuna' (insane) seems problematic because insanity is incompatible with the intention required for fasting. Two resolutions are offered: (1) the original text likely had 'majbura' (coerced), corrupted by scribes; (2) if the woman started the day sane and intended the fast, then later became insane and intercourse occurred, she could be called 'majnuna' for that part of the day. The opponents' proof is qiyas (analogy) to the case of forgetfully eating while fasting — since forgetfulness does not invalidate the fast, and sleep/insanity are even greater excuses, the fast should remain valid and no qada is needed. The Hanafi response distinguishes: forgetfulness is common, and obligating qada for it would cause widespread hardship, so the law exempts it (lifting qada). But intercourse with a sleeping or insane woman is rare, so applying qada does not cause hardship. Thus the analogy fails. However, kaffarah is not required because the woman had no intention, so no offense (jinaya) occurred. The Hanafi principle is: absence of intent negates jinaya, and kaffarah only attaches to a deliberate offense.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed obligatory fast on another day.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation for deliberately breaking a fast by intercourse, consisting of freeing a slave, fasting two months consecutively, or feeding sixty poor people.
نائمہ (na'imah): A woman who is asleep at the time intercourse occurs.
مجنونہ (majnunah): A woman who is insane; the text clarifies it could mean coerced (majbura) or someone who became insane after intending the fast.
جنایت (jinayah): A deliberate offense; in fasting context, intentionally invalidating the fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a sleeping woman who is subjected to intercourse while she is fasting?
A) Her fast is invalid and she must make it up (qada) and also give kaffarah.
B) Her fast is invalid but she must only make it up (qada), not kaffarah.
C) Her fast remains valid because she did not intend to break it.
D) Her fast is invalid and she must make it up only if she was aware of the intercourse.

Key Takeaway
A sleeping or insane woman subjected to intercourse must make up the fast (qada) but not expiate (kaffarah), distinguishing the ruling from forgetful eating due to the rarity of the situation.

The Hanafi Ruling on Vowing to Fast on Eid al-Adha
Inter-madhhab dispute on validity of nazr for fasting on Eid al-Adha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the validity of a nazr to fast on prohibited days and distinguish between inherent and external prohibition.

Core Idea
A vow to fast on Eid al-Adha is valid because fasting is inherently worshipful, but one must break it to avoid the external sin.

You have probably heard that fasting on Eid is prohibited. But does that mean a vow to do so is invalid? The Hanafi school has a nuanced answer: the vow itself is valid, but you must not actually fast. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this position and the inter-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Abu Hanifa and the Hanafi school rule regarding a nazr to fast on the day of Nahr: the vow is valid, but one must break the fast and make qada.
The position applies to all five prohibited days (Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, three Tashriq).
2
Identify the opponents and their view
Note that Imam Zufar (Hanafi), Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad hold that such a nazr is invalid because the act is prohibited.
Zufar is within the Hanafi school; this is an intra-Hanafi as well as inter-madhhab difference.
3
Examine the opponents' proof
Understand their dalil: explicit hadiths forbidding fasting on these days and the principle 'La nazr fi ma'siyat Allah'.
The hadiths are sahih and directly address the prohibition.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between the essence of the act (mashru) and the external prohibition (manhi 'anhu li-ghayrihi). The fasting itself is worshipful; the prohibition is due to turning away from Allah's invitation.
This is a key usul concept: the prohibition is attached to an attribute, not the act's essence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis require breaking the fast and qada; opponents say no qada needed, and if an oath was intended, kaffarah may apply.
This affects how a mufti advises a person who made such a vow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

كے دن کا روزہ ہے تو افطار کر دے اور قضاء کرے پس یہ نذر ہمارے نزدیک صحیح ہے امام زفر اور امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے یہ دونوں حضرات فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ نذر ایسی چیز کے ساتھ ہے جو معصیت ہے کیونکہ ان ایام کے روزے سے نہیں وارد ہوئی ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ نذر صوم مشروع کی نذر ہے اور نہی غیر کی وجہ سے ہے اور وہ اللہ کی دعوت کے قبول کرنے کو ترک کرنا ہے پس اس کی نذر تو صحیح ہو جائے گی لیکن افطار کر دے اس معصیت سے بچنے کے لئے جو روزے کے متصل ہے۔ پھر قضاء کرے واجب کو ساقط کرنے کے لئے اور اگر اس نے اس دن میں روزہ رکھ لیا تو ذمہ داری سے نکل جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس نے اسی طرح ادا کیا ہے جس طرح اس کو لازم کیا تھا۔ تشریح اب تک ان عبادات کا بیان ہوا جن کو اللہ تعالیٰ نے اپنے بندوں پر واجب کیا ہے مثلاً فرض نماز، زکوۃ ، رمضان کا روزہ وغیرہ۔ اس فصل میں اس کا بیان ہے جس کو بندہ بذات خود اپنے اوپر واجب کرتا ہے۔ بندہ کا کسی چیز کو بذات خود اپنے اوپر واجب کرنا نذر کہلاتا ہے اور نذر کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) منجز ، (۲) معلق منجز جو کسی شرط پر معلق نہ ہو، مثلاً کہا کہ مجھ پر ایک روزہ ہے اور معلق جو کسی شرط پر معلق ہو مثلاً کہا کہ اگر میرا یہ کام ہو گیا تو اللہ کے لئے ایک روزہ رکھوں گا۔ پھر نذر کی دو قسمیں ہیں معین اور غیر معین معین جیسے آئندہ جمعہ کا روزہ رکھوں گا اور غیر معین مثلاً ایک روزہ رکھوں گا۔ نذر کے صحیح ہونے کی چند شرطیں ضروری ہیں: (۱) شی منذور کی جنس سے شریعت میں بھی واجب ہو، چنانچہ بیمار کی عیادت کرنے کی نذر صحیح نہیں کیونکہ شریعت میں اس کی جنس سے کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہے۔ (۲) منذور خود مقصود ہو کسی عبادت کا وسیلہ نہ ہو، چنانچہ وضو اور قرأت قرآن کی نذر کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ دونوں خود مقصود نہیں ہیں بلکہ نماز کا وسیلہ ہیں ۔ (۳) شی منذور ایسی چیز نہ ہو جو اس پر خود واجب ہے خواہ فی الحال یا آئندہ زمانے میں ۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی نے ظہر پڑھنے کی نذر مانی تو یہ نذر صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ ظہر تو خود واجب ہے ۔ (۴) شی منذور بذاتہ معصیت نہ ہو جیسے غیر اللہ کے لئے روزہ رکھنے کی نذر کرنا تو چونکہ یہ خود حرام ہے اس لئے ہرگز جائز نہیں ہے۔ (۵) شی مبذور محال نہ ہو مثلاً جو دن گذرا اس کے روزے کی نذر صحیح نہیں ہے۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے عید الاضحی کے دن روزہ رکھنے کی نذر کی تو اس کو چاہئے کہ اس دن میں روزہ نہ رکھے بلکہ اس کی جگہ قضا کرے۔ حاصل یہ کہ یوم نحر کے روزے کی نذر کرنا ہمارے نزدیک تو صحیح ہے لیکن امام زفر اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک صحیح نہیں ہے اور یہی قول امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ ان دونوں حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لیوم فطر اور یوم نح اور تین ایام تشریق ان پانچ ایام میں روزہ رکھنا شرعاً ممنوع ہے، چنانچہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے أَلاَ لَا تَصُومُوا فِى هَذِهِ الْأَيَّام خبر داران ایام میں روزہ نہ رکھو اور ایک حدیث میں ب أَلاَ لَا تَصُومُوا فِي هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ فَإِنَّهَا أَيَّامُ أَكْلٍ وَ شُرْبٍ وَ بِعَالٍ آگاہ رہو کہ ان ایام خمسہ میں روزہ نہ رکھو کیونکہ یہ ایام کھانے پینے اور زن شوئی کے ہیں۔ بہر حال رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے منع فرمانے کی وجہ سے ان ایام میں روزہ رکھنے کی نذر کرنا ، نذر معصیت ہے اور معصیت کی نذر کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے لَا نَذَرَ فِی مَعْصِيَةِ اللهِ جس کام میں اللہ کی معصیت ہوتی ہو اس کی نذر صحیح نہیں ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ ان ایام میں روزہ رکھنے کی نذر کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یوم نحر کا روزہ اپنی ذات کے اعتبار سے مشروع ہے البتہ منھی عَنْهُ لِغَیرہ ہے یعنی ایک ایسی چیز کی وجہ سے ان دونوں کے اندر روزہ رکھنے سے منع کیا گیا ہے جو اس کی ذات میں داخل نہیں ہے وہ چیز اللہ کی دعوت سے اعراض کرنا ہے یعنی ان دنوں میں اللہ تعالیٰ اپنے بندوں کی ضیافت فرماتے ہیں اب اگر کوئی شخص ان دنوں میں روزہ رکھے گا تو گویا اس نے دعوت خداوندی سے اعراض کیا اور اللہ کی دعوت سے اعراض کرنا بہت بری بات ہے۔ بہر حال ان پانچ ایام میں روزہ رکھنا اپنی ذات کے اعتبار سے مشروع ہے اگر چہ وصف کے اعتبار سے معصیت اور غیر مشروع ہے لیکن اس کے باوجود کہ نذر صحیح ہے اس دن روزہ نہ رکھے تا کہ اس معصیت اور برائی سے بچ جائے جو اللہ کی دعوت سے اعراض کرنے کی وجہ سے روزہ کے ساتھ متصل ہو گئی ہے۔ ہاں نذر کی وجہ سے جو روزہ واجب ہوا ہے اس کو ادا کرنے کے لئے قضاء واجب ہے اور اگر ممنوع ہونے کے باوجود یوم نحر میں روزہ رکھ لیا تو نذر پوری ہو جائے گی کیونکہ جس طرح کے روزے کا التزام کیا تھا اس طرح کا روزہ اس نے ادا کر لیا یعنی یوم نحر میں روزہ رکھنے کی نذر کی وجہ سے جو روزہ اس پر واجب ہوا ہے وہ ناقص ہے اور ناقص ہی اس نے ادا کیا ہے پس جیسا واجب ہوا تھا ویسا ہی ادا کر لیا اس لئے نذر پوری ہوگی۔
The fast of the day is such that he should break it and make qada. So this vow (nazr) according to us is valid. Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i have a disagreement. These two honourable persons say that this vow is attached to something that is disobedience (ma'siyah), because fasting on these days is not prescribed (not entered). And our proof is that this vow is a vow of prescribed fasting, and the prohibition is due to something external, and that is abandoning accepting Allah's invitation. Therefore his vow will be valid, but he should break it to avoid the sin that is attached to the fast. Then he should make qada to fulfill the obligatory [vow]. And if he fasted on that day, he will be discharged of responsibility, because he performed it in the same way as it was obligated upon him. Explanation: So far the discussion has been about those acts of worship that Allah Almighty has made obligatory upon His servants, such as fard prayer, zakat, Ramadan fast, etc. In this chapter, the discussion is about that which a servant makes obligatory upon himself by himself. A servant making something obligatory upon himself by himself is called nazr. And nazr has two types: (1) Munajjaz (absolute), (2) Mu'allaq (conditional). Munajjaz is not conditional upon any condition, for example he said: 'Upon me is a fast.' Mu'allaq is conditional upon a condition, for example he said: 'If this work of mine is accomplished, then I will fast for Allah.' Then nazr has two types: mu'ayyan (specific) and ghayr mu'ayyan (non-specific). Specific like: 'I will fast on the coming Friday.' Non-specific like: 'I will fast one fast.' There are several conditions for the validity of a nazr: (1) The genus of the vowed thing must be obligatory in the Shari'ah as well. Thus vowing to visit a sick person is not valid because nothing of its genus is obligatory in the Shari'ah. (2) The vowed thing itself must be intended, not a means to another worship. Thus vowing to perform wudu or recite Qur'an is not valid because both are not intended in themselves but are means to prayer. (3) The vowed thing must not be something already obligatory upon him, either immediately or in the future. Thus if someone made a vow to pray Zuhr, this vow is not valid because Zuhr is itself obligatory. (4) The vowed thing must not be inherently disobedience, like vowing to fast for other than Allah; since this is itself haram, it is absolutely not permissible. (5) The vowed thing must not be impossible, for example vowing to fast a day that has passed is not valid. The ruling of the case is: If someone vowed to fast on the day of Eid al-Adha, then he should not fast on that day but instead make qada in its place. The conclusion is that making a vow to fast on the day of Nahr according to us is valid, but according to Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i it is not valid, and this is also the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. The proof of these two honourable persons (Zufar and Shafi'i) is that fasting on the day of Fitr, the day of Nahr, and the three days of Tashriq — these five days — is legally prohibited. Accordingly, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Beware, do not fast on these days.' And in another hadith: 'Beware, do not fast on these days, for they are days of eating, drinking, and conjugal relations.' In any case, due to the prohibition of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), vowing to fast on these days is a vow of disobedience, and a vow in disobedience is not valid because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no vow in disobedience to Allah.' Thus it is established that making a vow to fast on these days is not valid. And our proof is that the fast of the day of Nahr is prescribed (mashru') in its essence, but it is prohibited for something else (manhi 'anhu li-ghayrihi), meaning that fasting on these days is prohibited due to a thing that is not internal to its essence; that thing is turning away from Allah's invitation. That is, on these days Allah Almighty hosts His servants. Now if a person fasts on these days, it is as if he turned away from the Divine invitation, and turning away from Allah's invitation is a very bad thing. Nevertheless, fasting on these five days is prescribed in its essence, although in terms of the attribute (of turning away) it is disobedience and non-prescribed. But despite this, because the vow is valid, he should not fast on that day so that he avoids the sin and evil that is attached to the fast due to turning away from Allah's invitation. Yes, due to the vow, qada is obligatory to fulfill the fast that became obligatory. And if, despite the prohibition, he fasted on the day of Nahr, then the vow will be fulfilled because he performed the same kind of fast that he obligated himself to do, i.e., due to the vow to fast on the day of Nahr, the fast that became obligatory upon him is deficient (naqis), and he performed it deficiently. So just as it was obligated, so he performed it; therefore the vow will be fulfilled.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of a nazr (vow) to fast on the day of Nahr (Eid al-Adha) and by extension the other prohibited days (Eid al-Fitr and the three days of Tashriq). The Hanafi position, attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, is that such a nazr is valid (sahih). However, the person is instructed not to actually fast on that day because of an external prohibition: fasting on these days entails turning away from Allah's invitation to eat and celebrate. Instead, he must break the fast if he starts it and make qada (a makeup fast) later. If he does fast, the nazr is fulfilled but he commits a sin. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi) and Imam Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that such a nazr is invalid because the act itself is prohibited; thus vowing to do it is a vow of disobedience, which is null. The text presents the proof of the opposing school: explicit hadiths prohibiting fasting on those days and the principle 'no vow in disobedience.' The Hanafi response distinguishes between the essence of the act (which is legitimate—fasting is a worship) and the external factor that causes prohibition (turning away from Allah's invitation). Since the prohibition is not inherent in the act itself, the vow is valid, but one must avoid the sin by breaking the fast. The commentary then defines nazr, its types (munajjaz/mu'allaq, mu'ayyan/ghayr mu'ayyan), and conditions for validity, which serves as background. The core of the lesson is the application of the principle 'manhi 'anhu li-ghayrihi' (prohibited due to an external factor) in the context of vows, demonstrating the Hanafi method of reconciling opposing proofs.

Key Terms
نذر (nazr): A vow to perform an act of worship that is not originally obligatory, making it obligatory upon oneself.
منهي عنه لغيره (manhi 'anhu li-ghayrihi): An act that is prohibited not in itself but due to an external factor that makes it undesirable or sinful.
معصيت (ma'siyah): An act of disobedience to Allah; sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a person do if he vows to fast on the day of Eid al-Adha?
A) He must fast on that day to fulfill the vow.
B) He should break the fast and make it up later (qada).
C) The vow is invalid, so he does nothing.
D) He should fast and also pay kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a vow to fast on prohibited days, but requires breaking the fast and making qada to avoid the sin of turning away from Allah's invitation.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
7 min
Distinguishing Nazr from Yamin in Ambiguous Expressions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ambiguous nazr/yamin expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on ambiguous vow/oath expressions and identify the practical consequences of the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When both a vow and an oath are intended, Hanafi majority treats them as both valid simultaneously, not mutually exclusive.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when someone utters an ambiguous expression like 'Upon me is to fast on Friday' without clear wording, does it count as a nazr (vow), a yamin (oath), or both? The ruling hinges on the speaker's intention. The text presents six scenarios and a disagreement between the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf, rooted in linguistic principles of haqiqah and majaz.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance and the six scenarios
The text first lists six scenarios based on what the speaker intends: no intention, only nazr, nazr and not yamin, only yamin, yamin and not nazr, or both. Note the ruling for each scenario.
This step is about cataloguing the factual rulings before diving into the dispute.
2
State the disagreement
Contrast the positions: for the case where the speaker intends both nazr and yamin, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule it is both, while Abu Yusuf rules it is only yamin. Also note the difference when the speaker intends only yamin.
The disagreement centers on whether a single utterance can carry two legal categories simultaneously.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's linguistic reasoning
Understand Abu Yusuf's argument: in ambiguous expressions, nazr is the literal meaning (haqiqah) and yamin is figurative (majaz). Since haqiqah does not require intention and majaz does, when both are intended, the haqiqah (nazr) prevails. The utterance cannot be both at once.
This step requires familiarity with usul al-fiqh concepts of haqiqah and majaz.
4
Analyze the response of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
The majority argues there is no contradiction because nazr demands obligation for its own sake (li-dhatihi) and yamin demands obligation for something else (li-ghayrihi). Both aspects can coexist, analogous to combining gift and compensation in a conditional gift.
The key is that the two obligations are not mutually exclusive; they arise from different legal perspectives.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: if the utterance is breached, the majority requires both qada and kaffarah yamin, while Abu Yusuf would require only qada (if only nazr intended) or only kaffarah (if only yamin). The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
This step applies the dispute to real-life consequences.

Source Text

اگر قسم کی نیت تو کفارہ یمین لازم ہے
وَإِنْ نَوَى يَمِينًا فَعَلَيْهِ كَفَّارَةُ يَمِين يَعْنِي إِذَا أَفْطَرَ وَهَذِهِ الْمَسْأَلَةُ عَلَى وُجُوهِ سِتَّةٍ إِنْ لَمْ يَبُ نِيَّةً أَوْ نَوَى النَّذْرَ لَا غَيْرَ أَوْ نَوَى النَّذْرَ وَأَنْ لَا يَكُونَ يَمِينًا يَكُونُ نَذْرًا لِأَنَّهُ نَذْرٌ بِصِيغَتِهِ كَيْفَ وَقَدْ قَرَّرَهُ بِعَزِيمَةٍ وَإِنْ نَوَى الْيَمِينَ وَنَوَى أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ نَذْرًا يَكُونُ يَمِينًا لِأَنَّ الْيَمِينَ مُحْتَمَلُ كَلَامِهِ وَقَدْ عَيَّنَهُ وَنَفَى غَيْرَهُ وَإِنْ نَوَاهُمَا يَكُونُ نَذْرًا وَيَمِينًا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ وَعِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ يَكُونُ يَمِينًا وَلَوْ نَوَى الْيَمِينَ فَكَذَلِكَ عِنْدَهُمَا وَعِنْدَهُ يَكُونُ يَمِينًا لِأَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّ النَّذْرَ فِيهِ حَقِيقَةٌ وَالْيَمِينَ مَجَازٌ حَتَّى لَا يَتَوَقَّفُ الْأَوَّلُ عَلَى النِّيَّةِ وَيَتَوَقَّفُ الثَّانِي فَلَا يَنْتَظِمُهَا ثُمَّ الْمَجَازُ يَتَعَيَّنُ بِنِيَّةٍ وَعِنْدَهُمَا تُرَجَّحُ الْحَقِيقَةُ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ لَا مُنَافَاةَ بَيْنَ الْجِهَتَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُمَا يَقْتَضِيَانِ الْوُجُوبَ إِلَّا أَنَّ النَّذْرَ يَقْتَضِيهِ لِعَيْنِهِ وَالْيَمِينَ لِغَيْرِهِ فَجَمَعْنَا بَيْنَهُمَا عَمَلًا بِالدَّلِيلَيْنِ كَمَا جَمَعْنَا بَيْنَ جِهَتَيِ التَّبَرُّعِ وَالْمُعَاوَضَةِ فِي الْهَبَةِ بِشَرْطِ الْعِوَضِ
ترجمہ اور اگر قسم کی نیت کی ہو تو اس پر کفارہ یمین واجب ہے یعنی جب اس نے افطار کیا اور اس مسئلہ کی چھ صورتیں ہیں۔ اگر اس نے کچھ نیت نہ کی ہو یا فقط نذر کی نیت کی یا نذر کی نیت کی اور یہ نیت کی کہ یہ یمین نہ ہو تو اس کا یہ کلام نذر ہو گا۔ کیونکہ یہ کلام اپنے صیغہ کے اعتبار سے نذر ہے اور نذر کیسے نہ ہو حالانکہ اس نے اپنی نیت سے اس کو ثابت کر دیا ہے۔ اور اگر قسم کی نیت کی اور یہ نیت کی کہ نذر نہ ہوتو یہ کلام یمین ہوگا کیونکہ یمین اس کے کلام کا مشتمل ہے اور حال یہ کہ اس نے اس کو متعین کر لیا ہے اور اس کے علاوہ کی نفی کر دی ہے اور اگر دونوں کی نیت کی ہے تو یہ کلام طرفین کے نزدیک نذر اور یمین دونوں ہوگا اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک فقط یمین ہوگا اور اگر اس نے یمین کی نیت کی تو طرفین کے نزدیک نذر اور یمین دونوں ہوگا۔ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یمین ہوگا۔ ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کلام میں نذر حقیقت ہے اور یمین مجاز ہے حتی کہ نذر ہونا نیت پر موقوف نہیں ہے اور یمین ہونا نیت پر موقوف ہے پس یہ کلام دونوں کو شامل نہ ہوگا پھر مجاز تو نیت سے متعین ہو جاتا ہے اور ان دونوں کی نیت کے وقت حقیقت کو ترجیح ہوگی۔ اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دونوں جہتوں کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں ہے کیونکہ دونوں جہتیں وجوب کا تقاضا کرتی ہیں مگر نذر وجوب کا تقاضا لذاتہ کرتی ہے اور یمین لغیرہ تو ہم نے دونوں دلیلوں عمل کرتے ہوئے دونوں کو جمع کر دیا ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے بہ بشرط العوض میں جہت تبرع اور جہت معاوضہ دونوں کو جمع کر دیا ہے۔ تشریح نذر اور یمین میں فرق یہ ہے کہ نذر میں فقط قضا واجب ہوتی ہے اور یمین میں قضاء اور کفارہ یمین دونوں واجب ہوتے ہیں مثلاً اگر کسی نے ایک متعین روزہ رکھنے کی نذر کی اور اس متعین دن میں روزہ رکھ نہ سکا تو اس کی قضا واجب ہوگی اور اگر قسم کھائی کہ جمعہ کے دن کا روزہ رکھوں گا اور نہیں رکھ سکا تو قضاء بھی واجب ہوگی اور کفارہ یمین بھی ہوگا۔
And if he intended an oath (yamin), then upon him is the kaffarah of an oath. Meaning when he breaks the fast. And this issue has six forms: If he did not intend anything, or he intended only the vow (nazr), or he intended the vow and that it not be an oath, then it is a nazr because it is a nazr by its wording, how could it not be when he has confirmed it by determination? And if he intended the oath and intended that it not be a nazr, then it is an oath because the oath is possible from his speech, and he has specified it and negated what is other than it. And if he intended both, then according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad it is both a nazr and an oath, while according to Abu Yusuf it is only an oath. And if he intended the oath, then similarly according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) it is both, and according to him (Abu Yusuf) it is an oath. Abu Yusuf's argument is that in this speech, nazr is the literal meaning (haqiqah) and yamin is figurative (majaz), so that the former does not depend on intention and the latter depends on intention; therefore it cannot encompass both. Then the figurative becomes specified by intention, and when they intend both, the literal (nazr) takes precedence. And the argument of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that there is no contradiction between the two aspects, because both demand obligation (wujub), except that nazr demands it for itself (li-aynihi) and yamin demands it for something else (li-ghayrihi). So we combine both, acting on both proofs, just as we combined the aspects of gift (tabarru') and compensation (mu'awada) in a gift conditional on compensation. Translation: And if he intended an oath, then upon him is the kaffarah of an oath, i.e., when he breaks the fast. And this issue has six forms: If he intended nothing, or only intended the vow, or intended the vow and that it not be an oath, then his statement is a nazr because this statement is a nazr by its wording, and how could it not be when he has confirmed it by his intention? And if he intended the oath and intended that it not be a nazr, then this statement is an oath because the oath is contained in his speech, and he has specified it and negated what is other than it. And if he intended both, then this statement according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is both a nazr and an oath, and according to Abu Yusuf it is only an oath. And if he intended the oath, then similarly according to the two it is both, and according to him it is an oath. Abu Yusuf's argument is that in this speech, nazr is haqiqah and yamin is majaz, such that the first does not depend on intention and the second depends on intention; therefore it cannot include both. Then the majaz is specified by intention, and when they intend both, the haqiqah (nazr) takes precedence. And the argument of the two is that there is no contradiction between the two aspects because both demand obligation, except that nazr demands it for its own sake and yamin for something else. So we combine them, acting on both proofs, just as we combined the aspects of gift and compensation in a gift conditional on compensation. Explanation: The difference between nazr and yamin is that in nazr only qada is obligatory, while in yamin both qada and kaffarah yamin are obligatory. For example, if someone vowed to fast a specific fast and could not fast on that specific day, then qada is obligatory. And if he swore an oath saying 'I will fast on Friday' and could not fast, then both qada and kaffarah yamin are obligatory.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of an ambiguous utterance that could be either a nazr (vow) or a yamin (oath). The scenario involves someone uttering a phrase like 'Upon me is a fast on Friday' without clear wording indicating whether it is a vow or an oath. The ruling depends on intention. The text presents six scenarios: if the person intends nothing, only nazr, or nazr and not yamin, it is nazr. If he intends yamin and not nazr, it is yamin. If he intends both, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is both (nazr and yamin), while Abu Yusuf says it is only yamin. Similarly, if he intends yamin alone, the two say it is both, Abu Yusuf says yamin only. Abu Yusuf's reasoning is based on the linguistic principle that nazr is the literal meaning (haqiqah) of such phrases, while yamin is figurative (majaz). Haqiqah does not require intention, but majaz does. Therefore, the utterance cannot simultaneously be both; intention can only specify one (majaz). When both intentions are present, the haqiqah (nazr) wins out. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue there is no contradiction because both nazr and yamin demand obligation (wujub), but from different angles: nazr demands obligation for itself, yamin demands it for something else (e.g., fulfillment of an oath). Thus, both can apply simultaneously, analogously to a gift conditional on compensation, which combines generosity and exchange. The practical consequence: if the vow/oath is broken, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, both qada (makeup fast) and kaffarah yamin (expiation for oath) are required. According to Abu Yusuf, only kaffarah yamin applies if yamin is intended; if only nazr is intended, only qada applies. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, which gives effect to both intentions.

Key Terms
نذر (nazr): A vow to perform an act of worship; its breach requires qada (makeup) only.
یمین (yamin): An oath sworn by Allah; its breach requires both qada and kaffarah yamin.
حقیقت (haqiqah): The literal, original meaning of a word, which applies without need for intention.
مجاز (majaz): Figurative meaning that is not the literal, requiring intention to be specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if someone utters an ambiguous statement intending it both as a nazr and a yamin, what is the ruling?
A) It is only a nazr.
B) It is only a yamin.
C) It is both a nazr and a yamin.
D) It is invalid because of contradiction.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, an ambiguous utterance intended as both a vow and an oath is treated as both, requiring both qada and kaffarah upon breach—a position that rests on the absence of contradiction between the two obligations.

Sawm — Fasting

Six Scenarios of Intention in the Statement 'Lillahi Alayya Sawmu Yawmi al-Nahr'
Taxonomy of six scenarios with consensus and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the six scenarios of intention and state the corresponding ruling according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The legal effect of 'Lillahi alayya' depends entirely on the speaker's intention, yielding six distinct rulings.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a detailed taxonomy of intentions behind a common vow/oath construction. Understanding these six scenarios is essential for correctly applying the rules of nadhr and yamin in practice, as the consequences vary from mere qada to both qada and kaffarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six scenarios
List the six possible intentions: no intention, only nadhr, nadhr + negate yamin, yamin + negate nadhr, both nadhr and yamin, only yamin.
The first three and the fourth are agreed upon; scenarios 5 and 6 are disputed.
2
Determine the ruling for consensus scenarios
For scenarios 1-3 the statement is a nadhr; for scenario 4 it is a yamin. Apply the haqiqah principle: without intention, literal meaning prevails.
Consensus among the three imams.
3
Analyze the disputed scenarios (5 and 6)
Note the disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it both nadhr and yamin; Abu Yusuf considers it only one (nadhr if both intended, yamin if yamin only).
This leads to different practical outcomes.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete case
Take a person who utters the statement and later breaks the fast. Based on their intention, determine whether qada only or qada+kaffarah is required.
Use the mufta bihi position if uncertain.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
کتاب الصوم اگر چہ وصف کے اعتبار سے معصیت اور غیر مشروع ہے لیکن اس کے باوجود کہ نہ رسیح ہے اس دن روزہ نہ رکھے تا کہ اس معصیت اور برائی سے بیچ جائے جو اللہ کی دعوت سے اعراض کرنے کی وجہ سے روزہ کے ساتھ متصل ہو گئی ہے۔ ہاں نذر کی وجہ سے جو روزہ واجب ہوا ہے اس کو ادا کرنے کے لئے قضاء واجب ہے اور اگر ممنوع ہونے کے باوجود یوم نحر میں روز ہ ر کھا لیا تو نذر پوری ہو جائے گی کیونکہ جس طرح کے روزے کا التزام کیا تھا اس طرح کا روزہ اس نے ادا کر لیا یعنی یوم نحر میں روزہ رکھنے کی نذر کی وجہ سے جو روزہ اس پر واجب ہوا ہے وہ ناقص ہے اور ناقص ہی اس نے ادا کیا ہے پس جیسا واجب ہوا تھا ویسا ہی ادا کر لیا اس لئے نذر پوری ہوگی۔
اگر قسم کی نیت کی تو کفارہ یمین لازم ہے
وَإِنْ نَوَّى يَمِنِيْنَا فَعَلَيْهِ كَفَّارَةُ يَمِين يَعْنِي إِذَا أَفْطَرَ وَهَذِهِ الْمَسْأَلَةُ عَلَى وُجُوهِ سِتَّةٍ إِنْ لَمْ يَبُو شَيْئًا أَوْ نَوَى النَّذْرَ لَا غير أوْ نَوَى التَّذْرَ وَأنْ لا يَكُونَ يَمِينًا يَكُونُ نَذرًا لأنَّهُ نَذَرُ بِصِيعَتِهِ كَيْفَ وَقَدْ قَرَرَهُ بِعَزِيمَةٍ وَإِنْ نَوَى الْيَمِينَ وَنَوَى أَن لا يَكُونَ نَذَرَا يَكُونُ يَمِينًا لأنَّ الْيَمِيْنَ مُحْتَمَلُ كَلَامِ، وَقَدْ عَيَّنَهُ وَنَفَى غَيْرَهُ وَإِنْ نَوَاهُمَا يَكُونُ بَدْرًا وَيَمِيْنَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ وَعِندَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ يَكُونُ نَدْرًا وَلَوْ نَوَى الْيَمِينَ فَكَذَلِكَ عِندَهُمَا وَعِندَهُ يَكُونُ الأبى يُوسُفَ أَنَّ التَّذَرَ فِيهِ حَقِيقَةُ وَالْيَمِينُ مَجَارٌ حَتَّى لَا يَتَوَقَّفُ الْاَوَّلُ عَلَى النِّيَةِ وَيَتَوَقَّفُ الثَّانِي فَلَا يَنتَظِمُهَا ثُمَّ المَجارُ يَتَعَيَّنُ بِنِيَّةٍ وَعِندَ بَيْتِهِمَا تُتَرَجَحُ الْحَقِيقَةُ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ لا تُنَا فِي بَيْنَ الْجِهَتَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُمَا يَقْتَضِيَانِ الْوُجُوبَ إِلَّا أَنَّ البَدْرَ يَقْتَضِيهِ لِعَيْنِهِ وَالْيَمِينُ لِغَيْره فَجَمَعْنَا بَيْنَهُمَا عَمَلًا بِالدَّلِيلَيْنِ كَمَا جَمَعْنَا بَيْنَ . بَيْنَ جَهَتَى التَّبَرُّع وَالْمُعَاوَضَةِ فِي الْهَبَةِ بِشَرْطِ الْعِوَضِ
ترجمہ اور اگر قسم کی نیت کی ہو تو اس پر کفارہ یمین واجب ہے یعنی جب اس نے افطار کیا اور اس مسئلہ کی چھ صورتیں ہیں ۔ اگر اس نے کچھ نیت نہ کی ہو یا فقط نذر کی نیت کی یا نذر کی نیت کی اور یہ نیت کی کہ یہ یمین نہ ہو تو اس کا یہ کلام نذر ہو گا۔ کیونکہ یہ کلام اپنے صیغہ کے اعتبار سے نڈر ہے اور نذر کیسے نہ ہو حالانکہ اس نے اپنی نیت سے اس کو ثابت کر دیا ہے۔ اور اگر قسم کی نیت کی اور یہ نیت کی کہ نذر نہ ہوتو یہ کلام یمین ہوگا کیونکہ یمین اس کے کلام کا مشتمل ہے اور حال یہ کہ اس نے اس کو متعین کر لیا ہے اور اس کے علاوہ کی نفی کر دی ہے اور اگر دونوں کی نیت کی ہے تو یہ کلام طرفین کے نزدیک نذر اور معین دونوں ہوگا اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک فقط یمین ہوگا اور اگر اس نے یمین کی نیت کی تو طرفین کے نزدیک نذر اور یمین دونوں ہوگا۔ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یمین ہوگا۔ ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کلام میں نذریہ حقیقت ہے اور نہین مجاز ہے حتی کہ نذر ہونا نیت پر موقوف نہیں ہے اور یمین ہونا نیست پر موقوف ہے پس یہ کلام دونوں کو شامل نہ ہوگا پھر مجاز تو نیست سے متعین ہو جاتا ہے اور ان دونوں کی نیت کے وقت حقیقت کو ترجیح ہوگی۔ اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دونوں جہتوں کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں ہے کیونکہ دونوں جہتیں وجوب کا تقاضا کرتی ہیں مگر نذر وجوب کا تقاضا لذاتہ کرتی ہے اور یمین لغیرہ تو ہم نے دونوں دلیلوں
عمل کرتے ہوئے دونوں کو جمع کر دیا ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے بہ بشرط العوض میں جہت تبرع اور جہت معاوضہ دونوں کو جمع کر دیا ہے۔ تشریح نذر اور یمین میں فرق یہ ہے کہ نذر میں فقط قضا ، واجب ہوتی ہے اور یمین میں قضاء اور کفار و بیمین دونوں واجب ہوتے ہیں مثلا اگر کسی نے ایک متعین روزہ رکھنے کی نذر کی اور اس متعین دن میں روزہ رکھ نہ سکا تو اس کی قضا واجب ہوگی اور اگر قسم کھائی کہ جمعہ کے دن کا روزہ رکھوں گا اور نہیں رکھ سکا تو قضاء بھی واجب ہوگی اور کفارہ بہین بھی ہوگا۔

کتاب الصوم اب صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اللهِ عَلَى صَومُ يَوْمِ التَّحْرِ سے یمن کی نیت کی اور اس دن میں روزہ نہیں رکھا تو اس پر قضاء کے ساتھ کفارہ یمین بھی واجب ہوگا۔

اور یہ نیت کی کہ نذر نہ ہو، (۵) یا نڈر اور یمین دونوں کی نیت کی ہو، (۲) یا یہ کہ فقط یمین کی نیت کی ہو۔ اول کی تین صورتوں میں یہ کالام بالا جماع نذر ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کلام میں نذر حقیقت ہے اور بیین مجاز ہے اور یہ امر مسلم ہے کہ حقیقت محتاج نیت نہیں ہوتا البتہ مجاز محتاج نیست ہوتا ہے پس پہلی صورت میں یہ کلام نذر اس لئے ہوگا کہ اس صورت میں کوئی نیت نہیں کی گئی ہے اور بغیر نیت اور ارادے کے کلام حقیقت پر محمول ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مجاز پر اور حقیقت نذر ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں یہ کلام نذر پر محمول ہوگا اور دوسری صورت میں چونکہ نیت کے ساتھ نذر کو متعین کر دیا گیا اس لئے بدرجہ اولی یہ کلام نذر ہوگا۔ اور تیسری صورت میں چونکہ نذر کو نیت کے ساتھ متعین کر دیا گیا اور یمین کی نفی بھی کر دی گئی تو یہ کلام بدرجہ اولی نذر پر محمول ہوگا۔ چوتھی صورت میں یہ کلام فقط یمین ہوگا اور یہ حکم متفق علیہ ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کلام کی حقیقت اگر چہ نذر ہے لیکن یہ کلام بیبین ( مجاز ) کا بھی احتمال رکھتا ہے اس طرح پر کہ اللہ علی الخ میں لام ہے اور لام کبھی باکے معنی میں آتا ہے پس لام کو باء کے معنی میں لیکر بالا ہو جائے گا اور بائیمین اور قسم کے لئے آتا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ اس کلام میں یمین کے معنی کا احتمال ہے اور کلام جس معنی کا احتمال رکھتا ہو اس کی نیت کرنا درست ہے اس لئے اس کلام سے یمین کی نیت کرنا درست ہوگا۔ اور جب اس کلام سے یمین کی نیت کرنا درست ہے تو یہ کلام یمبین ہو گا۔ پانچویں صورت میں طرفین کے نزدیک یہ کلام نذر اور یمین دونوں ہو گا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک فقط نذر ہوگا۔ اور چھٹی صورت میں طرفین کے نزدیک تو نذر اور یمین دونوں ہو گا مگر امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک فقط یمین ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کام ( اللَّهِ عَلَى صَوْمُ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ ) میں نذر تو حقیقت ہے اور یمین مجاز ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ اس کلام کا نذر ہونا نیت پر موقوف نہیں ہے البتہ یمین ہونا نیت پر موقوف ہے۔ اب اگر نذر اور یمین دونوں کو مراد لیا گیا تو حقیقت اور مجاز کا جمع ہونا لازم آئے گا حالانکہ لفظ واحد سے حقیقت اور مجاز کو جمع کرنا جائز نہیں ہے پس اس کلام سے نذر اور یمین دونوں کا مراد ہونا تو محال ہو گیا پس جب دونوں کی نیت کی تو حقیقت کو تر جیح ہوگی اور حقیقت یعنی نذر مراد ہوگی اور جب حقیقت مراد ہے تو مجاز مراد نہ ہوگا اور جب یمین کی نیت کی تو مجاز نیت سے متعین ہو گیا لہذا حقیقت مراد نہ ہوگی۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کلام سے نذر اور یمین دونوں مراد لینے کے باوجود جمع بین الحقيقة والمجاز لازم نہیں آتا۔ کیونکہ لِلَّهِ عَلَى صَوْمُ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وجوب کے لئے موضوع ہے اور وجوب ہی میں مستعمل ہے غیر وجوب میں قطعا مستعمل نہیں ہے۔ البتہ یہ کلام وجوب
کے اندر دو جہتوں سے مستعمل ہے اور ان دونوں جہتوں میں کوئی منافات نہیں ہے ان میں ایک تو جہت نذر ہے ، دوم جہت بیمین ہے۔ لیکن (الحج : ٢٩) اتنا فرق ہے کہ نذرو جوب کا تقاضہ لذاتہ کرتی ہے کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے۔ وَلْيُوفُوا نُدُورَهُمْ اور یمین وجوب کا تقاضا لغیرہ کرتی
ہے اور وہ غیر اللہ کے نام کو بے حرمتی سے بچانا ہے۔ یعنی یمین کو پورا کرنا اس لئے واجب ہے تا کہ اللہ کے نام کی بے حرمتی نہ ہو ورنہ قسم تو ڑنے میں خواہ مخواہ اللہ کے نام کی بے حرمتی ہوتی ہے ۔ پس حاصل یہ ہوا کہ اس کلام کا موجب اور حقیقت تو وجوب ہے لیکن وجوب کا اتقانها دوطرف سے ہے ایک نذر کی طرف سے دو مین کی طرف سے اور ان دونوں پر عمل کرنا بھی ممکن ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں میں کوئی منافات نہیں
Although in terms of description it is disobedience and unlegislated, but despite that, he should not fast that day so that he may avoid that disobedience and evil which has become attached to fasting due to turning away from Allah's invitation. Yes, for the fast that became obligatory due to a vow, making it up is obligatory. And if despite being prohibited he fasted on the Day of Sacrifice, the vow will be fulfilled because he performed the kind of fast he had obligated himself to, i.e., the fast that became obligatory on him due to vowing to fast on the Day of Sacrifice is deficient, and he performed it as deficient. So just as it became obligatory, he performed it similarly, therefore the vow is fulfilled.
If he intended an oath, then the expiation of an oath is obligatory upon him.
وَإِنْ نَوَّى يَمِنِيْنَا فَعَلَيْهِ كَفَّارَةُ يَمِين يَعْنِي إِذَا أَفْطَرَ وَهَذِهِ الْمَسْأَلَةُ عَلَى وُجُوهِ سِتَّةٍ إِنْ لَمْ يَبُو شَيْئًا أَوْ نَوَى النَّذْرَ لَا غير أوْ نَوَى التَّذْرَ وَأنْ لا يَكُونَ يَمِينًا يَكُونُ نَذرًا لأنَّهُ نَذَرُ بِصِيعَتِهِ كَيْفَ وَقَدْ قَرَرَهُ بِعَزِيمَةٍ وَإِنْ نَوَى الْيَمِينَ وَنَوَى أَن لا يَكُونَ نَذَرَا يَكُونُ يَمِينًا لأنَّ الْيَمِيْنَ مُحْتَمَلُ كَلَامِ، وَقَدْ عَيَّنَهُ وَنَفَى غَيْرَهُ وَإِنْ نَوَاهُمَا يَكُونُ بَدْرًا وَيَمِيْنَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ وَعِندَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ يَكُونُ نَدْرًا وَلَوْ نَوَى الْيَمِينَ فَكَذَلِكَ عِندَهُمَا وَعِندَهُ يَكُونُ الأبى يُوسُفَ أَنَّ التَّذَرَ فِيهِ حَقِيقَةُ وَالْيَمِينُ مَجَارٌ حَتَّى لَا يَتَوَقَّفُ الْاَوَّلُ عَلَى النِّيَةِ وَيَتَوَقَّفُ الثَّانِي فَلَا يَنتَظِمُهَا ثُمَّ المَجارُ يَتَعَيَّنُ بِنِيَّةٍ وَعِندَ بَيْتِهِمَا تُتَرَجَحُ الْحَقِيقَةُ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ لا تُنَا فِي بَيْنَ الْجِهَتَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُمَا يَقْتَضِيَانِ الْوُجُوبَ إِلَّا أَنَّ البَدْرَ يَقْتَضِيهِ لِعَيْنِهِ وَالْيَمِينُ لِغَيْره فَجَمَعْنَا بَيْنَهُمَا عَمَلًا بِالدَّلِيلَيْنِ كَمَا جَمَعْنَا بَيْنَ . بَيْنَ جَهَتَى التَّبَرُّع وَالْمُعَاوَضَةِ فِي الْهَبَةِ بِشَرْطِ الْعِوَضِ
Translation: And if he intended an oath, then the expiation of an oath is obligatory upon him, i.e., when he broke the fast. And this issue has six forms. If he did not intend anything, or only intended a vow, or intended a vow and intended that it not be an oath, then his statement is a vow because his statement by its form is a vow, and how could it not be a vow when he has confirmed it with a resolve? And if he intended an oath and intended that it not be a vow, then it is an oath because an oath is included in his statement, and he has specified it and negated other than it. And if he intended both, then according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad it is both a vow and an oath, and according to Abu Yusuf it is only a vow. And if he intended an oath, then similarly according to them both [it is both], and according to him [Abu Yusuf] it is only an oath. The proof of Abu Yusuf is that in this statement, a vow is the literal meaning (haqiqah) and an oath is figurative (majaz), so much so that the first does not depend on intention and the second depends on intention, so the statement cannot include both. Then the figurative meaning is specified by intention, and in their view [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] the literal meaning is given preference when both are intended. And their proof is that there is no contradiction between the two aspects because both require obligation, except that a vow requires it for its own sake and an oath for something else. So we combine them by acting on both evidences, just as we combined between the aspect of donation and the aspect of compensation in a gift with a condition of compensation.
Explanation: The difference between a vow and an oath is that in a vow only making up (qada) is obligatory, and in an oath both making up and the expiation of an oath are obligatory. For example, if someone vowed to fast on a specific day and could not fast on that specific day, then making it up is obligatory. And if he swore that he would fast on Friday and could not, then making it up is obligatory and also the expiation of an oath.

Now the situation of the issue is that if someone intended an oath with "Lillahi alayya sawmu yawmi al-nahr" and did not fast that day, then upon him is making up along with the expiation of an oath.
The author of al-Hidayah says that this issue has six forms: (1) He did not intend anything from this statement, (2) or he only intended a vow, (3) or he intended a vow and intended that it not be an oath, (4) or he intended an oath and intended that it not be a vow, (5) or he intended both a vow and an oath, (6) or he only intended an oath. In the first three forms, this statement is a vow by consensus. The proof is that in this statement, a vow is the literal meaning (haqiqah) and an oath is figurative (majaz), and it is established that literal meaning does not need intention, while figurative meaning needs intention. So in the first form, it is a vow because no intention was made, and without intention a statement is applied to its literal meaning, not figurative. In the second form, since the vow was specified with intention, it is a fortiori a vow. In the third form, since the vow was specified with intention and the oath was negated, it is a fortiori a vow. In the fourth form, this statement is only an oath, and this ruling is agreed upon. Its proof is that although the literal meaning of this statement is a vow, it also probabilizes an oath, in that in "Lillahi alayya" there is a lam, and lam sometimes comes in the meaning of ba, so taking lam in the meaning of ba, it becomes "billahi" (by Allah), and ba is used for oaths. So it is established that this statement probabilizes the meaning of an oath, and it is valid to intend a meaning that a statement probabilizes, therefore intending an oath from this statement is valid. And when intending an oath from this statement is valid, then this statement becomes an oath. In the fifth form, according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) this statement is both a vow and an oath, and according to Imam Abu Yusuf it is only a vow. In the sixth form, according to them it is both a vow and an oath, but according to Imam Abu Yusuf it is only an oath. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that in this statement (Lillahi alayya sawmu yawmi al-nahr), a vow is literal and an oath is figurative, and that is why the statement being a vow does not depend on intention, but being an oath depends on intention. Now if both a vow and an oath are intended, then combining literal and figurative would be necessary, whereas it is not permissible to combine literal and figurative in a single word. So it becomes impossible for both vow and oath to be intended from this statement. Therefore, when both are intended, the literal meaning is given preference, i.e., the vow is intended, and when the literal meaning is intended, the figurative is not intended. And when he intends an oath, the figurative is specified by intention, so the literal is not intended. The proof of them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that intending both a vow and an oath from this statement does not necessitate combining literal and figurative. Because "Lillahi alayya sawmu yawmi al-nahr" is placed for obligation and is used in obligation, not in non-obligation at all. However, this statement is used within obligation from two aspects, and there is no contradiction between these two aspects. One is the aspect of vow, the second is the aspect of oath. But there is a difference that a vow requires obligation for its own sake because Allah Almighty said: "And let them fulfill their vows" (Quran 22:29), and an oath requires obligation for something else, and that other is protecting Allah's name from disrespect. That is, fulfilling an oath is obligatory so that Allah's name is not disrespected, otherwise breaking an oath inevitably involves disrespect of Allah's name. So the conclusion is that the effective cause and reality of this statement is obligation, but the obligation is from two sides: one from the side of vow and the other from the side of oath, and it is possible to act on both because there is no contradiction between them.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal effect of the statement 'Lillahi alayya sawmu yawmi al-nahr' (I owe Allah to fast on the Day of Sacrifice). The author of Al-Hidayah first provides a general ruling: if the speaker intended an oath (yamin) and then broke the fast, he must pay the expiation of an oath (kaffarat al-yamin). The passage then details six possible scenarios based on the speaker's intention and presents the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two shaykhs, 'al-tarafayn') on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other.

Summary of the six scenarios:
1. No intention: The statement is a vow (nadhr) by consensus.
2. Intention of nadhr only: It is a nadhr.
3. Intention of nadhr and negation of yamin: It is a nadhr.
4. Intention of yamin and negation of nadhr: It is a yamin (agreed upon).
5. Intention of both nadhr and yamin: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is both; according to Abu Yusuf, it is only a nadhr.
6. Intention of yamin only: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is both; according to Abu Yusuf, it is only a yamin.

The core disagreement concerns scenarios 5 and 6. Abu Yusuf argues that in the statement, 'nadhr' is the literal meaning (haqiqah) and 'yamin' is figurative (majaz). Since a single word cannot carry both literal and figurative meanings simultaneously when both are intended, the literal meaning prevails when both are intended, and the figurative is specified only when explicitly intended. Thus, when both are intended (scenario 5), it becomes nadhr only. When only yamin is intended (scenario 6), the figurative meaning is specified, so it becomes yamin only.

Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that there is no contradiction between the two aspects because both entail obligation (wujub). The statement is inherently about obligation; the difference lies in the cause: nadhr obligates intrinsically (li-dhatihi) based on the Quranic command to fulfill vows, while yamin obligates extrinsically (li-ghayrihi) to protect the sanctity of Allah's name. Since both aspects lead to obligation, they can be combined, analogous to how a gift with a condition of compensation (hibah bi shart al-'iwad) combines donation (tabarru') and compensation (mu'awadah).

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship for Allah.
يمين (yamin): An oath sworn by Allah.
حقيقة (haqiqah): Literal meaning of a word.
مجاز (majaz): Figurative meaning requiring contextual clue or intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In scenario 5 (both nadhr and yamin intended), what is the ruling according to Abu Yusuf?
A) It is both a vow and an oath.
B) It is only a vow.
C) It is only an oath.
D) It is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The legal effect of 'Lillahi alayya sawmu yawmi al-nahr' depends on intention: without intention it is a vow (nadhr), with specific intentions it can be an oath (yamin) or both, with a dispute on the latter.

Sawm — Fasting
advanced
10 min
The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Combining Nadhr and Yamin in One Utterance
Detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on combining nadhr and yamin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasoning behind the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding combining nadhr and yamin and apply it to a scenario where both are intended.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf forbids combining haqiqah and majaz; Abu Hanifa allows combining two obligation-causing aspects.

The disagreement between the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf turns on a subtle usul point: can a single utterance carry both its literal and figurative meanings simultaneously? The passage argues from both sides, and the practical consequence affects whether kaffarah is required in addition to qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of dispute
The dispute concerns scenarios 5 and 6: when both nadhr and yamin are intended, or when only yamin is intended.
Scenarios 1-4 are agreed upon.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and dalil
Abu Yusuf argues that nadhr is haqiqah (literal) and yamin is majaz (figurative). Combining both in one utterance is impossible because it requires combining haqiqah and majaz, which is impermissible. Therefore, when both are intended, the literal (nadhr) prevails; when yamin only is intended, the figurative is specified by intention.
This is a strict usul principle.
3
State Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's position and dalil
They argue that there is no contradiction because both nadhr and yamin require obligation (wujub). Nadhr obligates for its own sake (li-dhatihi), yamin for something else (li-ghayrihi). The same statement can be used for obligation from two aspects, just as a gift with a condition of compensation (hibah bi shart al-'iwad) combines donation and compensation.
They use qiyas with a known fiqh example.
4
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf
According to Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, both nadhr and yamin apply, so breaking the fast requires both qada and kaffarah. According to Abu Yusuf, only one applies: in scenario 5, only qada; in scenario 6, only qada+kaffarah (but note: in scenario 6, both sides require qada+kaffarah, so the practical difference is only in scenario 5).
Thus the real difference is when both are intended.
